1448 "INTRODUCTION"
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Heidi\" is a delightful story for children of life in the Alps,"
1448 "one of many tales written by the Swiss authoress, Johanna Spyri,"
1448 "who died in her home at Zurich in 1891. She had been well known"
1448 "to the younger readers of her own country since 1880, when she"
1448 "published her story, Heimathlos, which ran into three or more"
1448 "editions, and which, like her other books, as she states on the"
1448 "title page, was written for those who love children, as well as"
1448 "for the youngsters themselves. Her own sympathy with the"
1448 "instincts and longings of the child's heart is shown in her"
1448 "picture of Heidi. The record of the early life of this Swiss"
1448 "child amid the beauties of her passionately loved mountain-home"
1448 "and during her exile in the great town has been for many years a"
1448 "favorite book of younger readers in Germany and America."
1448 ""
1448 "Madame Spyri, like Hans Andersen, had by temperament a peculiar"
1448 "skill in writing the simple histories of an innocent world. In"
1448 "all her stories she shows an underlying desire to preserve"
1448 "children alike from misunderstanding and the mistaken kindness"
1448 "that frequently hinder the happiness and natural development of"
1448 "their lives and characters. The authoress, as we feel in reading"
1448 "her tales, lived among the scenes and people she describes, and"
1448 "the setting of her stories has the charm of the mountain scenery"
1448 "amid which she places her small actors."
1448 ""
1448 "Her chief works, besides Heidi, were:-- Am Sonntag; Arthur und"
1448 "Squirrel; Aus dem Leben; Aus den Schweizer Bergen; Aus Nah und"
1448 "Fern; Aus unserem, Lande; Cornelli wird erzogen; Einer vom Hause"
1448 "Lesa; 10 Geschichten fur Yung und Alt; Kurze Geschichten, 2"
1448 "vols.; Gritli's Kinder, 2 vols.; Heimathlos; Im Tilonethal; In"
1448 "Leuchtensa; Keiner zu Klein Helfer zu sein; Onkel Titus; Schloss"
1448 "Wildenstein; Sina; Ein Goldener Spruch; Die Hauffer Muhle;"
1448 "Verschollen, nicht vergessen; Was soll deim aus ihr werden; Was"
1448 "aus ihr Geworden ist.                                    M.E."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "HEIDI"
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER I. UP THE MOUNTAIN TO ALM-UNCLE>"
1448 ""
1448 "From the old and pleasantly situated village of Mayenfeld, a"
1448 "footpath winds through green and shady meadows to the foot of"
1448 "the mountains, which on this side look down from their stern and"
1448 "lofty heights upon the valley below. The land grows gradually"
1448 "wilder as the path ascends, and the climber has not gone far"
1448 "before he begins to inhale the fragrance of the short grass and"
1448 "sturdy mountain-plants, for the way is steep and leads directly"
1448 "up to the summits above."
1448 ""
1448 "On a clear sunny morning in June two figures might be seen"
1448 "climbing the narrow mountain path; one, a tall strong-looking"
1448 "girl, the other a child whom she was leading by the hand, and"
1448 "whose little checks were so aglow with heat that the crimson"
1448 "color could be seen even through the dark, sunburnt skin. And"
1448 "this was hardly to be wondered at, for in spite of the hot June"
1448 "sun the child was clothed as if to keep off the bitterest frost."
1448 "She did not look more than five years old, if as much, but what"
1448 "her natural figure was like, it would have been hard to say, for"
1448 "she had apparently two, if not three dresses, one above the"
1448 "other, and over these a thick red woollen shawl wound round"
1448 "about her, so that the little body presented a shapeless"
1448 "appearance, as, with its small feet shod in thick, nailed"
1448 "mountain-shoes, it slowly and laboriously plodded its way up in"
1448 "the heat. The two must have left the valley a good hour's walk"
1448 "behind them, when they came to the hamlet known as Dorfli, which"
1448 "is situated half-way up the mountain. Here the wayfarers met with"
1448 "greetings from all sides, some calling to them from windows, some"
1448 "from open doors, others from outside, for the elder girl was now"
1448 "in her old home. She did not, however, pause in her walk to"
1448 "respond to her friends' welcoming cries and questions, but passed"
1448 "on without stopping for a moment until she reached the last of"
1448 "the scattered houses of the hamlet. Here a voice called to her"
1448 "from the door: \"Wait a moment, Dete; if you are going up higher,"
1448 "I will come with you.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The girl thus addressed stood still, and the child immediately"
1448 "let go her hand and seated herself on the ground."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Are you tired, Heidi?\" asked her companion."
1448 ""
1448 "\"No, I am hot,\" answered the child."
1448 ""
1448 "\"We shall soon get to the top now. You must walk bravely on a"
1448 "little longer, and take good long steps, and in another hour we"
1448 "shall be there,\" said Dete in an encouraging voice."
1448 ""
1448 "They were now joined by a stout, good-natured-looking woman, who"
1448 "walked on ahead with her old acquaintance, the two breaking"
1448 "forth at once into lively conversation about everybody and"
1448 "everything in Dorfli and its surroundings, while the child"
1448 "wandered behind them."
1448 ""
1448 "\"And where are you off to with the child?\" asked the one who had"
1448 "just joined the party. \"I suppose it is the child your sister"
1448 "left?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes,\" answered Dete. \"I am taking her up to Uncle, where she"
1448 "must stay.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"The child stay up there with Alm-Uncle! You must be out of your"
1448 "senses, Dete! How can you think of such a thing! The old man,"
1448 "however, will soon send you and your proposal packing off home"
1448 "again!\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"He cannot very well do that, seeing that he is her grandfather."
1448 "He must do something for her. I have had the charge of the child"
1448 "till now, and I can tell you, Barbel, I am not going to give up"
1448 "the chance which has just fallen to me of getting a good place,"
1448 "for her sake. It is for the grandfather now to do his duty by"
1448 "her.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"That would be all very well if he were like other people,\""
1448 "asseverated stout Barbel warmly, \"but you know what he is. And"
1448 "what can he do with a child, especially with one so young! The"
1448 "child cannot possibly live with him. But where are you thinking"
1448 "of going yourself?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"To Frankfurt, where an extra good place awaits me,\" answered"
1448 "Dete. \"The people I am going to were down at the Baths last"
1448 "summer, and it was part of my duty to attend upon their rooms."
1448 "They would have liked then to take me away with them, but I"
1448 "could not leave. Now they are there again and have repeated their"
1448 "offer, and I intend to go with them, you may make up your mind"
1448 "to that!\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I am glad I am not the child!\" exclaimed Barbel, with a gesture"
1448 "of horrified pity. \"Not a creature knows anything about the old"
1448 "man up there! He will have nothing to do with anybody, and never"
1448 "sets his foot inside a church from one year's end to another."
1448 "When he does come down once in a while, everybody clears out of"
1448 "the way of him and his big stick. The mere sight of him, with"
1448 "his bushy grey eyebrows and his immense beard, is alarming"
1448 "enough. He looks like any old heathen or Indian, and few would"
1448 "care to meet him alone.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well, and what of that?\" said Dete, in a defiant voice, \"he is"
1448 "the grandfather all the same, and must look after the child. He"
1448 "is not likely to do her any harm, and if he does, he will be"
1448 "answerable for it, not I.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I should very much like to know,\" continued Barbel, in an"
1448 "inquiring tone of voice, \"what the old man has on his conscience"
1448 "that he looks as he does, and lives up there on the mountain"
1448 "like a hermit, hardly ever allowing himself to be seen. All kinds"
1448 "of things are said about him. You, Dete, however, must certainly"
1448 "have learnt a good deal concerning him from your sister--am I"
1448 "not right?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"You are right, I did, but I am not going to repeat what I"
1448 "heard; if it should come to his ears I should get into trouble"
1448 "about it.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Now Barbel had for long past been most anxious to ascertain"
1448 "particulars about Alm-Uncle, as she could not understand why he"
1448 "seemed to feel such hatred towards his fellow-creatures, and"
1448 "insisted on living all alone, or why people spoke about him half"
1448 "in whispers, as if afraid to say anything against him, and yet"
1448 "unwilling to take his Part. Moreover, Barbel was in ignorance as"
1448 "to why all the people in Dorfli called him Alm-Uncle, for he"
1448 "could not possibly be uncle to everybody living there. As,"
1448 "however, it was the custom, she did like the rest and called the"
1448 "old man Uncle. Barbel had only lived in Dorfli since her"
1448 "marriage, which had taken place not long before. Previous to"
1448 "that her home had been below in Prattigau, so that she was not"
1448 "well acquainted with all the events that had ever taken place,"
1448 "and with all the people who had ever lived in Dorfli and its"
1448 "neighborhood. Dete, on the contrary, had been born in Dorfli,"
1448 "and had lived there with her mother until the death of the latter"
1448 "the year before, and had then gone over to the Baths at Ragatz"
1448 "and taken service in the large hotel there as chambermaid. On the"
1448 "morning of this day she had come all the way from Ragatz with"
1448 "the child, a friend having given them a lift in a hay-cart as far"
1448 "as Mayenfeld. Barbel was therefore determined not to lose this"
1448 "good opportunity of satisfying her curiosity. She put her arm"
1448 "through Dete's in a confidential sort of way, and said: \"I know I"
1448 "can find out the real truth from you, and the meaning of all"
1448 "these tales that are afloat about him. I believe you know the"
1448 "whole story. Now do just tell me what is wrong with the old man,"
1448 "and if he was always shunned as he is now, and was always such a"
1448 "misanthrope.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"How can I possibly tell you whether he was always the same,"
1448 "seeing I am only six-and-twenty and he at least seventy years of"
1448 "age; so you can hardly expect me to know much about his youth."
1448 "If I was sure, however, that what I tell you would not go the"
1448 "whole round of Prattigau, I could relate all kinds of things"
1448 "about him; my mother came from Domleschg, and so did he.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Nonsense, Dete, what do you mean?\" replied Barbel, somewhat"
1448 "offended, \"gossip has not reached such a dreadful pitch in"
1448 "Prattigau as all that, and I am also quite capable of holding my"
1448 "tongue when it is necessary.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Very well then, I will tell you--but just wait a moment,\" said"
1448 "Dete in a warning voice, and she looked back to make sure that"
1448 "the child was not near enough to hear all she was going to"
1448 "relate; but the child was nowhere to be seen, and must have"
1448 "turned aside from following her companions some time before,"
1448 "while these were too eagerly occupied with their conversation to"
1448 "notice it. Dete stood still and looked around her in all"
1448 "directions. The footpath wound a little here and there, but"
1448 "could nevertheless be seen along its whole length nearly to"
1448 "Dorfli; no one, however, was visible upon it at this moment."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I see where she is,\" exclaimed Barbel, \"look over there!\" and"
1448 "she pointed to a spot far away from the footpath. \"She is"
1448 "climbing up the slope yonder with the goatherd and his goats. I"
1448 "wonder why he is so late to-day bringing them up. It happens"
1448 "well, however, for us, for he can now see after the child, and"
1448 "you can the better tell me your tale.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh, as to the looking after,\" remarked Dete, \"the boy need not"
1448 "put himself out about that; she is not by any means stupid for"
1448 "her five years, and knows how to use her eyes. She notices all"
1448 "that is going on, as I have often had occasion to remark, and"
1448 "this will stand her in good stead some day, for the old man has"
1448 "nothing beyond his two goats and his hut.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Did he ever have more?\" asked Barbel."
1448 ""
1448 "\"He? I should think so indeed,\" replied Dete with animation; \"he"
1448 "was owner once of one of the largest farms in Domleschg. He was"
1448 "the elder of two brothers; the younger was a quiet, orderly man,"
1448 "but nothing would please the other but to play the grand"
1448 "gentleman and go driving about the country and mixing with bad"
1448 "company, strangers that nobody knew. He drank and gambled away"
1448 "the whole of his property, and when this became known to his"
1448 "mother and father they died, one shortly after the other, of"
1448 "sorrow. The younger brother, who was also reduced to beggary,"
1448 "went off in his anger, no one knew whither, while Uncle himself,"
1448 "having nothing now left to him but his bad name, also"
1448 "disappeared. For some time his whereabouts were unknown, then"
1448 "some one found out that he had gone to Naples as a soldier;"
1448 "after that nothing more was heard of him for twelve or fifteen"
1448 "years. At the end of that time he reappeared in Domleschg,"
1448 "bringing with him a young child, whom he tried to place with some"
1448 "of his kinspeople. Every door, however, was shut in his face, for"
1448 "no one wished to have any more to do with him. Embittered by this"
1448 "treatment, he vowed never to set foot in Domleschg again, and he"
1448 "then came to Dorfli, where he continued to live with his little"
1448 "boy. His wife was probably a native of the Grisons, whom he had"
1448 "met down there, and who died soon after their marriage. He could"
1448 "not have been entirely without money, for he apprenticed his"
1448 "son, Tobias, to a carpenter. He was a steady lad, and kindly"
1448 "received by every one in Dorfli. The old man was, however, still"
1448 "looked upon with suspicion, and it was even rumoured that he had"
1448 "been forced to make his escape from Naples, or it might have gone"
1448 "badly with him, for that he had killed a man, not in fair fight,"
1448 "you understand, but in some brawl. We, however, did not refuse"
1448 "to acknowledge our relationship with him, my great-grandmother on"
1448 "my mother's side having been sister to his grandmother. So we"
1448 "called him Uncle, and as through my father we are also related to"
1448 "nearly every family in Dorfli, he became known all over the place"
1448 "as Uncle, and since he went to live on the mountain side he has"
1448 "gone everywhere by the name of Alm-Uncle.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"And what happened to Tobias?\" asked Barbel, who was listening"
1448 "with deep interest."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Wait a moment, I am coming to that, but I cannot tell you"
1448 "everything at once,\" replied Dete. \"Tobias was taught his trade"
1448 "in Mels, and when he had served his apprenticeship he came back"
1448 "to Dorfli and married my sister Adelaide. They had always been"
1448 "fond of one another, and they got on very well together after"
1448 "they were married. But their happiness did not last long. Her"
1448 "husband met with his death only two years after their marriage,"
1448 "a beam falling upon him as he was working, and killing him on the"
1448 "spot. They carried him home, and when Adelaide saw the poor"
1448 "disfigured body of her husband she was so overcome with horror"
1448 "and grief that she fell into a fever from which she never"
1448 "recovered. She had always been rather delicate and subject to"
1448 "curious attacks, during which no one knew whether she was awake"
1448 "or sleeping. And so two months after Tobias had been carried to"
1448 "the grave, his wife followed him. Their sad fate was the talk of"
1448 "everybody far and near, and both in private and public the"
1448 "general opinion was expressed that it was a punishment which"
1448 "Uncle had deserved for the godless life he had led. Some went so"
1448 "far even as to tell him so to his face. Our minister endeavored"
1448 "to awaken his conscience and exhorted him to repentance, but the"
1448 "old man grew only more wrathful and obdurate and would not speak"
1448 "to a soul, and every one did their best to keep out of his way."
1448 "All at once we heard that he had gone to live up the Alm and did"
1448 "not intend ever to come down again, and since then he has led"
1448 "his solitary life on the mountain side at enmity with God and"
1448 "man. Mother and I took Adelaide's little one, then only a year"
1448 "old, into our care. When mother died last year, and I went down"
1448 "to the Baths to earn some money, I paid old Ursel, who lives in"
1448 "the village just above, to keep and look after the child. I"
1448 "stayed on at the Baths through the winter, for as I could sew and"
1448 "knit I had no difficulty in finding plenty of work, and early in"
1448 "the spring the same family I had waited on before returned from"
1448 "Frankfurt, and again asked me to go back with them. And so we"
1448 "leave the day after to-morrow, and I can assure you, it is an"
1448 "excellent place for me.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"And you are going to give the child over to the old man up"
1448 "there? It surprises me beyond words that you can think of doing"
1448 "such a thing, Dete,\" said Barbel, in a voice full of reproach."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What do you mean?\" retorted Dete. \"I have done my duty by the"
1448 "child, and what would you have me do with it now? I cannot"
1448 "certainly take a child of five years old with me to Frankfurt."
1448 "But where are you going to yourself, Barbel; we are now half way"
1448 "up the Alm?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"We have just reached the place I wanted,\" answered Barbel. \"I"
1448 "had something to say to the goatherd's wife, who does some"
1448 "spinning for me in the winter. So good-bye, Dete, and good luck"
1448 "to you!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Dete shook hands with her friend and remained standing while"
1448 "Barbel went towards a small, dark brown hut, which stood a few"
1448 "steps away from the path in a hollow that afforded it some"
1448 "protection from the mountain wind. The hut was situated half way"
1448 "up the Alm, reckoning from Dorfli, and it was well that it was"
1448 "provided with some shelter, for it was so broken-down and"
1448 "dilapidated that even then it must have been very unsafe as a"
1448 "habitation, for when the stormy south wind came sweeping over"
1448 "the mountain, everything inside it, doors and windows, shook and"
1448 "rattled, and all the rotten old beams creaked and trembled. On"
1448 "such days as this, had the goatherd's dwelling been standing"
1448 "above on the exposed mountain side, it could not have escaped"
1448 "being blown straight down into the valley without a moment's"
1448 "warning."
1448 ""
1448 "Here lived Peter, the eleven-year-old boy, who every morning"
1448 "went down to Dorfli to fetch his goats and drive them up on to"
1448 "the mountain, where they were free to browse till evening on the"
1448 "delicious mountain plants."
1448 ""
1448 "Then Peter, with his light-footed animals, would go running and"
1448 "leaping down the mountain again till he reached Dorfli, and"
1448 "there he would give a shrill whistle through his fingers,"
1448 "whereupon all the owners of the goats would come out to fetch"
1448 "home the animals that belonged to them. It was generally the"
1448 "small boys and girls who ran in answer to Peter's whistle, for"
1448 "they were none of them afraid of the gentle goats, and this was"
1448 "the only hour of the day through all the summer months that Peter"
1448 "had any opportunity of seeing his young friends, since the rest"
1448 "of his time was spent alone with the goats. He had a mother and a"
1448 "blind grandmother at home, it is true, but he was always obliged"
1448 "to start off very early in the morning, and only got home late in"
1448 "the evening from Dorfli, for he always stayed as long as he could"
1448 "talking and playing with the other children; and so he had just"
1448 "time enough at home, and that was all, to swallow down his bread"
1448 "and milk in the morning, and again in the evening to get through"
1448 "a similar meal, lie down in bed and go to sleep. His father, who"
1448 "had been known also as the goatherd, having earned his living as"
1448 "such when younger, had been accidentally killed while cutting"
1448 "wood some years before. His mother, whose real name was Brigitta,"
1448 "was always called the goatherd's wife, for the sake of old"
1448 "association, while the blind grandmother was just \"grandmother\""
1448 "to all the old and young in the neighborhood."
1448 ""
1448 "Dete had been standing for a good ten minutes looking about her"
1448 "in every direction for some sign of the children and the goats."
1448 "Not a glimpse of them, however, was to be seen, so she climbed"
1448 "to a higher spot, whence she could get a fuller view of the"
1448 "mountain as it sloped beneath her to the valley, while, with"
1448 "ever-increasing anxiety on her face and in her movements, she"
1448 "continued to scan the surrounding slopes. Meanwhile the children"
1448 "were climbing up by a far and roundabout way, for Peter knew"
1448 "many spots where all kinds of good food, in the shape of shrubs"
1448 "and plants, grew for his goats, and he was in the habit of"
1448 "leading his flock aside from the beaten track. The child,"
1448 "exhausted with the heat and weight of her thick armor of clothes,"
1448 "panted and struggled after him at first with some difficulty. She"
1448 "said nothing, but her little eyes kept watching first Peter, as"
1448 "he sprang nimbly hither and thither on his bare feet, clad only"
1448 "in his short light breeches, and then the slim-legged goats that"
1448 "went leaping over rocks and shrubs and up the steep ascents with"
1448 "even greater ease. All at once she sat herself down on the"
1448 "ground, and as fast as her little fingers could move, began"
1448 "pulling off her shoes and stockings. This done she rose, unwound"
1448 "the hot red shawl and threw it away, and then proceeded to undo"
1448 "her frock. It was off in a second, but there was still another"
1448 "to unfasten, for Dete had put the Sunday frock on over the"
1448 "everyday one, to save the trouble of carrying it. Quick as"
1448 "lightning the everyday frock followed the other, and now the"
1448 "child stood up, clad only in her light short-sleeved under"
1448 "garment, stretching out her little bare arms with glee. She put"
1448 "all her clothes together in a tidy little heap, and then went"
1448 "jumping and climbing up after Peter and the goats as nimbly as"
1448 "any one of the party. Peter had taken no heed of what the child"
1448 "was about when she stayed behind, but when she ran up to him in"
1448 "her new attire, his face broke into a grin, which grew broader"
1448 "still as he looked back and saw the small heap of clothes lying"
1448 "on the ground, until his mouth stretched almost from ear to ear;"
1448 "he said nothing, however. The child, able now to move at her"
1448 "ease, began to enter into conversation with Peter, who had many"
1448 "questions to answer, for his companion wanted to know how many"
1448 "goats he had, where he was going to with them, and what he had to"
1448 "do when he arrived there. At last, after some time, they and the"
1448 "goats approached the hut and came within view of Cousin Dete."
1448 "Hardly had the latter caught sight of the little company climbing"
1448 "up towards her when she shrieked out: \"Heidi, what have you been"
1448 "doing! What a sight you have made of yourself! And where are your"
1448 "two frocks and the red wrapper? And the new shoes I bought, and"
1448 "the new stockings I knitted for you--everything gone! not a thing"
1448 "left! What can you have been thinking of, Heidi; where are all"
1448 "your clothes?\""
1448 ""
1448 "The child quietly pointed to a spot below on the mountain side"
1448 "and answered, \"Down there.\" Dete followed the direction of her"
1448 "finger; she could just distinguish something lying on the"
1448 "ground, with a spot of red on the top of it which she had no"
1448 "doubt was the woollen wrapper."
1448 ""
1448 "\"You good-for-nothing little thing!\" exclaimed Dete angrily,"
1448 "\"what could have put it into your head to do like that? What"
1448 "made you undress yourself? What do you mean by it?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I don't want any clothes,\" said the child, not showing any sign"
1448 "of repentance for her past deed."
1448 ""
1448 "\"You wretched, thoughtless child! have you no sense in you at"
1448 "all?\" continued Dete, scolding and lamenting. \"Who is going all"
1448 "that way down to fetch them; it's a good half-hour's walk!"
1448 "Peter, you go off and fetch them for me as quickly as you can,"
1448 "and don't stand there gaping at me, as if you were rooted to the"
1448 "ground!\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I am already past my time,\" answered Peter slowly, without"
1448 "moving from the spot where he had been standing with his hands"
1448 "in his pockets, listening to Dete's outburst of dismay and anger."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well, you won't get far if you only keep on standing there with"
1448 "your eyes staring out of your head,\" was Dete's cross reply;"
1448 "\"but see, you shall have something nice,\" and she held out a"
1448 "bright new piece of money to him that sparkled in the sun. Peter"
1448 "was immediately up and off down the steep mountain side, taking"
1448 "the shortest cut, and in an incredibly short space of time had"
1448 "reached the little heap of clothes, which he gathered up under"
1448 "his arm, and was back again so quickly that even Dete was"
1448 "obliged to give him a word of praise as she handed him the"
1448 "promised money. Peter promptly thrust it into his pocket and his"
1448 "face beamed with delight, for it was not often that he was the"
1448 "happy possessor of such riches."
1448 ""
1448 "\"You can carry the things up for me as far as Uncle's, as you are"
1448 "going the same way,\" went on Dete, who was preparing to continue"
1448 "her climb up the mountain side, which rose in a steep ascent"
1448 "immediately behind the goatherd's hut. Peter willingly undertook"
1448 "to do this, and followed after her on his bare feet, with his"
1448 "left arm round the bundle and the right swinging his goatherd's"
1448 "stick, while Heidi and the goats went skipping and jumping"
1448 "joyfully beside him. After a climb of more than three-quarters"
1448 "of an hour they reached the top of the Alm mountain. Uncle's hut"
1448 "stood on a projection of the rock, exposed indeed to the winds,"
1448 "but where every ray of sun could rest upon it, and a full view"
1448 "could be had of the valley beneath. Behind the hut stood three"
1448 "old fir trees, with long, thick, unlopped branches. Beyond these"
1448 "rose a further wall of mountain, the lower heights still"
1448 "overgrown with beautiful grass and plants, above which were"
1448 "stonier slopes, covered only with scrub, that led gradually up"
1448 "to the steep, bare rocky summits."
1448 ""
1448 "Against the hut, on the side looking towards the valley, Uncle"
1448 "had put up a seat. Here he was sitting, his pipe in his mouth"
1448 "and his hands on his knees, quietly looking out, when the"
1448 "children, the goats and Cousin Dete suddenly clambered into view."
1448 "Heidi was at the top first. She went straight up to the old man,"
1448 "put out her hand, and said, \"Good-evening, Grandfather.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"So, so, what is the meaning of this?\" he asked gruffly, as he"
1448 "gave the child an abrupt shake of the hand, and gazed long and"
1448 "scrutinisingly at her from under his bushy eyebrows. Heidi"
1448 "stared steadily back at him in return with unflinching gaze, for"
1448 "the grandfather, with his long beard and thick grey eyebrows that"
1448 "grew together over his nose and looked just like a bush, was"
1448 "such a remarkable appearance, that Heidi was unable to take her"
1448 "eyes off him. Meanwhile Dete had come up, with Peter after her,"
1448 "and the latter now stood still a while to watch what was going"
1448 "on."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I wish you good-day, Uncle,\" said Dete, as she walked towards"
1448 "him, \"and I have brought you Tobias and Adelaide's child. You"
1448 "will hardly recognise her, as you have never seen her since she"
1448 "was a year old.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"And what has the child to do with me up here?\" asked the old"
1448 "man curtly. \"You there,\" he then called out to Peter, \"be off"
1448 "with your goats, you are none too early as it is, and take mine"
1448 "with you.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter obeyed on the instant and quickly disappeared, for the old"
1448 "man had given him a look that made him feel that he did not want"
1448 "to stay any longer."
1448 ""
1448 "\"The child is here to remain with you,\" Dete made answer. \"I"
1448 "have, I think, done my duty by her for these four years, and now"
1448 "it is time for you to do yours.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"That's it, is it?\" said the old man, as he looked at her with a"
1448 "flash in his eye. \"And when the child begins to fret and whine"
1448 "after you, as is the way with these unreasonable little beings,"
1448 "what am I to do with her then?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"That's your affair,\" retorted Dete. \"I know I had to put up"
1448 "with her without complaint when she was left on my hands as an"
1448 "infant, and with enough to do as it was for my mother and self."
1448 "Now I have to go and look after my own earnings, and you are the"
1448 "next of kin to the child. If you cannot arrange to keep her, do"
1448 "with her as you like. You will be answerable for the result if"
1448 "harm happens to her, though you have hardly need, I should think,"
1448 "to add to the burden already on your conscience.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Now Dete was not quite easy in her own conscience about what she"
1448 "was doing, and consequently was feeling hot and irritable, and"
1448 "said more than she had intended. As she uttered her last words,"
1448 "Uncle rose from his seat. He looked at her in a way that made"
1448 "her draw back a step or two, then flinging out his arm, he said"
1448 "to her in a commanding voice: \"Be off with you this instant, and"
1448 "get back as quickly as you can to the place whence you came, and"
1448 "do not let me see your face again in a hurry.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Dete did not wait to be told twice. \"Good-bye to you then, and"
1448 "to you too, Heidi,\" she called, as she turned quickly away and"
1448 "started to descend the mountain at a running pace, which she did"
1448 "not slacken till she found herself safely again at Dorfli, for"
1448 "some inward agitation drove her forwards as if a steam-engine"
1448 "was at work inside her. Again questions came raining down upon"
1448 "her from all sides, for every one knew Dete, as well as all"
1448 "particulars of the birth and former history of the child, and"
1448 "all wondered what she had done with it. From every door and"
1448 "window came voices calling: \"Where is the child?\" \"Where have you"
1448 "left the child, Dete?\" and more and more reluctantly Dete made"
1448 "answer, \"Up there with Alm-Uncle!\" \"With Alm-Uncle, have I not"
1448 "told you so already?\""
1448 ""
1448 "Then the women began to hurl reproaches at her; first one cried"
1448 "out, \"How could you do such a thing!\" then another, \"To think of"
1448 "leaving a helpless little thing up there,\"--while again and"
1448 "again came the words, \"The poor mite! the poor mite!\" pursuing"
1448 "her as she went along. Unable at last to bear it any longer Dete"
1448 "ran forward as fast as she could until she was beyond reach of"
1448 "their voices. She was far from happy at the thought of what she"
1448 "had done, for the child had been left in her care by her dying"
1448 "mother. She quieted herself, however, with the idea that she"
1448 "would be better able to do something for the child if she was"
1448 "earning plenty of money, and it was a relief to her to think"
1448 "that she would soon be far away from all these people who were"
1448 "making such a fuss about the matter, and she rejoiced further"
1448 "still that she was at liberty now to take such a good place."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER II. AT HOME WITH GRANDFATHER>"
1448 ""
1448 "As soon as Dete had disappeared the old man went back to his"
1448 "bench, and there he remained seated, staring on the ground"
1448 "without uttering a sound, while thick curls of smoke floated"
1448 "upward from his pipe. Heidi, meanwhile, was enjoying herself in"
1448 "her new surroundings; she looked about till she found a shed,"
1448 "built against the hut, where the goats were kept; she peeped in,"
1448 "and saw it was empty. She continued her search and presently"
1448 "came to the fir trees behind the hut. A strong breeze was blowing"
1448 "through them, and there was a rushing and roaring in their"
1448 "topmost branches, Heidi stood still and listened. The sound"
1448 "growing fainter, she went on again, to the farther corner of the"
1448 "hut, and so round to where her grandfather was sitting. Seeing"
1448 "that he was in exactly the same position as when she left him,"
1448 "she went and placed herself in front of the old man, and putting"
1448 "her hands behind her back, stood and gazed at him. Her"
1448 "grandfather looked up, and as she continued standing there"
1448 "without moving, \"What is it you want?\" he asked."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I want to see what you have inside the house,\" said Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Come then!\" and the grandfather rose and went before her"
1448 "towards the hut."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Bring your bundle of clothes in with you,\" he bid her as she"
1448 "was following."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I shan't want them any more,\" was her prompt answer."
1448 ""
1448 "The old man turned and looked searchingly at the child, whose"
1448 "dark eyes were sparkling in delighted anticipation of what she"
1448 "was going to see inside. \"She is certainly not wanting in"
1448 "intelligence,\" he murmured to himself. \"And why shall you not"
1448 "want them any more?\" he asked aloud."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Because I want to go about like the goats with their thin light"
1448 "legs.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well, you can do so if you like,\" said her grandfather, \"but"
1448 "bring the things in, we must put them in the cupboard.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi did as she was told. The old man now opened the door and"
1448 "Heidi stepped inside after him; she found herself in a good-"
1448 "sized room, which covered the whole ground floor of the hut. A"
1448 "table and a chair were the only furniture; in one corner stood"
1448 "the grandfather's bed, in another was the hearth with a large"
1448 "kettle hanging above it; and on the further side was a large door"
1448 "in the wall--this was the cupboard. The grandfather opened it;"
1448 "inside were his clothes, some hanging up, others, a couple of"
1448 "shirts, and some socks and handkerchiefs, lying on a shelf; on a"
1448 "second shelf were some plates and cups and glasses, and on a"
1448 "higher one still, a round loaf, smoked meat, and cheese, for"
1448 "everything that Alm-Uncle needed for his food and clothing was"
1448 "kept in this cupboard. Heidi, as soon as it was opened, ran"
1448 "quickly forward and thrust in her bundle of clothes, as far back"
1448 "behind her grandfather's things as possible, so that they might"
1448 "not easily be found again. She then looked carefully round the"
1448 "room, and asked, \"Where am I to sleep, grandfather?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Wherever you like,\" he answered."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi was delighted, and began at once to examine all the nooks"
1448 "and corners to find out where it would be pleasantest to sleep."
1448 "In the corner near her grandfather's bed she saw a short ladder"
1448 "against the wall; up she climbed and found herself in the"
1448 "hayloft. There lay a large heap of fresh sweet-smelling hay,"
1448 "while through a round window in the wall she could see right"
1448 "down the valley."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I shall sleep up here, grandfather,\" she called down to him,"
1448 "\"It's lovely, up here. Come up and see how lovely it is!\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh, I know all about it,\" he called up in answer."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I am getting the bed ready now,\" she called down again, as she"
1448 "went busily to and fro at her work, \"but I shall want you to"
1448 "bring me up a sheet; you can't have a bed without a sheet, you"
1448 "want it to lie upon.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"All right,\" said the grandfather, and presently he went to the"
1448 "cupboard, and after rummaging about inside for a few minutes he"
1448 "drew out a long, coarse piece of stuff, which was all he had to"
1448 "do duty for a sheet. He carried it up to the loft, where he"
1448 "found Heidi had already made quite a nice bed. She had put an"
1448 "extra heap of hay at one end for a pillow, and had so arranged it"
1448 "that, when in bed, she would be able to see comfortably out"
1448 "through the round window."
1448 ""
1448 "\"That is capital,\" said her grandfather; \"now we must put on the"
1448 "sheet, but wait a moment first,\" and he went and fetched another"
1448 "large bundle of hay to make the bed thicker, so that the child"
1448 "should not feel the hard floor under her--\"there, now bring it"
1448 "here.\" Heidi had got hold of the sheet, but it was almost too"
1448 "heavy for her to carry; this was a good thing, however, as the"
1448 "close thick stuff would prevent the sharp stalks of the hay"
1448 "running through and pricking her. The two together now spread"
1448 "the sheet over the bed, and where it was too long or too broad,"
1448 "Heidi quickly tucked it in under the hay. It looked now as tidy"
1448 "and comfortable a bed as you could wish for, and Heidi stood"
1448 "gazing thoughtfully at her handiwork."
1448 ""
1448 "\"We have forgotten something now, grandfather,\" she said after a"
1448 "short silence."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What's that?\" he asked."
1448 ""
1448 "\"A coverlid; when you get into bed, you have to creep in between"
1448 "the sheets and the coverlid.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh, that's the way, is it? But suppose I have not got a"
1448 "coverlid?\" said the old man."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well, never mind, grandfather,\" said Heidi in a consoling tone"
1448 "of voice, \"I can take some more hay to put over me,\" and she was"
1448 "turning quickly to fetch another armful from the heap, when her"
1448 "grandfather stopped her. \"Wait a moment,\" he said, and he"
1448 "climbed down the ladder again and went towards his bed. He"
1448 "returned to the loft with a large, thick sack, made of flax,"
1448 "which he threw down, exclaiming, \"There, that is better than hay,"
1448 "is it not?\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi began tugging away at the sack with all her little might,"
1448 "in her efforts to get it smooth and straight, but her small"
1448 "hands were not fitted for so heavy a job. Her grandfather came to"
1448 "her assistance, and when they had got it tidily spread over the"
1448 "bed, it all looked so nice and warm and comfortable that Heidi"
1448 "stood gazing at it in delight. \"That is a splendid coverlid,\" she"
1448 "said, \"and the bed looks lovely altogether! I wish it was night,"
1448 "so that I might get inside it at once.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I think we might have something to eat first,\" said the"
1448 "grandfather, \"what do you think?\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi in the excitement of bed-making had forgotten everything"
1448 "else; but now when she began to think about food she felt"
1448 "terribly hungry, for she had had nothing to eat since the piece"
1448 "of bread and little cup of thin coffee that had been her"
1448 "breakfast early that morning before starting on her long, hot"
1448 "journey. So she answered without hesitation, \"Yes, I think so"
1448 "too.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Let us go down then, as we both think alike,\" said the old man,"
1448 "and he followed the child down the ladder. Then he went up to"
1448 "the hearth, pushed the big kettle aside, and drew forward the"
1448 "little one that was hanging on the chain, and seating himself on"
1448 "the round-topped, three-legged stool before the fire, blew it up"
1448 "into a clear bright flame. The kettle soon began to boil, and"
1448 "meanwhile the old man held a large piece of cheese on a long"
1448 "iron fork over the fire, turning it round and round till it was"
1448 "toasted a nice golden yellow color on each side. Heidi watched"
1448 "all that was going on with eager curiosity. Suddenly some new"
1448 "idea seemed to come into her head, for she turned and ran to the"
1448 "cupboard, and then began going busily backwards and forwards."
1448 "Presently the grandfather got up and came to the table with a"
1448 "jug and the cheese, and there he saw it already tidily laid with"
1448 "the round loaf and two plates and two knives each in its right"
1448 "place; for Heidi had taken exact note that morning of all that"
1448 "there was in the cupboard, and she knew which things would be"
1448 "wanted for their meal."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Ah, that's right,\" said the grandfather, \"I am glad to see that"
1448 "you have some ideas of your own,\" and as he spoke he laid the"
1448 "toasted cheese on a layer of bread, \"but there is still"
1448 "something missing.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi looked at the jug that was steaming away invitingly, and"
1448 "ran quickly back to the cupboard. At first she could only see a"
1448 "small bowl left on the shelf, but she was not long in"
1448 "perplexity, for a moment later she caught sight of two glasses"
1448 "further back, and without an instant's loss of time she returned"
1448 "with these and the bowl and put them down on the table."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Good, I see you know how to set about things; but what will you"
1448 "do for a seat?\" The grandfather himself was sitting on the only"
1448 "chair in the room. Heidi flew to the hearth, and dragging the"
1448 "three-legged stool up to the table, sat herself down upon it."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well, you have managed to find a seat for yourself, I see, only"
1448 "rather a low one I am afraid,\" said the grandfather, \"but you"
1448 "would not be tall enough to reach the table even if you sat in"
1448 "my chair; the first thing now, however, is to have something to"
1448 "eat, so come along.\""
1448 ""
1448 "With that he stood up, filled the bowl with milk, and placing it"
1448 "on the chair, pushed it in front of Heidi on her little three-"
1448 "legged stool, so that she now had a table to herself. Then he"
1448 "brought her a large slice of bread and a piece of the golden"
1448 "cheese, and told her to eat. After which he went and sat down on"
1448 "the corner of the table and began his own meal. Heidi lifted the"
1448 "bowl with both hands and drank without pause till it was empty,"
1448 "for the thirst of all her long hot journey had returned upon"
1448 "her. Then she drew a deep breath--in the eagerness of her thirst"
1448 "she had not stopped to breathe--and put down the bowl."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Was the milk nice?\" asked her grandfather."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I never drank any so good before,\" answered Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Then you must have some more,\" and the old man filled her bowl"
1448 "again to the brim and set it before the child, who was now"
1448 "hungrily beginning her bread having first spread it with the"
1448 "cheese, which after being toasted was soft as butter; the two"
1448 "together tasted deliciously, and the child looked the picture of"
1448 "content as she sat eating, and at intervals taking further"
1448 "draughts of milk. The meal being over, the grandfather went"
1448 "outside to put the goat-shed in order, and Heidi watched with"
1448 "interest while he first swept it out, and then put fresh straw"
1448 "for the goats to sleep upon. Then he went to the little well-"
1448 "shed, and there he cut some long round sticks, and a small round"
1448 "board; in this he bored some holes and stuck the sticks into"
1448 "them, and there, as if made by magic, was a three-legged stool"
1448 "just like her grandfather's, only higher. Heidi stood and looked"
1448 "at it, speechless with astonishment."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What do you think that is?\" asked her grandfather."
1448 ""
1448 "\"It's my stool, I know, because it is such a high one; and it"
1448 "was made all of a minute,\" said the child, still lost in wonder"
1448 "and admiration."
1448 ""
1448 "\"She understands what she sees, her eyes are in the right"
1448 "place,\" remarked the grandfather to himself, as he continued his"
1448 "way round the hut, knocking in a nail here and there, or making"
1448 "fast some part of the door, and so with hammer and nails and"
1448 "pieces of wood going from spot to spot, mending or clearing away"
1448 "wherever work of the kind was needed. Heidi followed him step by"
1448 "step, her eyes attentively taking in all that he did, and"
1448 "everything that she saw was a fresh source of pleasure to her."
1448 ""
1448 "And so the time passed happily on till evening. Then the wind"
1448 "began to roar louder than ever through the old fir trees; Heidi"
1448 "listened with delight to the sound, and it filled her heart so"
1448 "full of gladness that she skipped and danced round the old"
1448 "trees, as if some unheard of joy had come to her. The grandfather"
1448 "stood and watched her from the shed."
1448 ""
1448 "Suddenly a shrill whistle was heard. Heidi paused in her"
1448 "dancing, and the grandfather came out. Down from the heights"
1448 "above the goats came springing one after another, with Peter in"
1448 "their midst. Heidi sprang forward with a cry of joy and rushed"
1448 "among the flock, greeting first one and then another of her old"
1448 "friends of the morning. As they neared the hut the goats stood"
1448 "still, and then two of their number, two beautiful slender"
1448 "animals, one white and one brown, ran forward to where the"
1448 "grandfather was standing and began licking his hands, for he was"
1448 "holding a little salt which he always had ready for his goats on"
1448 "their return home. Peter disappeared with the remainder of his"
1448 "flock. Heidi tenderly stroked the two goats in turn, running"
1448 "first to one side of them and then the other, and jumping about"
1448 "in her glee at the pretty little animals. \"Are they ours,"
1448 "grandfather? Are they both ours? Are you going to put them in the"
1448 "shed? Will they always stay with us?\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi's questions came tumbling out one after the other, so that"
1448 "her grandfather had only time to answer each of them with \"Yes,"
1448 "yes.\" When the goats had finished licking up the salt her"
1448 "grandfather told her to go and fetch her bowl and the bread."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi obeyed and was soon back again. The grandfather milked the"
1448 "white goat and filled her basin, and then breaking off a piece"
1448 "of bread, \"Now eat your supper,\" he said, \"and then go up to bed."
1448 "Cousin Dete left another little bundle for you with a nightgown"
1448 "and other small things in it, which you will find at the bottom"
1448 "of the cupboard if you want them. I must go and shut up the"
1448 "goats, so be off and sleep well.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Good-night, grandfather! good-night. What are their names,"
1448 "grandfather, what are their names?\" she called out as she ran"
1448 "after his retreating figure and the goats."
1448 ""
1448 "\"The white one is named Little Swan, and the brown one Little"
1448 "Bear,\" he answered."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Good-night, Little Swan, good-night, Little Bear!\" she called"
1448 "again at the top of her voice, for they were already inside the"
1448 "shed. Then she sat down on the seat and began to eat and drink,"
1448 "but the wind was so strong that it almost blew her away; so she"
1448 "made haste and finished her supper and then went indoors and"
1448 "climbed up to her bed, where she was soon lying as sweetly and"
1448 "soundly asleep as any young princess on her couch of silk."
1448 ""
1448 "Not long after, and while it was still twilight, the grandfather"
1448 "also went to bed, for he was up every morning at sunrise, and"
1448 "the sun came climbing up over the mountains at a very early hour"
1448 "during these summer months. The wind grew so tempestuous during"
1448 "the night, and blew in such gusts against the walls, that the"
1448 "hut trembled and the old beams groaned and creaked. It came"
1448 "howling and wailing down the chimney like voices of those in"
1448 "pain, and it raged with such fury among the old fir trees that"
1448 "here and there a branch was snapped and fell. In the middle of"
1448 "the night the old man got up. \"The child will be frightened,\" he"
1448 "murmured half aloud. He mounted the ladder and went and stood by"
1448 "the child's bed."
1448 ""
1448 "Outside the moon was struggling with the dark, fast-driving"
1448 "clouds, which at one moment left it clear and shining, and the"
1448 "next swept over it, and all again was dark. Just now the"
1448 "moonlight was falling through the round window straight on to"
1448 "Heidi's bed. She lay under the heavy coverlid, her cheeks rosy"
1448 "with sleep, her head peacefully resting on her little round arm,"
1448 "and with a happy expression on her baby face as if dreaming of"
1448 "something pleasant. The old man stood looking down on the"
1448 "sleeping child until the moon again disappeared behind the"
1448 "clouds and he could see no more, then he went back to bed."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER III. OUT WITH THE GOATS>"
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi was awakened early the next morning by a loud whistle; the"
1448 "sun was shining through the round window and falling in golden"
1448 "rays on her bed and on the large heap of hay, and as she opened"
1448 "her eyes everything in the loft seemed gleaming with gold. She"
1448 "looked around her in astonishment and could not imagine for a"
1448 "while where she was. But her grandfather's deep voice was now"
1448 "heard outside, and then Heidi began to recall all that had"
1448 "happened: how she had come away from her former home and was now"
1448 "on the mountain with her grandfather instead of with old Ursula."
1448 "The latter was nearly stone deaf and always felt cold, so that"
1448 "she sat all day either by the hearth in the kitchen or by the"
1448 "sitting-room stove, and Heidi had been obliged to stay close to"
1448 "her, for the old woman was so deaf that she could not tell where"
1448 "the child was if out of her sight. And Heidi, shut up within the"
1448 "four walls, had often longed to be out of doors. So she felt"
1448 "very happy this morning as she woke up in her new home and"
1448 "remembered all the many new things that she had seen the day"
1448 "before and which she would see again that day, and above all she"
1448 "thought with delight of the two dear goats. Heidi jumped quickly"
1448 "out of bed and a very few minutes sufficed her to put on the"
1448 "clothes which she had taken off the night before, for there were"
1448 "not many of them. Then she climbed down the ladder and ran"
1448 "outside the hut. There stood Peter already with his flock of"
1448 "goats, and the grandfather was just bringing his two out of the"
1448 "shed to join the others. Heidi ran forward to wish good-morning"
1448 "to him and the goats."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Do you want to go with them on to the mountain?\" asked her"
1448 "grandfather. Nothing could have pleased Heidi better, and she"
1448 "jumped for joy in answer."
1448 ""

1448 ""
1448 "\"I know that one too,\" he said, giving her its name. \"So you"
1448 "enjoyed being out with the goats?\""
1448 ""
1448 "Then Heidi went on to give him an account of the whole day, and"
1448 "of how delightful it had all been, and particularly described"
1448 "the fire that had burst out everywhere in the evening. And then"
1448 "nothing would do but her grandfather must tell how it came, for"
1448 "Peter knew nothing about it."
1448 ""
1448 "The grandfather explained to her that it was the sun that did"
1448 "it. \"When he says good-night to the mountains he throws his most"
1448 "beautiful colors over them, so that they may not forget him"
1448 "before he comes again the next day.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi was delighted with this explanation, and could hardly bear"
1448 "to wait for another day to come that she might once more climb"
1448 "up with the goats and see how the sun bid good-night to the"
1448 "mountains. But she had to go to bed first, and all night she"
1448 "slept soundly on her bed of hay, dreaming of nothing but of"
1448 "shining mountains with red roses all over them, among which"
1448 "happy little Snowflake went leaping in and out."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER IV. THE VISIT TO GRANDMOTHER>"
1448 ""
1448 "The next morning the sun came out early as bright as ever, and"
1448 "then Peter appeared with the goats, and again the two children"
1448 "climbed up together to the high meadows, and so it went on day"
1448 "after day till Heidi, passing her life thus among the grass and"
1448 "flowers, was burnt brown with the sun, and grew so strong and"
1448 "healthy that nothing ever ailed her. She was happy too, and"
1448 "lived from day to day as free and lighthearted as the little"
1448 "birds that make their home among the green forest trees. Then the"
1448 "autumn came, and the wind blew louder and stronger, and the"
1448 "grandfather would say sometimes, \"To-day you must stay at home,"
1448 "Heidi; a sudden gust of the wind would blow a little thing like"
1448 "you over the rocks into the valley below in a moment.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Whenever Peter heard that he must go alone he looked very"
1448 "unhappy, for he saw nothing but mishaps of all kinds ahead, and"
1448 "did not know how he should bear the long dull day without Heidi."
1448 "Then, too, there was the good meal he would miss, and besides"
1448 "that the goats on these days were so naughty and obstinate that"
1448 "he had twice the usual trouble with them, for they had grown so"
1448 "accustomed to Heidi's presence that they would run in every"
1448 "direction and refuse to go on unless she was with them. Heidi"
1448 "was never unhappy, for wherever she was she found something to"
1448 "interest or amuse her. She liked best, it is true, to go out"
1448 "with Peter up to the flowers and the great bird, where there was"
1448 "so much to be seen, and so many experiences to go through among"
1448 "the goats with their different characters; but she also found her"
1448 "grandfather's hammering and sawing and carpentering very"
1448 "entertaining, and if it should chance to be the day when the"
1448 "large round goat's-milk cheese was made she enjoyed beyond"
1448 "measure looking on at this wonderful performance, and watching"
1448 "her grandfather, as with sleeves rolled back, he stirred the"
1448 "great cauldron with his bare arms. The thing which attracted her"
1448 "most, however, was the waving and roaring of the three old fir"
1448 "trees on these windy days. She would run away repeatedly from"
1448 "whatever she might be doing, to listen to them, for nothing"
1448 "seemed so strange and wonderful to her as the deep mysterious"
1448 "sound in the tops of the trees. She would stand underneath them"
1448 "and look up, unable to tear herself away, looking and listening"
1448 "while they bowed and swayed and roared as the mighty wind rushed"
1448 "through them. There was no longer now the warm bright sun that"
1448 "had shone all through the summer, so Heidi went to the cupboard"
1448 "and got out her shoes and stockings and dress, for it was"
1448 "growing colder every day, and when Heidi stood under the fir"
1448 "trees the wind blew through her as if she was a thin little leaf,"
1448 "but still she felt she could not stay indoors when she heard the"
1448 "branches waving outside."
1448 ""
1448 "Then it grew very cold, and Peter would come up early in the"
1448 "morning blowing on his fingers to keep them warm. But he soon"
1448 "left off coming, for one night there was a heavy fall of snow"
1448 "and the next morning the whole mountain was covered with it, and"
1448 "not a single little green leaf was to be seen anywhere upon it."
1448 "There was no Peter that day, and Heidi stood at the little window"
1448 "looking out in wonderment, for the snow was beginning again, and"
1448 "the thick flakes kept falling till the snow was up to the"
1448 "window, and still they continued to fall, and the snow grew"
1448 "higher, so that at last the window could not be opened, and she"
1448 "and her grandfather were shut up fast within the hut. Heidi"
1448 "thought this was great fun and ran from one window to the other"
1448 "to see what would happen next, and whether the snow was going to"
1448 "cover up the whole hut, so that they would have to light a lamp"
1448 "although it was broad daylight. But things did not get as bad as"
1448 "that, and the next day, the snow having ceased, the grandfather"
1448 "went out and shovelled away the snow round the house, and threw"
1448 "it into such great heaps that they looked like mountains standing"
1448 "at intervals on either side the hut. And now the windows and door"
1448 "could be opened, and it was well it was so, for as Heidi and her"
1448 "grandfather were sitting one afternoon on their three-legged"
1448 "stools before the fire there came a great thump at the door"
1448 "followed by several others, and then the door opened. It was"
1448 "Peter, who had made all that noise knocking the snow off his"
1448 "shoes; he was still white all over with it, for he had had to"
1448 "fight his way through deep snowdrifts, and large lumps of snow"
1448 "that had frozen upon him still clung to his clothes. He had been"
1448 "determined, however, not to be beaten and to climb up to the"
1448 "hut, for it was a week now since he had seen Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Good-evening,\" he said as he came in; then he went and placed"
1448 "himself as near the fire as he could without saying another"
1448 "word, but his whole face was beaming with pleasure at finding"
1448 "himself there. Heidi looked on in astonishment, for Peter was"
1448 "beginning to thaw all over with the warmth, so that he had the"
1448 "appearance of a trickling waterfall."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well, General, and how goes it with you?\" said the grandfather,"
1448 "\"now that you have lost your army you will have to turn to your"
1448 "pen and pencil.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Why must he turn to his pen and pencil?\" asked Heidi"
1448 "immediately, full of curiosity."
1448 ""
1448 "\"During the winter he must go to school,\" explained her"
1448 "grandfather, \"and learn how to read and write; it's a bit hard,"
1448 "although useful sometimes afterwards. Am I not right, General?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, indeed,\" assented Peter."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi's interest was now thoroughly awakened, and she had so"
1448 "many questions to put to Peter about all that was to be done and"
1448 "seen and heard at school, and the conversation took so long that"
1448 "Peter had time to get thoroughly dry. Peter had always great"
1448 "difficulty in putting his thoughts into words, and he found his"
1448 "share of the talk doubly difficult to-day, for by the time he had"
1448 "an answer ready to one of Heidi's questions she had already put"
1448 "two or three more to him, and generally such as required a whole"
1448 "long sentence in reply."
1448 ""
1448 "The grandfather sat without speaking during this conversation,"
1448 "only now and then a twitch of amusement at the corners of his"
1448 "mouth showed that he was listening."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well, now, General, you have been under fire for some time and"
1448 "must want some refreshment, come and join us,\" he said at last,"
1448 "and as he spoke he rose and went to fetch the supper out of the"
1448 "cupboard, and Heidi pushed the stools to the table. There was"
1448 "also now a bench fastened against the wall, for as he was no"
1448 "longer alone the grandfather had put up seats of various kinds"
1448 "here and there, long enough to hold two persons, for Heidi had a"
1448 "way of always keeping close to her grandfather whether he was"
1448 "walking, sitting or standing. So there was comfortable place for"
1448 "them all three, and Peter opened his round eyes very wide when"
1448 "he saw what a large piece of meat Alm-Uncle gave him on his thick"
1448 "slice of bread. It was a long time since Peter had had anything"
1448 "so nice to eat. As soon as the pleasant meal was over Peter"
1448 "began to get ready for returning home, for it was already growing"
1448 "dark. He had said his \"good-night\" and his thanks, and was just"
1448 "going out, when he turned again and said, \"I shall come again"
1448 "next Sunday, this day week, and grandmother sent word that she"
1448 "would like you to come and see her one day.\""
1448 ""
1448 "It was quite a new idea to Heidi that she should go and pay"
1448 "anybody a visit, and she could not get it out of her head; so"
1448 "the first thing she said to her grandfather the next day was, \"I"
1448 "must go down to see the grandmother to-day; she will be expecting"
1448 "me.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"The snow is too deep,\" answered the grandfather, trying to put"
1448 "her off. But Heidi had made up her mind to go, since the"
1448 "grandmother had sent her that message. She stuck to her"
1448 "intention and not a day passed but what in the course of it she"
1448 "said five or six times to her grandfather, \"I must certainly go"
1448 "to-day, the grandmother will be waiting for me.\""
1448 ""
1448 "On the fourth day, when with every step one took the ground"
1448 "crackled with frost and the whole vast field of snow was hard as"
1448 "ice, Heidi was sitting on her high stool at dinner with the"
1448 "bright sun shining in upon her through the window, and again"
1448 "repeated her little speech, \"I must certainly go down to see the"
1448 "grandmother to-day, or else I shall keep her waiting too long.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The grandfather rose from table, climbed up to the hay-loft and"
1448 "brought down the thick sack that was Heidi's coverlid, and said,"
1448 "\"Come along then!\" The child skipped out gleefully after him"
1448 "into the glittering world of snow."
1448 ""
1448 "The old fir trees were standing now quite silent, their branches"
1448 "covered with the white snow, and they looked so lovely as they"
1448 "glittered and sparkled in the sunlight that Heidi jumped for joy"
1448 "at the sight and kept on calling out, \"Come here, come here,"
1448 "grandfather! The fir trees are all silver and gold!\" The"
1448 "grandfather had gone into the shed and he now came out dragging"
1448 "a large hand-sleigh along with him; inside it was a low seat, and"
1448 "the sleigh could be pushed forward and guided by the feet of the"
1448 "one who sat upon it with the help of a pole that was fastened to"
1448 "the side. After he had been taken round the fir trees by Heidi"
1448 "that he might see their beauty from all sides, he got into the"
1448 "sleigh and lifted the child on to his lap; then he wrapped her"
1448 "up in the sack, that she might keep nice and warm, and put his"
1448 "left arm closely round her, for it was necessary to hold her"
1448 "tight during the coming journey. He now grasped the pole with his"
1448 "right hand and gave the sleigh a push forward with his two feet."
1448 "The sleigh shot down the mountain side with such rapidity that"
1448 "Heidi thought they were flying through the air like a bird, and"
1448 "shouted aloud with delight. Suddenly they came to a standstill,"
1448 "and there they were at Peter's hut. Her grandfather lifted her"
1448 "out and unwrapped her. \"There you are, now go in, and when it"
1448 "begins to grow dark you must start on your way home again.\" Then"
1448 "he left her and went up the mountain, pulling his sleigh after"
1448 "him."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi opened the door of the hut and stepped into a tiny room"
1448 "that looked very dark, with a fireplace and a few dishes on a"
1448 "wooden shelf; this was the little kitchen. She opened another"
1448 "door, and now found herself in another small room, for the place"
1448 "was not a herdsman's hut like her grandfather's, with one large"
1448 "room on the ground floor and a hay-loft above, but a very old"
1448 "cottage, where everything was narrow and poor and shabby. A"
1448 "table was close to the door, and as Heidi stepped in she saw a"
1448 "woman sitting at it, putting a patch on a waistcoat which Heidi"
1448 "recognised at once as Peter's. In the corner sat an old woman,"
1448 "bent with age, spinning. Heidi was quite sure this was the"
1448 "grandmother, so she went up to the spinning-wheel and said, \"Good-"
1448 "day, grandmother, I have come at last; did you think I was a long"
1448 "time coming?\""
1448 ""
1448 "The woman raised her head and felt for the hand that the child"
1448 "held out to her, and when she found it, she passed her own over"
1448 "it thoughtfully for a few seconds, and then said, \"Are you the"
1448 "child who lives up with Alm-Uncle, are you Heidi?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, yes,\" answered Heidi, \"I have just come down in the sleigh"
1448 "with grandfather.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Is it possible! Why your hands are quite warm! Brigitta, did Alm-"
1448 "Uncle come himself with the child?\""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter's mother had left her work and risen from the table and"
1448 "now stood looking at Heidi with curiosity, scanning her from head"
1448 "to foot. \"I do not know, mother, whether Uncle came himself; it"
1448 "is hardly likely, the child probably makes a mistake.\""
1448 ""
1448 "But Heidi looked steadily at the woman, not at all as if in any"
1448 "uncertainty, and said, \"I know quite well who wrapped me in my"
1448 "bedcover and brought me down in the sleigh: it was grandfather.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"There was some truth then perhaps in what Peter used to tell us"
1448 "of Alm-Uncle during the summer, when we thought he must be"
1448 "wrong,\" said grandmother; \"but who would ever have believed that"
1448 "such a thing was possible? I did not think the child would live"
1448 "three weeks up there. What is she like, Brigitta?\""
1448 ""
1448 "The latter had so thoroughly examined Heidi on all sides that"
1448 "she was well able to describe her to her mother."
1448 ""
1448 "\"She has Adelaide's slenderness of figure, but her eyes are dark"
1448 "and her hair curly like her father's and the old man's up there:"
1448 "she takes after both of them, I think.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi meanwhile had not been idle; she had made the round of the"
1448 "room and looked carefully at everything there was to be seen."
1448 "All of a sudden she exclaimed, \"Grandmother, one of your shutters"
1448 "is flapping backwards and forwards; grandfather would put a nail"
1448 "in and make it all right in a minute, or else it will break one"
1448 "of the panes some day; look, look, how it keeps on banging!\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Ah, dear child,\" said the old woman, \"I am not able to see it,"
1448 "but I can hear that and many other things besides the shutter."
1448 "Everything about the place rattles and creaks when the wind is"
1448 "blowing, and it gets inside through all the cracks and holes."
1448 "The house is going to pieces, and in the night, when the two"
1448 "others are asleep, I often lie awake in fear and trembling,"
1448 "thinking that the whole place will give way and fall and kill us."
1448 "And there is not a creature to mend anything for us, for Peter"
1448 "does not understand such work.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"But why cannot you see, grandmother, that the shutter is loose."
1448 "Look, there it goes again, see, that one there!\" And Heidi"
1448 "pointed to the particular shutter."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Alas, child, it is not only that I cannot see--I can see,"
1448 "nothing, nothing,\" said the grandmother in a voice of"
1448 "lamentation."
1448 ""
1448 "\"But if I were to go outside and put back the shutter so that"
1448 "you had more light, then you could see, grandmother?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"No, no, not even then, no one can make it light for me again.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"But if you were to go outside among all the white snow, then"
1448 "surely you would find it light; just come with me, grandmother,"
1448 "and I will show you.\" Heidi took hold of the old woman's hand to"
1448 "lead her along, for she was beginning to feel quite distressed"
1448 "at the thought of her being without light."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Let me be, dear child; it is always dark for me now; whether in"
1448 "snow or sun, no light can penetrate my eyes.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"But surely it does in summer, grandmother,\" said Heidi, more"
1448 "and more anxious to find some way out of the trouble, \"when the"
1448 "hot sun is shining down again, and he says good-night to the"
1448 "mountains, and they all turn on fire, and the yellow flowers"
1448 "shine like gold, then, you will see, it will be bright and"
1448 "beautiful for you again.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Ah, child, I shall see the mountains on fire or the yellow"
1448 "flowers no more; it will never be light for me again on earth,"
1448 "never.\""
1448 ""
1448 "At these words Heidi broke into loud crying. In her distress she"
1448 "kept on sobbing out, \"Who can make it light for you again? Can"
1448 "no one do it? Isn't there any one who can do it?\""
1448 ""
1448 "The grandmother now tried to comfort the child, but it was not"
1448 "easy to quiet her. Heidi did not often weep, but when she did"
1448 "she could not get over her trouble for a long while. The"
1448 "grandmother had tried all means in her power to allay the child's"
1448 "grief, for it went to her heart to hear her sobbing so bitterly."
1448 "At last she said, \"Come here, dear Heidi, come and let me tell"
1448 "you something. You cannot think how glad one is to hear a kind"
1448 "word when one can no longer see, and it is such a pleasure to me"
1448 "to listen to you while you talk. So come and sit beside me and"
1448 "tell me something; tell me what you do up there, and how"
1448 "grandfather occupies himself. I knew him very well in old days;"
1448 "but for many years now I have heard nothing of him, except"
1448 "through Peter, who never says much.\""
1448 ""
1448 "This was a new and happy idea to Heidi; she quickly dried her"
1448 "tears and said in a comforting voice, \"Wait, grandmother, till I"
1448 "have told grandfather everything, he will make it light for you"
1448 "again, I am sure, and will do something so that the house will"
1448 "not fall; he will put everything right for you.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The grandmother was silent, and Heidi now began to give her a"
1448 "lively description of her life with the grandfather, and of the"
1448 "days she spent on the mountain with the goats, and then went on"
1448 "to tell her of what she did now during the winter, and how her"
1448 "grandfather was able to make all sorts of things, seats and"
1448 "stools, and mangers where the hay was put for Little Swan and"
1448 "Little Bear, besides a new large water-tub for her to bathe in"
1448 "when the summer came, and a new milk-bowl and spoon, and Heidi"
1448 "grew more and more animated as she enumerated all the beautiful"
1448 "things which were made so magically out of pieces of wood; she"
1448 "then told the grandmother how she stood by him and watched all"
1448 "he did, and how she hoped some day to be able to make the same"
1448 "herself."
1448 ""
1448 "The grandmother listened with the greatest attention, only from"
1448 "time to time addressing her daughter, \"Do you hear that,"
1448 "Brigitta? Do you hear what she is saying about Uncle?\""
1448 ""
1448 "The conversation was all at once interrupted by a heavy thump on"
1448 "the door, and in marched Peter, who stood stock-still, opening"
1448 "his eyes with astonishment, when he caught sight of Heidi; then"
1448 "his face beamed with smiles as she called out, \"Good-evening,"
1448 "Peter.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"What, is the boy back from school already?\" exclaimed the"
1448 "grandmother in surprise. \"I have not known an afternoon pass so"
1448 "quickly as this one for years. How is the reading getting on,"
1448 "Peter?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Just the same,\" was Peter's answer."
1448 ""
1448 "The old woman gave a little sigh. \"Ah, well,\" she said, \"I hoped"
1448 "you would have something different to tell me by this time, as"
1448 "you are going to be twelve years old this February.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"What was it that you hoped he would have to tell you?\" asked"
1448 "Heidi, interested in all the grandmother said."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I mean that he ought to have learnt to read a bit by now,\""
1448 "continued the grandmother. \"Up there on the shelf is an old"
1448 "prayer-book, with beautiful songs in it which I have not heard"
1448 "for a long time and cannot now remember to repeat to myself, and"
1448 "I hoped that Peter would soon learn enough to be able to read"
1448 "one of them to me sometimes; but he finds it too difficult.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I must get a light, it is getting too dark to see,\" said"
1448 "Peter's mother, who was still busy mending his waistcoat. \"I feel"
1448 "too as if the afternoon had gone I hardly know how.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi now jumped up from her low chair, and holding out her hand"
1448 "hastily to the grandmother said, \"Good-night, grandmother, if it"
1448 "is getting dark I must go home at once,\" and bidding good-bye to"
1448 "Peter and his mother she went towards the door. But the"
1448 "grandmother called out in an anxious voice, \"Wait, wait, Heidi;"
1448 "you must not go alone like that, Peter must go with you; and"
1448 "take care of the child, Peter, that she does not fall, and don't"
1448 "let her stand still for fear she should get frozen, do you hear?"
1448 "Has she got anything warm to put around her throat?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I have not anything to put on,\" called back Heidi, \"but I am"
1448 "sure I shall not be cold,\" and with that she ran outside and"
1448 "went off at such a pace that Peter had difficulty in overtaking"
1448 "her. The grandmother, still in distress, called out to her"
1448 "daughter, \"Run after her, Brigitta; the child will be frozen to"
1448 "death on such a night as this; take my shawl, run quickly!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Brigitta ran out. But the children had taken but a few steps"
1448 "before they saw the grandfather coming down to meet them, and in"
1448 "another minute his long strides had brought him to their side."
1448 ""
1448 "\"That's right, Heidi; you have kept your word,\" said the"
1448 "grandfather, and then wrapping the sack firmly round her he"
1448 "lifted her in his arms and strode off with her up the mountain."
1448 "Brigitta was just in time to see him do all this, and on her"
1448 "return to the hut with Peter expressed her astonishment to the"
1448 "grandmother. The latter was equally surprised, and kept on"
1448 "saying, \"God be thanked that he is good to the child, God be"
1448 "thanked! Will he let her come to me again, I wonder! the child"
1448 "has done me so much good. What a loving little heart it is, and"
1448 "how merrily she tells her tale!\" And she continued to dwell with"
1448 "delight on the thought of the child until she went to bed, still"
1448 "saying now and again, \"If only she will come again! Now I have"
1448 "really something left in the world to take pleasure in.\" And"
1448 "Brigitta agreed with all her mother said, and Peter nodded his"
1448 "head in approval each time his grandmother spoke, saying, with a"
1448 "broad smile of satisfaction, \"I told you so!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Meanwhile Heidi was chattering away to her grandfather from"
1448 "inside her sack; her voice, however, could not reach him through"
1448 "the many thick folds of her wrap, and as therefore it was"
1448 "impossible to understand a word she was saying, he called to"
1448 "her, \"Wait till we get home, and then you can tell me all about"
1448 "it.\" They had no sooner got inside the hut than Heidi, having"
1448 "been released from her covering, at once began what she had to"
1448 "say, \"Grandfather, to-morrow we must take the hammer and the long"
1448 "nails and fasten grandmother's shutter, and drive in a lot more"
1448 "nails in other places, for her house shakes and rattles all"
1448 "over.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"We must, must we? who told you that?\" asked her grandfather."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Nobody told me, but I know it for all that,\" replied Heidi,"
1448 "\"for everything is giving way, and when the grandmother cannot"
1448 "sleep, she lies trembling for fear at the noise, for she thinks"
1448 "that every minute the house will fall down on their heads; and"
1448 "everything now is dark for grandmother, and she does not think"
1448 "any one can make it light for her again, but you will be able"
1448 "to, I am sure, grandfather. Think how dreadful it is for her to"
1448 "be always in the dark, and then to be frightened at what may"
1448 "happen, and nobody can help her but you. To-morrow we must go and"
1448 "help her; we will, won't we, grandfather?\""
1448 ""
1448 "The child was clinging to the old man and looking up at him in"
1448 "trustful confidence. The grandfather looked down at Heidi for a"
1448 "while without speaking, and then said, \"Yes, Heidi, we will do"
1448 "something to stop the rattling, at least we can do that; we will"
1448 "go down about it to-morrow!\""
1448 ""
1448 "The child went skipping round the room for joy, crying out, \"We"
1448 "shall go to-morrow! we shall go to-morrow!\""
1448 ""
1448 "The grandfather kept his promise. On the following afternoon he"
1448 "brought the sleigh out again, and as on the previous day, he set"
1448 "Heidi down at the door of the grandmother's hut and said, \"Go in"
1448 "now, and when it grows dark, come out again.\" Then he put the"
1448 "sack in the sleigh and went round the house."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi had hardly opened the door and sprung into the room when"
1448 "the grandmother called out from her corner, \"It's the child"
1448 "again! here she comes!\" and in her delight she let the thread"
1448 "drop from her fingers, and the wheel stood still as she"
1448 "stretched out both her hands in welcome. Heidi ran to her, and"
1448 "then quickly drew the little stool close up to the old woman, and"
1448 "seating herself upon it, began to tell and ask her all kinds of"
1448 "things. All at once came the sound of heavy blows against the"
1448 "wall of the hut and the grandmother gave such a start of alarm"
1448 "that she nearly upset the spinning-wheel, and cried in a"
1448 "trembling voice, \"Ah, my God, now it is coming, the house is"
1448 "going to fall upon us!\" But Heidi caught her by the arm, and said"
1448 "soothingly, \"No, no, grandmother, do not be frightened, it is"
1448 "only grandfather with his hammer; he is mending up everything, so"
1448 "that you shan't have such fear and trouble.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Is it possible! is it really possible! so the dear God has not"
1448 "forgotten us!\" exclaimed the grandmother. \"Do you hear,"
1448 "Brigitta, what that noise is? Did you hear what the child says?"
