1448 "Now, as I listen, I can tell it is a hammer; go outside,"
1448 "Brigitta, and if it is Alm-Uncle, tell him he must come inside a"
1448 "moment that I may thank him.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Brigitta went outside and found Alm-Uncle in the act of"
1448 "fastening some heavy pieces of new wood along the wall. She"
1448 "stepped up to him and said, \"Good-evening, Uncle, mother and I"
1448 "have to thank you for doing us such a kind service, and she would"
1448 "like to tell you herself how grateful she is; I do not know who"
1448 "else would have done it for us; we shall not forget your"
1448 "kindness, for I am sure--\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"That will do,\" said the old man, interrupting her."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I know what you think of Alm-Uncle without your telling me. Go"
1448 "indoors again, I can find out for myself where the mending is"
1448 "wanted.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Brigitta obeyed on the spot, for Uncle had a way with him that"
1448 "made few people care to oppose his will. He went on knocking"
1448 "with his hammer all round the house, and then mounted the narrow"
1448 "steps to the roof, and hammered away there, until he had used up"
1448 "all the nails he had brought with him. Meanwhile it had been"
1448 "growing dark, and he had hardly come down from the roof and"
1448 "dragged the sleigh out from behind the goat-shed when Heidi"
1448 "appeared outside. The grandfather wrapped her up and took her in"
1448 "his arms as he had done the day before, for although he had to"
1448 "drag the sleigh up the mountain after him, he feared that if the"
1448 "child sat in it alone her wrappings would fall off and that she"
1448 "would be nearly if not quite frozen, so he carried her warm and"
1448 "safe in his arms."
1448 ""
1448 "So the winter went by. After many years of joyless life, the"
1448 "blind grandmother had at last found something to make her happy;"
1448 "her days were no longer passed in weariness and darkness, one"
1448 "like the other without pleasure or change, for now she had"
1448 "always something to which she could look forward. She listened"
1448 "for the little tripping footstep as soon as day had come, and"
1448 "when she heard the door open and knew the child was really there,"
1448 "she would call out, \"God be thanked, she has come again!\" And"
1448 "Heidi would sit by her and talk and tell her everything she knew"
1448 "in so lively a manner that the grandmother never noticed how the"
1448 "time went by, and never now as formerly asked Brigitta, \"Isn't"
1448 "the day done yet?\" but as the child shut the door behind her on"
1448 "leaving, would exclaim, \"How short the afternoon has seemed;"
1448 "don't you think so, Brigitta?\" And this one would answer, \"I do"
1448 "indeed; it seems as if I had only just cleared away the mid-day"
1448 "meal.\" And the grandmother would continue, \"Pray God the child is"
1448 "not taken from me, and that Alm-Uncle continues to let her come!"
1448 "Does she look well and strong, Brigitta?\" And the latter would"
1448 "answer, \"She looks as bright and rosy as an apple.\""
1448 ""
1448 "And Heidi had also grown very fond of the old grandmother, and"
1448 "when at last she knew for certain that no one could make it"
1448 "light for her again, she was overcome with sorrow; but the"
1448 "grandmother told her again that she felt the darkness much less"
1448 "when Heidi was with her, and so every fine winter's day the child"
1448 "came travelling down in her sleigh. The grandfather always took"
1448 "her, never raising any objection, indeed he always carried the"
1448 "hammer and sundry other things down in the sleigh with him, and"
1448 "many an afternoon was spent by him in making the goatherd's"
1448 "cottage sound and tight. It no longer groaned and rattled the"
1448 "whole night through, and the grandmother, who for many winters"
1448 "had not been able to sleep in peace as she did now, said she"
1448 "should never forget what the Uncle had done for her."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER V. TWO VISITS AND WHAT CAME OF THEM>"
1448 ""
1448 "Quickly the winter passed, and still more quickly the bright"
1448 "glad summer, and now another winter was drawing to its close."
1448 "Heidi was still as light-hearted and happy as the birds, and"
1448 "looked forward with more delight each day to the coming spring,"
1448 "when the warm south wind would roar through the fir trees and"
1448 "blow away the snow, and the warm sun would entice the blue and"
1448 "yellow flowers to show their heads, and the long days out on the"
1448 "mountain would come again, which seemed to Heidi the greatest"
1448 "joy that the earth could give. Heidi was now in her eighth year;"
1448 "she had learnt all kinds of useful things from her grandfather;"
1448 "she knew how to look after the goats as well as any one, and"
1448 "Little Swan and Bear would follow her like two faithful dogs, and"
1448 "give a loud bleat of pleasure when they heard her voice. Twice"
1448 "during the course of this last winter Peter had brought up a"
1448 "message from the schoolmaster at Dorfli, who sent word to Alm-"
1448 "Uncle that he ought to send Heidi to school, as she was over the"
1448 "usual age, and ought indeed to have gone the winter before. Uncle"
1448 "had sent word back each time that the schoolmaster would find him"
1448 "at home if he had anything he wished to say to him, but that he"
1448 "did not intend to send Heidi to school, and Peter had faithfully"
1448 "delivered his message."
1448 ""
1448 "When the March sun had melted the snow on the mountain side and"
1448 "the snowdrops were peeping out all over the valley, and the fir"
1448 "trees had shaken off their burden of snow and were again merrily"
1448 "waving their branches in the air, Heidi ran backwards and"
1448 "forwards with delight first to the goat-shed then to the fir-"
1448 "trees, and then to the hut-door, in order to let her grandfather"
1448 "know how much larger a piece of green there was under the trees,"
1448 "and then would run off to look again, for she could hardly wait"
1448 "till everything was green and the full beautiful summer had"
1448 "clothed the mountain with grass and flowers. As Heidi was thus"
1448 "running about one sunny March morning, and had just jumped over"
1448 "the water-trough for the tenth time at least, she nearly fell"
1448 "backwards into it with fright, for there in front of her, looking"
1448 "gravely at her, stood an old gentleman dressed in black. When he"
1448 "saw how startled she was, he said in a kind voice, \"Don't be"
1448 "afraid of me, for I am very fond of children. Shake hands! You"
1448 "must be the Heidi I have heard of; where is your grandfather?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"He is sitting by the table, making round wooden spoons,\" Heidi"
1448 "informed him, as she opened the door."
1448 ""
1448 "He was the old village pastor from Dorfli who had been a"
1448 "neighbor of Uncle's when he lived down there, and had known him"
1448 "well. He stepped inside the hut, and going up to the old man, who"
1448 "was bending over his work, said, \"Good-morning, neighbor.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The grandfather looked up in surprise, and then rising said,"
1448 "\"Good-morning\" in return. He pushed his chair towards the"
1448 "visitor as he continued, \"If you do not mind a wooden seat there"
1448 "is one for you.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The pastor sat down. \"It is a long time since I have seen you,"
1448 "neighbor,\" he said."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Or I you,\" was the answer."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I have come to-day to talk over something with you,\" continued"
1448 "the pastor. \"I think you know already what it is that has"
1448 "brought me here,\" and as he spoke he looked towards the child who"
1448 "was standing at the door, gazing with interest and surprise at"
1448 "the stranger."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Heidi, go off to the goats,\" said her grandfather. \"You take"
1448 "them a little salt and stay with them till I come.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi vanished on the spot."
1448 ""
1448 "\"The child ought to have been at school a year ago, and most"
1448 "certainly this last winter,\" said the pastor. \"The schoolmaster"
1448 "sent you word about it, but you gave him no answer. What are you"
1448 "thinking of doing with the child, neighbor?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I am thinking of not sending her to school,\" was the answer."
1448 ""
1448 "The visitor, surprised, looked across at the old man, who was"
1448 "sitting on his bench with his arms crossed and a determined"
1448 "expression about his whole person."
1448 ""
1448 "\"How are you going to let her grow up then?\" he asked."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I am going to let her grow up and be happy among the goats and"
1448 "birds; with them she is safe, and will learn nothing evil.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"But the child is not a goat or a bird, she is a human being. If"
1448 "she learns no evil from these comrades of hers, she will at the"
1448 "same time learn nothing; but she ought not to grow up in"
1448 "ignorance, and it is time she began her lessons. I have come now"
1448 "that you may have leisure to think over it, and to arrange about"
1448 "it during the summer. This is the last winter that she must be"
1448 "allowed to run wild; next winter she must come regularly to"
1448 "school every day.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"She will do no such thing,\" said the old man with calm"
1448 "determination."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Do you mean that by no persuasion can you be brought to see"
1448 "reason, and that you intend to stick obstinately to your"
1448 "decision?\" said the pastor, growing somewhat angry. \"You have"
1448 "been about the world, and must have seen and learnt much, and I"
1448 "should have given you credit for more sense, neighbor.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Indeed,\" replied the old man, and there was a tone in his voice"
1448 "that betrayed a growing irritation on his part too, \"and does"
1448 "the worthy pastor really mean that he would wish me next winter"
1448 "to send a young child like that some miles down the mountain on"
1448 "ice-cold mornings through storm and snow, and let her return at"
1448 "night when the wind is raging, when even one like ourselves"
1448 "would run a risk of being blown down by it and buried in the"
1448 "snow? And perhaps he may not have forgotten the child's mother,"
1448 "Adelaide? She was a sleep-walker, and had fits. Might not the"
1448 "child be attacked in the same way if obliged to over-exert"
1448 "herself? And some one thinks they can come and force me to send"
1448 "her? I will go before all the courts of justice in the country,"
1448 "and then we shall see who will force me to do it!\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"You are quite right, neighbor,\" said the pastor in a friendly"
1448 "tone of voice. \"I see it would have been impossible to send the"
1448 "child to school from here. But I perceive that the child is dear"
1448 "to you; for her sake do what you ought to have done long ago:"
1448 "come down into Dorfli and live again among your fellowmen. What"
1448 "sort of a life is this you lead, alone, and with bitter thoughts"
1448 "towards God and man! If anything were to happen to you up here"
1448 "who would there be to help you? I cannot think but what you must"
1448 "be half-frozen to death in this hut in the winter, and I do not"
1448 "know how the child lives through it!\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"The child has young blood in her veins and a good roof over her"
1448 "head, and let me further tell the pastor, that I know where wood"
1448 "is to be found, and when is the proper time to fetch it; the"
1448 "pastor can go and look inside my wood-shed; the fire is never"
1448 "out in my hut the whole winter through. As to going to live below"
1448 "that is far from my thoughts; the people despise me and I them;"
1448 "it is therefore best for all of us that we live apart.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"No, no, it is not best for you; I know what it is you lack,\""
1448 "said the pastor in an earnest voice. \"As to the people down"
1448 "there looking on you with dislike, it is not as bad as you think."
1448 "Believe me, neighbor; seek to make your peace with God, pray for"
1448 "forgiveness where you need it, and then come and see how"
1448 "differently people will look upon you, and how happy you may yet"
1448 "be.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The pastor had risen and stood holding out his hand to the old"
1448 "man as he added with renewed earnestness, \"I will wager,"
1448 "neighbor, that next winter you will be down among us again, and"
1448 "we shall be good neighbors as of old. I should be very grieved"
1448 "if any pressure had to be put upon you; give me your hand and"
1448 "promise me that you will come and live with us again and become"
1448 "reconciled to God and man.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Alm-Uncle gave the pastor his hand and answered him calmly and"
1448 "firmly, \"You mean well by me I know, but as to that which you"
1448 "wish me to do, I say now what I shall continue to say, that I"
1448 "will not send the child to school nor come and live among you.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Then God help you!\" said the pastor, and he turned sadly away"
1448 "and left the hut and went down the mountain."
1448 ""
1448 "Alm-Uncle was out of humor. When Heidi said as usual that"
1448 "afternoon, \"Can we go down to grandmother now?\" he answered,"
1448 "\"Not to-day.\" He did not speak again the whole of that day, and"
1448 "the following morning when Heidi again asked the same question,"
1448 "he replied, \"We will see.\" But before the dinner bowls had been"
1448 "cleared away another visitor arrived, and this time it was"
1448 "Cousin Dete. She had a fine feathered hat on her head, and a long"
1448 "trailing skirt to her dress which swept the floor, and on the"
1448 "floor of a goatherd's hut there are all sorts of things that do"
1448 "not belong to a dress."
1448 ""
1448 "The grandfather looked her up and down without uttering a word."
1448 "But Dete was prepared with an exceedingly amiable speech and"
1448 "began at once to praise the looks of the child. She was looking"
1448 "so well she should hardly have known her again, and it was"
1448 "evident that she had been happy and well-cared for with her"
1448 "grandfather; but she had never lost sight of the idea of taking"
1448 "the child back again, for she well understood that the little"
1448 "one must be much in his way, but she had not been able to do it"
1448 "at first. Day and night, however, she had thought over the means"
1448 "of placing the child somewhere, and that was why she had come to-"
1448 "day, for she had just heard of something that would be a lucky"
1448 "chance for Heidi beyond her most ambitious hopes. Some immensely"
1448 "wealthy relatives of the people she was serving, who had the"
1448 "most splendid house almost in Frankfurt, had an only daughter,"
1448 "young and an invalid, who was always obliged to go about in a"
1448 "wheeled chair; she was therefore very much alone and had no one"
1448 "to share her lessons, and so the little girl felt dull. Her"
1448 "father had spoken to Dete's mistress about finding a companion"
1448 "for her, and her mistress was anxious to help in the matter, as"
1448 "she felt so sympathetic about it. The lady-housekeeper had"
1448 "described the sort of child they wanted, simple-minded and"
1448 "unspoilt, and not like most of the children that one saw now-a-"
1448 "days. Dete had thought at once of Heidi and had gone off without"
1448 "delay to see the lady-housekeeper, and after Dete had given her a"
1448 "description of Heidi, she had immediately agreed to take her. And"
1448 "no one could tell what good fortune there might not be in store"
1448 "for Heidi, for if she was once with these people and they took a"
1448 "fancy to her, and anything happened to their own daughter--one"
1448 "could never tell, the child was so weakly--and they did not feel"
1448 "they could live without a child, why then the most unheard of"
1448 "luck--"
1448 ""
1448 "\"Have you nearly finished what you had to say?\" broke in Alm-"
1448 "Uncle, who had allowed her to talk on uninterruptedly so far."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Ugh!\" exclaimed Dete, throwing up her head in disgust, \"one"
1448 "would think I had been talking to you about the most ordinary"
1448 "matter; why there is not one person in all Prattigau who would"
1448 "not thank God if I were to bring them such a piece of news as I"
1448 "am bringing you.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"You may take your news to anybody you like, I will have nothing"
1448 "to do with it.\""
1448 ""
1448 "But now Dete leaped up from her seat like a rocket and cried,"
1448 "\"If that is all you have to say about it, why then I will give"
1448 "you a bit of my mind. The child is now eight years old and knows"
1448 "nothing, and you will not let her learn. You will not send her"
1448 "to church or school, as I was told down in Dorfli, and she is my"
1448 "own sister's child. I am responsible for what happens to her, and"
1448 "when there is such a good opening for a child, as this which"
1448 "offers for Heidi, only a person who cares for nobody and never"
1448 "wishes good to any one would think of not jumping at it. But I"
1448 "am not going to give in, and that I tell you; I have everybody in"
1448 "Dorfli on my side; there is not one person there who will not"
1448 "take my part against you; and I advise you to think well before"
1448 "bringing it into court, if that is your intention; there are"
1448 "certain things which might be brought up against you which you"
1448 "would not care to hear, for when one has to do with law-courts"
1448 "there is a great deal raked up that had been forgotten.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Be silent!\" thundered the Uncle, and his eyes flashed with"
1448 "anger. \"Go and be done with you! and never let me see you again"
1448 "with your hat and feather, and such words on your tongue as you"
1448 "come with today!\" And with that he strode out of the hut."
1448 ""
1448 "\"You have made grandfather angry,\" said Heidi, and her dark eyes"
1448 "had anything but a friendly expression in them as she looked at"
1448 "Dete."
1448 ""
1448 "\"He will soon be all right again; come now,\" said Dete"
1448 "hurriedly, \"and show me where your clothes are.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I am not coming,\" said Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Nonsense,\" continued Dete; then altering her tone to one half-"
1448 "coaxing, half-cross, \"Come, come, you do not understand any"
1448 "better than your grandfather; you will have all sorts of good"
1448 "things that you never dreamed of.\" Then she went to the cupboard"
1448 "and taking out Heidi's things rolled them up in a bundle. \"Come"
1448 "along now, there's your hat; it is very shabby but will do for"
1448 "the present; put it on and let us make haste off.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I am not coming,\" repeated Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Don't be so stupid and obstinate, like a goat; I suppose it's"
1448 "from the goats you have learnt to be so. Listen to me: you saw"
1448 "your grandfather was angry and heard what he said, that he did"
1448 "not wish to see us ever again; he wants you now to go away with"
1448 "me and you must not make him angrier still. You can't think how"
1448 "nice it is at Frankfurt, and what a lot of things you will see,"
1448 "and if you do not like it you can come back again; your"
1448 "grandfather will be in a good temper again by that time.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Can I return at once and be back home again here this evening?\""
1448 "asked Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What are you talking about, come along now! I tell you that you"
1448 "can come back here when you like. To-day we shall go as far as"
1448 "Mayenfeld, and early to-morrow we shall start in the train, and"
1448 "that will bring you home again in no time when you wish it, for"
1448 "it goes as fast as the wind.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Dete had now got the bundle under her arm and the child by the"
1448 "hand, and so they went down the mountain together."
1448 ""
1448 "As it was still too early in the year to take his goats out,"
1448 "Peter continued to go to school at Dorfli, but now and again he"
1448 "stole a holiday, for he could see no use in learning to read,"
1448 "while to wander about a bit and look for stout sticks which"
1448 "might be wanted some day he thought a far better employment. As"
1448 "Dete and Heidi neared the grandmother's hut they met Peter coming"
1448 "round the corner; he had evidently been well rewarded that day"
1448 "for his labors, for he was carrying an immense bundle of long"
1448 "thick hazel sticks on his shoulders. He stood still and stared"
1448 "at the two approaching figures; as they came up to him, he"
1448 "exclaimed, \"Where are you going, Heidi?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I am only just going over to Frankfurt for a little visit with"
1448 "Dete,\" she replied; \"but I must first run in to grandmother, she"
1448 "will be expecting me.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"No, no, you must not stop to talk; it is already too late,\""
1448 "said Dete, holding Heidi, who was struggling to get away, fast by"
1448 "the hand. \"You can go in when you come back, you must come along"
1448 "now,\" and she pulled the child on with her, fearing that if she"
1448 "let her go in Heidi might take it into her head again that she"
1448 "did not wish to come, and that the grandmother might stand by"
1448 "her. Peter ran into the hut and banged against the table with"
1448 "his bundle of sticks with such violence that everything in the"
1448 "room shook, and his grandmother leaped up with a cry of alarm"
1448 "from her spinning-wheel. Peter had felt that he must give vent to"
1448 "his feelings somehow."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What is the matter? What is the matter?\" cried the frightened"
1448 "old woman, while his mother, who had also started up from her"
1448 "seat at the shock, said in her usual patient manner, \"What is"
1448 "it, Peter? why do you behave so roughly?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Because she is taking Heidi away,\" explained Peter."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Who? who? where to, Peter, where to?\" asked the grandmother,"
1448 "growing still more agitated; but even as she spoke she guessed"
1448 "what had happened, for Brigitta had told her shortly before that"
1448 "she had seen Dete going up to Alm-Uncle. The old woman rose"
1448 "hastily and with trembling hands opened the window and called"
1448 "out beseechingly, \"Dete, Dete, do not take the child away from"
1448 "us! do not take her away!\""
1448 ""
1448 "The two who were hastening down the mountain heard her voice,"
1448 "and Dete evidently caught the words, for she grasped Heidi's hand"
1448 "more firmly. Heidi struggled to get free, crying, \"Grandmother"
1448 "is calling, I must go to her.\""
1448 ""
1448 "But Dete had no intention of letting the child go, and quieted"
1448 "her as best she could; they must make haste now, she said, or"
1448 "they would be too late and not able to go on the next day to"
1448 "Frankfurt, and there the child would see how delightful it was,"
1448 "and Dete was sure would not wish to go back when she was once"
1448 "there. But if Heidi wanted to return home she could do so at"
1448 "once, and then she could take something she liked back to"
1448 "grandmother. This was a new idea to Heidi, and it pleased her so"
1448 "much that Dete had no longer any difficulty in getting her"
1448 "along."
1448 ""
1448 "After a few minutes' silence, Heidi asked, \"What could I take"
1448 "back to her?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"We must think of something nice,\" answered Dete; \"a soft roll"
1448 "of white bread; she would enjoy that, for now she is old she can"
1448 "hardly eat the hard, black bread.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"No, she always gives it back to Peter, telling him it is too"
1448 "hard, for I have seen her do it myself,\" affirmed Heidi. \"Do let"
1448 "us make haste, for then perhaps we can get back soon from"
1448 "Frankfurt, and I shall be able to give her the white bread to-"
1448 "day.\" And Heidi started off running so fast that Dete with the"
1448 "bundle under her arm could scarcely keep up with her. But she"
1448 "was glad, nevertheless, to get along so quickly, for they were"
1448 "nearing Dorfli, where her friends would probably talk and"
1448 "question in a way that might put other ideas into Heidi's head."
1448 "So she went on straight ahead through the village, holding Heidi"
1448 "tightly by the hand, so that they might all see that it was on"
1448 "the child's account she was hurrying along at such a rate. To"
1448 "all their questions and remarks she made answer as she passed \"I"
1448 "can't stop now, as you see, I must make haste with the child as"
1448 "we have yet some way to go.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Are you taking her away?\" \"Is she running away from Alm-Uncle?\""
1448 "\"It's a wonder she is still alive!\" \"But what rosy cheeks she"
1448 "has!\" Such were the words which rang out on all sides, and Dete"
1448 "was thankful that she had not to stop and give any distinct"
1448 "answers to them, while Heidi hurried eagerly forward without"
1448 "saying a word."
1448 ""
1448 "From that day forward Alm-Uncle looked fiercer and more"
1448 "forbidding than ever when he came down and passed through"
1448 "Dorfli. He spoke to no one, and looked such an ogre as he came"
1448 "along with his pack of cheeses on his back, his immense stick in"
1448 "his hand, and his thick, frowning eyebrows, that the women would"
1448 "call to their little ones, \"Take care! get out of Alm-Uncle's way"
1448 "or he may hurt you!\""
1448 ""
1448 "The old man took no notice of anybody as he strode through the"
1448 "village on his way to the valley below, where he sold his"
1448 "cheeses and bought what bread and meat he wanted for himself."
1448 "After he had passed the villagers all crowded together looking"
1448 "after him, and each had something to say about him; how much"
1448 "wilder he looked than usual, how now he would not even respond to"
1448 "anybody's greeting, while they all agreed that it was a great"
1448 "mercy the child had got away from him, and had they not all"
1448 "noticed how the child had hurried along as if afraid that her"
1448 "grandfather might be following to take her back? Only the blind"
1448 "grandmother would have nothing to say against him, and told those"
1448 "who came to her to bring her work, or take away what she had"
1448 "spun, how kind and thoughtful he had been with the child, how"
1448 "good to her and her daughter, and how many afternoons he had"
1448 "spent mending the house which, but for his help, would certainly"
1448 "by this time have fallen down over their heads. And all this was"
1448 "repeated down in Dorfli; but most of the people who heard it said"
1448 "that grandmother was too old to understand, and very likely had"
1448 "not heard rightly what was said; as she was blind she was"
1448 "probably also deaf."
1448 ""
1448 "Alm-Uncle went no more now to the grandmother's house, and it"
1448 "was well that he had made it so safe, for it was not touched"
1448 "again for a long time. The days were sad again now for the old"
1448 "blind woman, and not one passed but what she would murmur"
1448 "complainingly, \"Alas! all our happiness and pleasure have gone"
1448 "with the child, and now the days are so long and dreary! Pray"
1448 "God, I see Heidi again once more before I die!\""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER VI. A NEW CHAPTER ABOUT NEW THINGS>"
1448 ""
1448 "In her home at Frankfurt, Clara, the little daughter of Herr"
1448 "Sesemann, was lying on the invalid couch on which she spent her"
1448 "whole day, being wheeled in it from room to room. Just now she"
1448 "was in what was known as the study, where, to judge by the"
1448 "various things standing and lying about, which added to the cosy"
1448 "appearance of the room, the family was fond of sitting. A"
1448 "handsome bookcase with glass doors explained why it was called"
1448 "the study, and here evidently the little girl was accustomed to"
1448 "have her lessons."
1448 ""
1448 "Clara's little face was thin and pale, and at this moment her"
1448 "two soft blue eyes were fixed on the clock, which seemed to her"
1448 "to go very slowly this day, and with a slight accent of"
1448 "impatience, which was very rare with her, she asked, \"Isn't it"
1448 "time yet, Fraulein Rottenmeier?\""
1448 ""
1448 "This lady was sitting very upright at a small work-table, busy"
1448 "with her embroidery. She had on a mysterious-looking loose"
1448 "garment, a large collar or shoulder-cape that gave a certain"
1448 "solemnity to her appearance, which was enhanced by a very lofty"
1448 "dome-shaped head dress. For many years past, since the mistress"
1448 "of the house had died, the housekeeping and the superintendence"
1448 "of the servants had been entrusted by Herr Sesemann to Fraulein"
1448 "Rottenmeier. He himself was often away from home, and he left"
1448 "her in sole charge, with the condition only that his little"
1448 "daughter should have a voice in all matters, and that nothing"
1448 "should be done against her wish."
1448 ""
1448 "As Clara was putting her impatient question for the second time,"
1448 "Dete and Heidi arrived at the front door, and the former"
1448 "inquired of the coachman, who had just got down from his box, if"
1448 "it was too late to see Fraulein Rottenmeier."
1448 ""
1448 "\"That's not my business,\" grumbled the coachman; \"ring the bell"
1448 "in the hall for Sebastian.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Dete did so, and Sebastian came downstairs; he looked astonished"
1448 "when he saw her, opening his eyes till they were nearly as big"
1448 "as the large round buttons on his coat."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Is it too late for me to see Fraulein Rottenmeier?\" Dete asked"
1448 "again."
1448 ""
1448 "\"That's not my business,\" answered the man; \"ring that other"
1448 "bell for the maid Tinette,\" and without troubling himself any"
1448 "farther Sebastian disappeared."
1448 ""
1448 "Dete rang again. This time Tinette appeared with a spotless"
1448 "white cap perched on the top of her head and a mocking expression"
1448 "of face."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What is it?\" she called from the top of the stairs. Dete"
1448 "repeated her question. Tinette disappeared, but soon came back"
1448 "and called down again to Dete, \"Come up, she is expecting you.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Dete and Heidi went upstairs and into the study, Tinette"
1448 "following. Dete remained standing politely near the door, still"
1448 "holding Heidi tightly by the hand, for she did not know what the"
1448 "child might take it into her head to do amid these new"
1448 "surroundings."
1448 ""
1448 "Fraulein Rottenmeier rose slowly and went up to the little new"
1448 "companion for the daughter of the house, to see what she was"
1448 "like. She did not seem very pleased with her appearance. Heidi"
1448 "was dressed in her plain little woollen frock, and her hat was"
1448 "an old straw one bent out of shape. The child looked innocently"
1448 "out from beneath it, gazing with unconcealed astonishment at the"
1448 "lady's towering head dress."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What is your name?\" asked Fraulein Rottenmeier, after"
1448 "scrutinisingly examining the child for some minutes, while Heidi"
1448 "in return kept her eyes steadily fixed upon the lady."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Heidi,\" she answered in a clear, ringing voice."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What? what? that's no Christian name for a child; you were not"
1448 "christened that. What name did they give you when you were"
1448 "baptized?\" continued Fraulein Rottenmeier."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I do not remember,\" replied Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What a way to answer!\" said the lady, shaking her head. \"Dete,"
1448 "is the child a simpleton or only saucy?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"If the lady will allow me, I will speak for the child, for she"
1448 "is very unaccustomed to strangers,\" said Dete, who had given"
1448 "Heidi a silent poke for making such an unsuitable answer. \"She"
1448 "is certainly not stupid nor yet saucy, she does not know what it"
1448 "means even; she speaks exactly as she thinks. To-day she is for"
1448 "the first time in a gentleman's house and she does not know good"
1448 "manners; but she is docile and very willing to learn, if the"
1448 "lady will kindly make excuses for her. She was christened"
1448 "Adelaide, after her mother, my sister, who is now dead.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well, that's a name that one can pronounce,\" remarked Fraulein"
1448 "Rottenmeier. \"But I must tell you, Dete, that I am astonished to"
1448 "see so young a child. I told you that I wanted a companion of"
1448 "the same age as the young lady of the house, one who could share"
1448 "her lessons, and all her other occupations. Fraulein Clara is now"
1448 "over twelve; what age is this child?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"If the lady will allow me,\" began Dete again, in her usual"
1448 "fluent manner, \"I myself had lost count of her exact age; she is"
1448 "certainly a little younger, but not much; I cannot say"
1448 "precisely, but I think she is ten, or thereabouts.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Grandfather told me I was eight,\" put in Heidi. Dete gave her"
1448 "another poke, but as the child had not the least idea why she"
1448 "did so she was not at all confused."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What--only eight!\" cried Fraulein Rottenmeier angrily. \"Four"
1448 "years too young! Of what use is such a child! And what have you"
1448 "learnt? What books did you have to learn from?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"None,\" said Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "\"How? what? How then did you learn to read?\" continued the lady."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I have never learnt to read, or Peter either,\" Heidi informed"
1448 "her."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Mercy upon us! you do not know how to read! Is it really so?\""
1448 "exclaimed Fraulein Rottenmeier, greatly horrified. \"Is it"
1448 "possible--not able to read? What have you learnt then?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Nothing,\" said Heidi with unflinching truthfulness."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Young woman,\" said the lady to Dete, after having paused for a"
1448 "minute or two to recover from her shock, \"this is not at all the"
1448 "sort of companion you led me to suppose; how could you think of"
1448 "bringing me a child like this?\""
1448 ""
1448 "But Dete was not to be put down so easily, and answered warmly,"
1448 "\"If the lady will allow me, the child is exactly what I thought"
1448 "she required; the lady described what she wished for, a child"
1448 "unlike all other children, and I could find no other to suit,"
1448 "for the greater number I know are not peculiar, but one very much"
1448 "the same as the other, and I thought this child seemed as if made"
1448 "for the place. But I must go now, for my mistress will be waiting"
1448 "for me; if the lady will permit I will come again soon and see"
1448 "how she is getting on.\" And with a bow Dete quickly left the room"
1448 "and ran downstairs. Fraulein Rottenmeier stood for a moment taken"
1448 "aback and then ran after Dete. If the child was to stop she had"
1448 "many things yet to say and ask about her, and there the child"
1448 "was, and what was more, Dete, as she plainly saw, meant to leave"
1448 "her there."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi remained by the door where she had been standing since she"
1448 "first came in. Clara had looked on during the interview without"
1448 "speaking; now she beckoned to Heidi and said, \"Come here!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi went up to her."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Would you rather be called Heidi or Adelaide?\" asked Clara."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I am never called anything but Heidi,\" was the child's prompt"
1448 "answer."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Then I shall always call you by that name,\" said Clara, \"it"
1448 "suits you. I have never heard it before, but neither have I ever"
1448 "seen a child like you before. Have you always had that short"
1448 "curly hair?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, I think so,\" said Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Are you pleased to come to Frankfurt?\" went on Clara."
1448 ""
1448 "\"No, but I shall go home to-morrow and take grandmother a white"
1448 "loaf,\" explained Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well, you are a funny child!\" exclaimed Clara. \"You were"
1448 "expressly sent for to come here and to remain with me and share"
1448 "my lessons; there will be some fun about them now as you cannot"
1448 "read, something new to do, for often they are dreadfully dull,"
1448 "and I think the morning will never pass away. You know my tutor"
1448 "comes every morning at about ten o'clock, and then we go on with"
1448 "lessons till two, and it does seem such a long time. Sometimes"
1448 "he takes up the book and holds it close up to his face, as if he"
1448 "was very short-sighted, but I know it's only because he wants so"
1448 "dreadfully to gape, and Fraulein Rottenmeier takes her large"
1448 "handkerchief out also now and then and covers her face with it,"
1448 "as if she was moved by what we had been reading, but that is"
1448 "only because she is longing to gape too. And I myself often want"
1448 "to gape, but I am obliged to stop myself, for if Fraulein"
1448 "Rottenmeier sees me gaping she runs off at once and fetches the"
1448 "cod-liver oil and says I must have a dose, as I am getting weak"
1448 "again, and the cod-liver oil is horrible, so I do my best not to"
1448 "gape. But now it will be much more amusing, for I shall be able"
1448 "to lie and listen while you learn to read.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi shook her head doubtfully when she heard of learning to"
1448 "read."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh, nonsense, Heidi, of course you must learn to read,"
1448 "everybody must, and my tutor is very kind, and never cross, and"
1448 "he will explain everything to you. But mind, when he explains"
1448 "anything to you, you won't be able to understand; but don't ask"
1448 "any questions, or else he will go on explaining and you will"
1448 "understand less than ever. Later when you have learnt more and"
1448 "know about things yourself, then you will begin to understand"
1448 "what he meant.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Fraulein Rottenmeier now came back into the room; she had not"
1448 "been able to overtake Dete, and was evidently very much put out;"
1448 "for she had wanted to go into more details concerning the child,"
1448 "and to convince Dete how misleading she had been, and how unfit"
1448 "Heidi was as a companion for Clara; she really did not know what"
1448 "to be about, or how to undo the mischief, and it made her all"
1448 "the more angry that she herself was responsible for it, having"
1448 "consented to Heidi being fetched. She ran backwards and forwards"
1448 "in a state of agitation between the study and the dining-room,"
1448 "and then began scolding Sebastian, who was standing looking at"
1448 "the table he had just finished laying to see that nothing was"
1448 "missing."
1448 ""
1448 "\"You can finish your thoughts to-morrow morning; make haste, or"
1448 "we shall get no dinner to-day at all.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Then hurrying out she called Tinette, but in such an ill-"
1448 "tempered voice that the maid came tripping forward with even more"
1448 "mincing steps than usual, but she looked so pert that even"
1448 "Fraulein Rottenmeier did not venture to scold her, which only"
1448 "made her suppressed anger the greater."
1448 ""
1448 "\"See that the room is prepared for the little girl who has just"
1448 "arrived,\" said the lady, with a violent effort at self-control."
1448 "\"Everything is ready; it only wants dusting.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"It's worth my troubling about,\" said Tinette mockingly as she"
1448 "turned away."
1448 ""
1448 "Meanwhile Sebastian had flung open the folding doors leading"
1448 "into the dining-room with rather more noise than he need, for he"
1448 "was feeling furious, although he did not dare answer back when"
1448 "Fraulein Rottenmeier spoke to him; he then went up to Clara's"
1448 "chair to wheel her into the next room. As he was arranging the"
1448 "handle at the back preparatory to doing so, Heidi went near and"
1448 "stood staring at him. Seeing her eyes fixed upon him, he"
1448 "suddenly growled out, \"Well, what is there in me to stare at like"
1448 "that?\" which he would certainly not have done if he had been"
1448 "aware that Fraulein Rottenmeier was just then entering the room."
1448 "\"You look so like Peter,\" answered Heidi. The lady-housekeeper"
1448 "clasped her hands in horror. \"Is it possible!\" she stammered half-"
1448 "aloud, \"she is now addressing the servant as if he were a friend!"
1448 "I never could have imagined such a child!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Sebastian wheeled the couch into the dining-room and helped"
1448 "Clara on to her chair. Fraulein Rottenmeier took the seat beside"
1448 "her and made a sign to Heidi to take the one opposite. They were"
1448 "the only three at table, and as they sat far apart there was"
1448 "plenty of room for Sebastian to hand his dishes. Beside Heidi's"
1448 "plate lay a nice white roll, and her eyes lighted up with"
1448 "pleasure as she saw it. The resemblance which Heidi had noticed"
1448 "had evidently awakened in her a feeling of confidence towards"
1448 "Sebastian, for she sat as still as a mouse and without moving"
1448 "until he came up to her side and handed her the dish of fish;"
1448 "then she looked at the roll and asked, \"Can I have it?\" Sebastian"
1448 "nodded, throwing a side glance at Fraulein Rottenmeier to see"
1448 "what effect this request would have upon her. Heidi immediately"
1448 "seized the roll and put it in her pocket. Sebastian's face became"
1448 "convulsed, he was overcome with inward laughter but knew his"
1448 "place too well to laugh aloud. Mute and motionless he still"
1448 "remained standing beside Heidi; it was not his duty to speak, nor"
1448 "to move away until she had helped herself. Heidi looked"
1448 "wonderingly at him for a minute or two, and then said, \"Am I to"
1448 "eat some of that too?\" Sebastian nodded again. \"Give me some"
1448 "then,\" she said, looking calmly at her plate. At this Sebastian's"
1448 "command of his countenance became doubtful, and the dish began to"
1448 "tremble suspiciously in his hands."
1448 ""
1448 "\"You can put the dish on the table and come back presently,\""
1448 "said Fraulein Rottenmeier with a severe expression of face."
1448 "Sebastian disappeared on the spot. \"As for you, Adelaide, I see I"
1448 "shall have to teach you the first rules of behavior,\" continued"
1448 "the lady-housekeeper with a sigh. \"I will begin by explaining to"
1448 "you how you are to conduct yourself at table,\" and she went on to"
1448 "give Heidi minute instructions as to all she was to do. \"And"
1448 "now,\" she continued, \"I must make you particularly understand"
1448 "that you are not to speak to Sebastian at table, or at any other"
1448 "time, unless you have an order to give him, or a necessary"
1448 "question to put to him; and then you are not to address him as"
1448 "if he was some one belonging to you. Never let me hear you speak"
1448 "to him in that way again! It is the same with Tinette, and for"
1448 "myself you are to address me as you hear others doing. Clara"
1448 "must herself decide what you are to call her.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Why, Clara, of course,\" put the latter. Then followed a long"
1448 "list of rules as to general behavior, getting up and going to"
1448 "bed, going in and out of the room, shutting the doors, keeping"
1448 "everything tidy, during the course of which Heidi's eyes"
1448 "gradually closed, for she had been up before five o'clock that"
1448 "morning and had had a long journey. She leant back in her chair"
1448 "and fell fast asleep. Fraulein Rottenmeier having at last come"
1448 "to the end of her sermonizing said, \"Now remember what I have"
1448 "said, Adelaide! Have you understood it all?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Heidi has been asleep for ever so long,\" said Clara, her face"
1448 "rippling all over with amusement, for she had not had such an"
1448 "entertaining dinner for a long time."
1448 ""
1448 "\"It is really insupportable what one has to go through with this"
1448 "child,\" exclaimed Fraulein Rottenmeier, in great indignation,"
1448 "and she rang the bell so violently that Tinette and Sebastian"
1448 "both came running in and nearly tumbling over one another; but no"
1448 "noise was sufficient to wake Heidi, and it was with difficulty"
1448 "they could rouse her sufficiently to get her along to her"
1448 "bedroom, to reach which she had to pass first through the study,"
1448 "then through Clara's bedroom, then through Fraulein Rottenmeier's"
1448 "sitting-room, till she came to the corner room that had been set"
1448 "apart for her."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER VII. FRAULEIN ROTTENMEIER SPENDS AN UNCOMFORTABLE DAY>"
1448 ""
1448 "When Heidi opened her eyes on her first morning in Frankfurt she"
1448 "could not think where she was. Then she rubbed them and looked"
1448 "about her. She was sitting up in a high white bed, on one side"
1448 "of a large, wide room, into which the light was falling through"
1448 "very, very long white curtains; near the window stood two chairs"
1448 "covered with large flowers, and then came a sofa with the same"
1448 "flowers, in front of which was a round table; in the corner was"
1448 "a washstand, with things upon it that Heidi had never seen in her"
1448 "life before. But now all at once she remembered that she was in"
1448 "Frankfurt; everything that had happened the day before came back"
1448 "to her, and finally she recalled clearly the instructions that"
1448 "had been given her by the lady-housekeeper, as far as she had"
1448 "heard them. Heidi jumped out of bed and dressed herself; then"
1448 "she ran first to one window and then another; she wanted to see"
1448 "the sky and country outside; she felt like a bird in a cage"
1448 "behind those great curtains. But they were too heavy for her to"
1448 "put aside, so she crept underneath them to get to the window. But"
1448 "these again were so high that she could only just get her head"
1448 "above the sill to peer out. Even then she could not see what she"
1448 "longed for. In vain she went first to one and then the other of"
1448 "the windows--she could see nothing but walls and windows and"
1448 "again walls and windows. Heidi felt quite frightened. It was"
1448 "still early, for Heidi was accustomed to get up early and run"
1448 "out at once to see how everything was looking, if the sky was"
1448 "blue and if the sun was already above the mountains, or if the"
1448 "fir trees were waving and the flowers had opened their eyes. As a"
1448 "bird, when it first finds itself in its bright new cage, darts"
1448 "hither and thither, trying the bars in turn to see if it cannot"
1448 "get through them and fly again into the open, so Heidi continued"
1448 "to run backwards and forwards, trying to open first one and then"
1448 "the other of the windows, for she felt she could not bear to see"
1448 "nothing but walls and windows, and somewhere outside there must"
1448 "be the green grass, and the last unmelted snows on the mountain"
1448 "slopes, which Heidi so longed to see. But the windows remained"
1448 "immovable, try what Heidi would to open them, even endeavoring"
1448 "to push her little fingers under them to lift them up; but it was"
1448 "all no use. When after a while Heidi saw that her efforts were"
1448 "fruitless, she gave up trying, and began to think whether she"
1448 "would not go out and round the house till she came to the grass,"
1448 "but then she remembered that the night before she had only seen"
1448 "stones in front of the house. At that moment a knock came to the"
1448 "door, and immediately after Tinette put her head inside and"
1448 "said, \"Breakfast is ready.\" Heidi had no idea what an invitation"
1448 "so worded meant, and Tinette's face did not encourage any"
1448 "questioning on Heidi's part, but rather the reverse. Heidi was"
1448 "sharp enough to read its expression, and acted accordingly. So"
1448 "she drew the little stool out from under the table, put it in"
1448 "the corner and sat down upon it, and there silently awaited what"
1448 "would happen next. Shortly after, with a good deal of rustling"
1448 "and bustling Fraulein Rottenmeier appeared, who again seemed"
1448 "very much put out and called to Heidi, \"What is the matter with"
1448 "you, Adelheid? Don't you understand what breakfast is? Come along"
1448 "at once!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi had no difficulty in understanding now and followed at"
1448 "once. Clara had been some time at the breakfast table and she"
1448 "gave Heidi a kindly greeting, her face looking considerably more"
1448 "cheerful than usual, for she looked forward to all kinds of new"
1448 "things happening again that day. Breakfast passed off quietly;"
1448 "Heidi ate her bread and butter in a perfectly correct manner,"
1448 "and when the meal was over and Clara wheeled back into the study,"
1448 "Fraulein Rottenmeier told her to follow and remain with Clara"
1448 "until the tutor should arrive and lessons begin."
1448 ""
1448 "As soon as the children were alone again, Heidi asked, \"How can"
1448 "one see out from here, and look right down on to the ground?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"You must open the window and look out,\" replied Clara amused."
1448 ""
1448 "\"But the windows won't open,\" responded Heidi sadly."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, they will,\" Clara assured her. \"You cannot open them, nor"
1448 "I either, but when you see Sebastian you can ask him to open"
1448 "one.\""
1448 ""
1448 "It was a great relief to Heidi to know that the windows could be"
1448 "opened and that one could look out, for she still felt as if she"
1448 "was shut up in prison. Clara now began to ask her questions"
1448 "about her home, and Heidi was delighted to tell her all about the"
1448 "mountain and the goats, and the flowery meadows which were so"
1448 "dear to her."
1448 ""
1448 "Meanwhile her tutor had arrived; Fraulein Rottenmeier, however,"
1448 "did not bring him straight into the study but drew him first"
1448 "aside into the dining-room, where she poured forth her troubles"
1448 "and explained to him the awkward position in which she was"
1448 "placed, and how it had all come about. It appeared that she had"
1448 "written some time back to Herr Sesemann to tell him that his"
1448 "daughter very much wished to have a companion, and had added how"
1448 "desirable she thought it herself, as it would be a spur to Clara"
1448 "at her lessons and an amusement for her in her playtime."
1448 "Fraulein Rottenmeier had privately wished for this arrangement on"
1448 "her own behalf, as it would relieve her from having always to"
1448 "entertain the sick girl herself, which she felt at times was too"
1448 "much for her. The father had answered that he was quite willing"
1448 "to let his daughter have a companion, provided she was treated in"
1448 "every way like his own child, as he would not have any child"
1448 "tormented or put upon, \"which was a very unnecessary remark,\" put"
1448 "in Fraulein Rottenmeier, \"for who wants to torment children!\" But"
1448 "now she went on to explain how dreadfully she had been taken in"
1448 "about the child, and related all the unimaginable things of which"
1448 "she had already been guilty, so that not only would he have to"
1448 "begin with teaching her the A B C, but would have to start with"
1448 "the most rudimentary instruction as regarded everything to do"
1448 "with daily life. She could see only one way out of this"
1448 "disastrous state of affairs, and that was for the tutor to"
1448 "declare that it was impossible for the two to learn together"
1448 "without detriment to Clara, who was so far ahead of the other;"
1448 "that would be a valid excuse for getting rid of the child, and"
1448 "Herr Sesemann would be sure to agree to the child being sent home"
1448 "again, but she dared not do this without his order, since he was"
1448 "aware that by this time the companion had arrived. But the tutor"
1448 "was a cautious man and not inclined to take a partial view of"
1448 "matters. He tried to calm Fraulein Rottenmeier, and gave it as"
1448 "his opinion that if the little girl was backward in some things"
1448 "she was probably advanced in others, and a little regular"
1448 "teaching would soon set the balance right. When Fraulein"
1448 "Rottenmeier saw that he was not ready to support her, and"
1448 "evidently quite ready to undertake teaching the alphabet, she"
1448 "opened the study door, which she quickly shut again as soon as he"
1448 "had gone through, remaining on the other side herself, for she"
1448 "had a perfect horror of the A B C. She walked up and down the"
1448 "dining-room, thinking over in her own mind how the servants were"
1448 "to be told to address Adelaide. The father had written that she"
1448 "was to be treated exactly like his own daughter, and this would"
1448 "especially refer, she imagined, to the servants. She was not"
1448 "allowed, however, a very long interval of time for consideration,"
1448 "for suddenly the sound of a frightful crash was heard in the"
1448 "study, followed by frantic cries for Sebastian. She rushed into"
1448 "the room. There on the floor lay in a confused heap, books,"
1448 "exercise-books, inkstand, and other articles with the table-cloth"
1448 "on the top, while from beneath them a dark stream of ink was"
1448 "flowing all across the floor. Heidi had disappeared."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Here's a state of things!\" exclaimed Fraulein Rottenmeier,"
1448 "wringing her hands. \"Table-cloth, books, work-basket, everything"
1448 "lying in the ink! It was that unfortunate child, I suppose!\""
1448 ""
1448 "The tutor was standing looking down at the havoc in distress;"
1448 "there was certainly only one view to be taken of such a matter"
1448 "as this and that an unfavorable one. Clara meanwhile appeared to"
1448 "find pleasure in such an unusual event and in watching the"
1448 "results. \"Yes, Heidi did it,\" she explained, \"but quite by"
1448 "accident; she must on no account be punished; she jumped up in"
1448 "such violent haste to get away that she dragged the tablecloth"
1448 "along with her, and so everything went over. There were a number"
1448 "of vehicles passing, that is why she rushed off like that;"
1448 "perhaps she has never seen a carriage.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Is it not as I said? She has not the smallest notion about"

1448 "listen while her lessons are going on. But where is the child"
1448 "who has caused all this trouble? Surely she has not run away!"
1448 "What would Herr Sesemann say to me?\" She ran out of the room and"
1448 "down the stairs. There, at the bottom, standing in the open door-"
1448 "way, was Heidi, looking in amazement up and down the street."
1448 ""

1448 "that?\" called Fraulein Rottenmeier."
1448 ""

1448 "passing carriages had reached her, and which to Heidi had seemed"

1448 ""

1448 ""

1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER VIII. THERE IS GREAT COMMOTION IN THE LARGE HOUSE>"
1448 ""
1448 "Sebastian had just shown the tutor into the study on the"
1448 "following morning when there came another and very loud ring at"
1448 "the bell, which Sebastian ran quickly to answer. \"Only Herr"
1448 "Sesemann rings like that,\" he said to himself; \"he must have"
1448 "returned home unexpectedly.\" He pulled open the door, and there"
1448 "in front of him he saw a ragged little boy carrying a hand-organ"
1448 "on his back."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What's the meaning of this?\" said Sebastian angrily. \"I'll"
1448 "teach you to ring bells like that! What do you want here?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I want to see Clara,\" the boy answered."
1448 ""
1448 "\"You dirty, good-for-nothing little rascal, can't you be polite"
1448 "enough to say 'Miss Clara'? What do you want with her?\""
1448 "continued Sebastian roughly. \"She owes me fourpence,\" explained"
1448 "the boy."
1448 ""
1448 "\"You must be out of your mind! And how do you know that any"
1448 "young lady of that name lives here?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"She owes me twopence for showing her the way there, and"
1448 "twopence for showing her the way back.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"See what a pack of lies you are telling! The young lady never"
1448 "goes out, cannot even walk; be off and get back to where you"
1448 "came from, before I have to help you along.\""
1448 ""
1448 "But the boy was not to be frightened away; he remained standing,"
1448 "and said in a determined voice, \"But I saw her in the street,"
1448 "and can describe her to you; she has short, curly black hair, and"
1448 "black eyes, and wears a brown dress, and does not talk quite"
1448 "like we do.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oho!\" thought Sebastian, laughing to himself, \"the little miss"
1448 "has evidently been up to more mischief.\" Then, drawing the boy"
1448 "inside he said aloud, \"I understand now, come with me and wait"
1448 "outside the door till I tell you to go in. Be sure you begin"
1448 "playing your organ the instant you get inside the room; the lady"
1448 "is very fond of music.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Sebastian knocked at the study door, and a voice said, \"Come"
1448 "in.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"There is a boy outside who says he must speak to Miss Clara"
1448 "herself,\" Sebastian announced."
1448 ""
1448 "Clara was delighted at such an extraordinary and unexpected"
1448 "message."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Let him come in at once,\" replied Clara; \"he must come in, must"
1448 "he not,\" she added, turning to her tutor, \"if he wishes so"
1448 "particularly to see me?\""
1448 ""
1448 "The boy was already inside the room, and according to"
1448 "Sebastian's directions immediately began to play his organ."
1448 "Fraulein Rottenmeier, wishing to escape the A B C, had retired"
1448 "with her work to the dining-room. All at once she stopped and"
1448 "listened. Did those sounds come up from the street? And yet they"
1448 "seemed so near! But how could there be an organ playing in the"
1448 "study? And yet--it surely was so. She rushed to the other end of"
1448 "the long dining-room and tore open the door. She could hardly"
1448 "believe her eyes. There, in the middle of the study, stood a"
1448 "ragged boy turning away at his organ in the most energetic"
1448 "manner. The tutor appeared to be making efforts to speak, but his"
1448 "voice could not be heard. Both children were listening"
1448 "delightedly to the music."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Leave off! leave off at once!\" screamed Fraulein Rottenmeier."
1448 "But her voice was drowned by the music. She was making a dash"
1448 "for the boy, when she saw something on the ground crawling"
1448 "towards her feet--a dreadful dark object--a tortoise. At this"
1448 "sight she jumped higher than she had for many long years before,"
1448 "shrieking with all her might, \"Sebastian! Sebastian!\""
1448 ""
1448 "The organ-player suddenly stopped, for this time her voice had"
1448 "risen louder than the music. Sebastian was standing outside bent"
1448 "double with laughter, for he had been peeping to see what was"
1448 "going on. By the time he entered the room Fraulein Rottenmeier"
1448 "had sunk into a chair."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Take them all out, boy and animal! Get them away at once!\" she"
1448 "commanded him."
1448 ""
1448 "Sebastian pulled the boy away, the latter having quickly caught"
1448 "up the tortoise, and when he had got him outside he put"
1448 "something into his hand. \"There is the fourpence from Miss Clara,"
1448 "and another fourpence for the music. You did it all quite right!\""
1448 "and with that he shut the front door upon him."
1448 ""
1448 "Quietness reigned again in the study, and lessons began once"
1448 "more; Fraulein Rottenmeier now took up her station in the study"
1448 "in order by her presence to prevent any further dreadful goings-"
1448 "on."
1448 ""
1448 "But soon another knock came to the door, and Sebastian again"
1448 "stepped in, this time to say that some one had brought a large"
1448 "basket with orders that it was to be given at once to Miss"
1448 "Clara."
1448 ""
1448 "\"For me?\" said Clara in astonishment, her curiosity very much"
1448 "excited, \"bring it in at once that I may see what it is like.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Sebastian carried in a large covered basket and retired."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I think the lessons had better be finished first before the"
1448 "basket is unpacked,\" said Fraulein Rottenmeier."
1448 ""
1448 "Clara could not conceive what was in it, and cast longing"
1448 "glances towards it. In the middle of one of her declensions she"
1448 "suddenly broke off and said to the tutor, \"Mayn't I just give one"
1448 "peep inside to see what is in it before I go on?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"On some considerations I am for it, on others against it,\" he"
1448 "began in answer; \"for it, on the ground that if your whole"
1448 "attention is directed to the basket--\" but the speech remained"
1448 "unfinished. The cover of the basket was loose, and at this"
1448 "moment one, two, three, and then two more, and again more kittens"
1448 "came suddenly tumbling on to the floor and racing about the room"
1448 "in every direction, and with such indescribable rapidity that it"
1448 "seemed as if the whole room was full of them. They jumped over"
1448 "the tutor's boots, bit at his trousers, climbed up Fraulein"
1448 "Rottenmeier's dress, rolled about her feet, sprang up on to"
1448 "Clara's couch, scratching, scrambling, and mewing: it was a sad"
1448 "scene of confusion. Clara, meanwhile, pleased with their"
1448 "gambols, kept on exclaiming, \"Oh, the dear little things! how"
1448 "pretty they are! Look, Heidi, at this one; look, look, at that"
1448 "one over there!\" And Heidi in her delight kept running after them"
1448 "first into one corner and then into the other. The tutor stood up"
1448 "by the table not knowing what to do, lifting first his right foot"
1448 "and then his left to get it away from the scrambling, scratching"
1448 "kittens. Fraulein Rottenmeier was unable at first to speak at"
1448 "all, so overcome was she with horror, and she did not dare rise"
1448 "from her chair for fear that all the dreadful little animals"
1448 "should jump upon her at once. At last she found voice to call"
1448 "loudly, \"Tinette! Tinette! Sebastian! Sebastian!\""
1448 ""
1448 "They came in answer to her summons and gathered up the kittens,"
1448 "by degrees they got them all inside the basket again and then"
1448 "carried them off to put with the other two."
1448 ""
1448 "To-day again there had been no opportunity for gaping. Late that"
1448 "evening, when Fraulein Rottenmeier had somewhat recovered from"
1448 "the excitement of the morning, she sent for the two servants,"
1448 "and examined them closely concerning the events of the morning."
1448 "And then it came out that Heidi was at the bottom of them,"
1448 "everything being the result of her excursion of the day before."
1448 "Fraulein Rottenmeier sat pale with indignation and did not know"
1448 "at first how to express her anger. Then she made a sign to"
1448 "Tinette and Sebastian to withdraw, and turning to Heidi, who was"
1448 "standing by Clara's couch, quite unable to understand of what sin"
1448 "she had been guilty, began in a severe voice,--"
1448 ""
1448 "\"Adelaide, I know of only one punishment which will perhaps make"
1448 "you alive to your ill conduct, for you are an utter little"
1448 "barbarian, but we will see if we cannot tame you so that you"
1448 "shall not be guilty of such deeds again, by putting you in a"
1448 "dark cellar with the rats and black beetles.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi listened in silence and surprise to her sentence, for she"
1448 "had never seen a cellar such as was now described; the place"
1448 "known at her grandfather's as the cellar, where the fresh made"
1448 "cheeses and the new milk were kept, was a pleasant and inviting"
1448 "place; neither did she know at all what rats and black beetles"
1448 "were like."
1448 ""
1448 "But now Clara interrupted in great distress. \"No, no, Fraulein"
1448 "Rottenmeier, you must wait till papa comes; he has written to"
1448 "say that he will soon be home, and then I will tell him"
1448 "everything, and he will say what is to be done with Heidi.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Fraulein Rottenmeier could not do anything against this superior"
1448 "authority, especially as the father was really expected very"
1448 "shortly. She rose and said with some displeasure, \"As you will,"
1448 "Clara, but I too shall have something to say to Herr Sesemann.\""
1448 "And with that she left the room."
1448 ""
1448 "Two days now went by without further disturbance. Fraulein"
1448 "Rottenmeier, however, could not recover her equanimity; she was"
1448 "perpetually reminded by Heidi's presence of the deception that"
1448 "had been played upon her, and it seemed to her that ever since"
1448 "the child had come into the house everything had been topsy-"
1448 "turvy, and she could not bring things into proper order again."
1448 "Clara had grown much more cheerful; she no longer found time hang"
1448 "heavy during the lesson hours, for Heidi was continually making a"
1448 "diversion of some kind or other. She jumbled all her letters up"
1448 "together and seemed quite unable to learn them, and when the"
1448 "tutor tried to draw her attention to their different shapes, and"
1448 "to help her by showing her that this was like a little horn, or"
1448 "that like a bird's bill, she would suddenly exclaim in a joyful"
1448 "voice, \"That is a goat!\" \"That is a bird of prey!\" For the"
1448 "tutor's descriptions suggested all kinds of pictures to her mind,"
1448 "but left her still incapable of the alphabet. In the later"
1448 "afternoons Heidi always sat with Clara, and then she would give"
1448 "the latter many and long descriptions of the mountain and of her"
1448 "life upon it, and the burning longing to return would become so"
1448 "overpowering that she always finished with the words, \"Now I must"
1448 "go home! to-morrow I must really go!\" But Clara would try to"
1448 "quiet her, and tell Heidi that she must wait till her father"
1448 "returned, and then they would see what was to be done. And if"
1448 "Heidi gave in each time and seemed quickly to regain her good"
1448 "spirits, it was because of a secret delight she had in the"
1448 "thought that every day added two more white rolls to the number"
1448 "she was collecting for grandmother; for she always pocketed the"
1448 "roll placed beside her plate at dinner and supper, feeling that"
1448 "she could not bear to eat them, knowing that grandmother had no"
1448 "white bread and could hardly eat the black bread which was so"
1448 "hard. After dinner Heidi had to sit alone in her room for a"
1448 "couple of hours, for she understood now that she might not run"
1448 "about outside at Frankfurt as she did on the mountain, and so she"
1448 "did not attempt it. Any conversation with Sebastian in the dining-"
1448 "room was also forbidden her, and as to Tinette, she kept out of"
1448 "her way, and never thought of speaking to her, for Heidi was"
1448 "quite aware that the maid looked scornfully at her and always"
1448 "spoke to her in a mocking voice. So Heidi had plenty of time from"
1448 "day to day to sit and picture how everything at home was now"
1448 "turning green, and how the yellow flowers were shining in the"
1448 "sun, and how all around lay bright in the warm sunshine, the snow"
1448 "and the rocks, and the whole wide valley, and Heidi at times"
1448 "could hardly contain herself for the longing to be back home"
1448 "again. And Dete had told her that she could go home whenever she"
1448 "liked. So it came about one day that Heidi felt she could not"
1448 "bear it any longer, and in haste she tied all the rolls up in her"
1448 "red shawl, put on her straw hat, and went downstairs. But just as"
1448 "she reached the hall-door she met Fraulein Rottenmeier herself,"
1448 "just returning from a walk, which put a stop to Heidi's journey."
1448 ""
1448 "Fraulein Rottenmeier stood still a moment, looking at her from"
1448 "top to toe in blank astonishment, her eye resting particularly"
1448 "on the red bundle. Then she broke out,--"
1448 ""
1448 "\"What have you dressed yourself like that for? What do you mean"
1448 "by this? Have I not strictly forbidden you to go running about"
1448 "in the streets? And here you are ready to start off again, and"
1448 "going out looking like a beggar.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I was not going to run about, I was going home,\" said Heidi,"
1448 "frightened."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What are you talking about! Going home! You want to go home?\""
1448 "exclaimed Fraulein Rottenmeier, her anger rising. \"To run away"
1448 "like that! What would Herr Sesemann say if he knew! Take care"
1448 "that he never hears of this! And what is the matter with his"
1448 "house, I should like to know! Have you not been better treated"
1448 "than you deserved? Have you wanted for a thing? Have you ever in"
1448 "your life before had such a house to live in, such a table, or"
1448 "so many to wait upon you? Have you?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"No,\" replied Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I should think not indeed!\" continued the exasperated lady."
1448 "\"You have everything you can possibly want here, and you are an"
1448 "ungrateful little thing; it's because you are too well off and"
1448 "comfortable that you have nothing to do but think what naughty"
1448 "thing you can do next!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Then Heidi's feelings got the better of her, and she poured"
1448 "forth her trouble. \"Indeed I only want to go home, for if I stay"
1448 "so long away Snowflake will begin crying again, and grandmother"
1448 "is waiting for me, and Greenfinch will get beaten, because I am"
1448 "not there to give Peter any cheese, and I can never see how the"
1448 "sun says good-night to the mountains; and if the great bird were"
1448 "to fly over Frankfurt he would croak louder than ever about"
1448 "people huddling all together and teaching each other bad things,"
1448 "and not going to live up on the rocks, where it is so much"
1448 "better.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Heaven have mercy on us, the child is out of her mind!\" cried"
1448 "Fraulein Rottenmeier, and she turned in terror and went quickly"
1448 "up the steps, running violently against Sebastian in her hurry."
1448 "\"Go and bring that unhappy little creature in at once,\" she"
1448 "ordered him, putting her hand to her forehead which she had"
1448 "bumped against his."
1448 ""
1448 "Sebastian did as he was told, rubbing his own head as he went,"
1448 "for he had received a still harder blow."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi had not moved, she stood with her eyes aflame and"
1448 "trembling all over with inward agitation."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What, got into trouble again?\" said Sebastian in a cheerful"
1448 "voice; but when he looked more closely at Heidi and saw that she"
1448 "did not move, he put his hand kindly on her shoulder, and said,"
1448 "trying to comfort her, \"There, there, don't take it to heart so"
1448 "much; keep up your spirits, that is the great thing! She has"
1448 "nearly made a hole in my head, but don't you let her bully you.\""
1448 "Then seeing that Heidi still did not stir, \"We must go; she"
1448 "ordered me to take you in.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi now began mounting the stairs, but with a slow, crawling"
1448 "step, very unlike her usual manner. Sebastian felt quite sad as"
1448 "he watched her, and as he followed her up he kept trying to"
1448 "encourage her. \"Don't you give in! don't let her make you"
1448 "unhappy! You keep up your courage! Why we've got such a sensible"
1448 "little miss that she has never cried once since she was here;"
1448 "many at that age cry a good dozen times a day. The kittens are"
1448 "enjoying themselves very much up in their home; they jump about"
1448 "all over the place and behave as if they were little mad things."
1448 "Later we will go up and see them, when Fraulein is out of the"
1448 "way, shall we?\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi gave a little nod of assent, but in such a joyless manner"
1448 "that it went to Sebastian's heart, and he followed her with"
1448 "sympathetic eyes as she crept away to her room."
1448 ""
1448 "At supper that evening Fraulein Rottenmeier did not speak, but"
1448 "she cast watchful looks towards Heidi as if expecting her at any"
1448 "minute to break out in some extraordinary way; but Heidi sat"
1448 "without moving or eating; all that she did was to hastily hide"
1448 "her roll in her pocket."
1448 ""
1448 "When the tutor arrived next morning, Fraulein Rottenmeier drew"
1448 "him privately aside, and confided her fear to him that the"
1448 "change of air and the new mode of life and unaccustomed"
1448 "surroundings had turned Heidi's head; then she told him of the"
1448 "incident of the day before, and of Heidi's strange speech. But"
1448 "the tutor assured her she need not be in alarm; he had already"
1448 "become aware that the child was somewhat eccentric, but otherwise"
1448 "quite right in her mind, and he was sure that, with careful"
1448 "treatment and education, the right balance would be restored, and"
1448 "it was this he was striving after. He was the more convinced of"
1448 "this by what he now heard, and by the fact that he had so far"
1448 "failed to teach her the alphabet, Heidi seeming unable to"
1448 "understand the letters."
1448 ""
1448 "Fraulein Rottenmeier was considerably relieved by his words, and"
1448 "released the tutor to his work. In the course of the afternoon"
1448 "the remembrance of Heidi's appearance the day before, as she was"
1448 "starting out on her travels, suddenly returned to the lady, and"
1448 "she made up her mind that she would supplement the child's"
1448 "clothing with various garments from Clara's wardrobe, so as to"
1448 "give her a decent appearance when Herr Sesemann returned. She"
1448 "confided her intention to Clara, who was quite willing to make"
1448 "over any number of dresses and hats to Heidi; so the lady went"
1448 "upstairs to overhaul the child's belongings and see what was to"
1448 "be kept and what thrown away. She returned, however, in the"
1448 "course of a few minutes with an expression of horror upon her"
1448 "face."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What is this, Adelaide, that I find in your wardrobe!\" she"
1448 "exclaimed. \"I never heard of any one doing such a thing before!"
1448 "In a cupboard meant for clothes, Adelaide, what do I see at the"
1448 "bottom but a heap of rolls! Will you believe it, Clara, bread in"
1448 "a wardrobe! a whole pile of bread! Tinette,\" she called to that"
1448 "young woman, who was in the dining-room, \"go upstairs and take"
1448 "away all those rolls out of Adelaide's cupboard and the old"
1448 "straw hat on the table.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"No! no!\" screamed Heidi. \"I must keep the hat, and the rolls"
1448 "are for grandmother,\" and she was rushing to stop Tinette when"
1448 "Fraulein Rottenmeier took hold of her. \"You will stop here, and"
1448 "all that bread and rubbish shall be taken to the place they"
1448 "belong to,\" she said in a determined tone as she kept her hand"
1448 "on the child to prevent her running forward."
1448 ""
1448 "Then Heidi in despair flung herself down on Clara's couch and"
1448 "broke into a wild fit of weeping, her crying becoming louder and"
1448 "more full of distress, every minute, while she kept on sobbing"
1448 "out at intervals, \"Now grandmother's' bread is all gone! They"
1448 "were all for grandmother, and now they are taken away, and"
1448 "grandmother won't have one,\" and she wept as if her heart would"
1448 "break. Fraulein Rottenmeier ran out of the room. Clara was"
1448 "distressed and alarmed at the child's crying. \"Heidi, Heidi,\""
1448 "she said imploringly, \"pray do not cry so! listen to me; don't be"
1448 "so unhappy; look now, I promise you that you shall have just as"
1448 "many rolls, or more, all fresh and new to take to grandmother"
1448 "when you go home; yours would have been hard and stale by then."
1448 "Come, Heidi, do not cry any more!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi could not get over her sobs for a long time; she would"
1448 "never have been able to leave off crying at all if it had not"
1448 "been for Clara's promise, which comforted her. But to make sure"
1448 "that she could depend upon it she kept on saying to Clara, her"
1448 "voice broken with her gradually subsiding sobs, \"Will you give"
1448 "me as many, quite as many, as I had, for grandmother?\" And Clara"
1448 "assured her each time that she would give her as many, \"or"
1448 "more,\" she added, \"only be happy again.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi appeared at supper with her eyes red with weeping, and"
1448 "when she saw her roll she could not suppress a sob. But she made"
1448 "an effort to control herself, for she knew she must sit quietly"
1448 "at table. Whenever Sebastian could catch her eye this evening he"
1448 "made all sorts of strange signs, pointing to his own head and"
1448 "then to hers, and giving little nods as much as to say, \"Don't"
1448 "you be unhappy! I have got it all safe for you.\""
1448 ""
1448 "When Heidi was going to get into bed that night she found her"
1448 "old straw hat lying under the counterpane. She snatched it up"
1448 "with delight, made it more out of shape still in her joy, and"
1448 "then, after wrapping a handkerchief round it, she stuck it in a"
1448 "corner of the cupboard as far back as she could."
1448 ""
1448 "It was Sebastian who had hidden it there for her; he had been in"
1448 "the dining-room when Tinette was called, and had heard all that"
1448 "went on with the child and the latter's loud weeping. So he"
1448 "followed Tinette, and when she came out of Heidi's room carrying"
1448 "the rolls and the hat, he caught up the hat and said, \"I will"
1448 "see to this old thing.\" He was genuinely glad to have been able"
1448 "to save it for Heidi, and that was the meaning of his encouraging"
1448 "signs to her at supper."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER IX. HERR SESEMANN HEARS OF THINGS WHICH ARE NEW TO HIM>"
1448 ""
1448 "A few days after these events there was great commotion and much"
1448 "running up and down stairs in Herr Sesemann's house. The master"
1448 "had just returned, and Sebastian and Tinette were busy carrying"
1448 "up one package after another from the carriage, for Herr"
1448 "Sesemann always brought back a lot of pretty things for his home."
1448 "He himself had not waited to do anything before going in to see"
1448 "his daughter. Heidi was sitting beside her, for it was late"
1448 "afternoon, when the two were always together. Father and"
1448 "daughter greeted each other with warm affection, for they were"
1448 "deeply attached to one another. Then he held out his hand to"
1448 "Heidi, who had stolen away into the corner, and said kindly to"
1448 "her, \"And this is our little Swiss girl; come and shake hands"
1448 "with me! That's right! Now, tell me, are Clara and you good"
1448 "friends with one another, or do you get angry and quarrel, and"
1448 "then cry and make it up, and then start quarreling again on the"
1448 "next occasion?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"No, Clara is always kind to me,\" answered Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "\"And Heidi,\" put in Clara quickly, \"has not once tried to"
1448 "quarrel.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"That's all right, I am glad to hear it,\" said her father, as he"
1448 "rose from his chair. \"But you must excuse me, Clara, for I want"
1448 "my dinner; I have had nothing to eat all day. Afterwards I will"
1448 "show you all the things I have brought home with me.\""
1448 ""
1448 "He found Fraulein Rottenmeier in the dining-room superintending"
1448 "the preparation for his meal, and when he had taken his place"
1448 "she sat down opposite to him, looking the every embodiment of bad"
1448 "news, so that he turned to her and said, \"What am I to expect,"
1448 "Fraulein Rottenmeier? You greet me with an expression of"
