1448 "alive, there is no reason why she should be dead.\""
1448 ""
1448 "After a while sleep fell on Heidi too, and after her disturbed"
1448 "night and early rising she slept so soundly that she did not"
1448 "wake till Sebastian shook her by the arm and called to her, \"Wake"
1448 "up, wake up! we shall have to get out directly; we are just in"
1448 "Basle!\""
1448 ""
1448 "There was a further railway journey of many hours the next day."
1448 "Heidi again sat with her basket on her knee, for she would not"
1448 "have given it up to Sebastian on any consideration; to-day she"
1448 "never even opened her mouth, for her excitement, which increased"
1448 "with every mile of the journey, kept her speechless. All of a"
1448 "sudden, before Heidi expected it, a voice called out,"
1448 "\"Mayenfeld.\" She and Sebastian both jumped up, the latter also"
1448 "taken by surprise. In another minute they were both standing on"
1448 "the platform with Heidi's trunk, and the train was steaming away"
1448 "down the valley. Sebastian looked after it regretfully, for he"
1448 "preferred the easier mode of travelling to a wearisome climb on"
1448 "foot, especially as there was danger no doubt as well as fatigue"
1448 "in a country like this, where, according to Sebastian's idea,"
1448 "everything and everybody were half savage. He therefore looked"
1448 "cautiously to either side to see who was a likely person to ask"
1448 "the safest way to Dorfli."
1448 ""
1448 "Just outside the station he saw a shabby-looking little cart and"
1448 "horse which a broad-shouldered man was loading with heavy sacks"
1448 "that had been brought by the train, so he went up to him and"
1448 "asked which was the safest way to get to Dorfli."
1448 ""
1448 "\"All the roads about here are safe,\" was the curt reply."
1448 ""
1448 "So Sebastian altered his question and asked which was the best"
1448 "way to avoid falling over the precipice, and also how a box"
1448 "could be conveyed to Dorfli. The man looked at the box, weighing"
1448 "it with his eye, and then volunteered if it was not too heavy to"
1448 "take it on his own cart, as he was driving to Dorfli. After some"
1448 "little interchange of words it was finally agreed that the man"
1448 "should take both the child and the box to Dorfli, and there find"
1448 "some one who could be sent on with Heidi up the mountain."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I can go by myself, I know the way well from Dorfli,\" put in"
1448 "Heidi, who had been listening attentively to the conversation."
1448 "Sebastian was greatly relieved at not having to do any mountain"
1448 "climbing. He drew Heidi aside and gave her a thick rolled"
1448 "parcel, and a letter for her grandfather; the parcel, he told"
1448 "her, was a present from Herr Sesemann, and she must put it at the"
1448 "bottom of her basket under the rolls and be very careful not to"
1448 "lose it, as Herr Sesemann would be very vexed if she did, and"
1448 "never be the same to her again; so little miss was to think well"
1448 "of what he said."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I shall be sure not to lose it,\" said Heidi confidently, and"
1448 "she at once put the roll and the letter at the bottom of her"
1448 "basket. The trunk meanwhile had been hoisted into the cart, and"
1448 "now Sebastian lifted Heidi and her basket on to the high seat and"
1448 "shook hands with her; he then made signs to her to keep her eye"
1448 "on the basket, for the driver was standing near and Sebastian"
1448 "thought it better to be careful, especially as he knew that he"
1448 "ought himself to have seen the child safely to her journey's"
1448 "end. The driver now swung himself up beside Heidi, and the cart"
1448 "rolled away in the direction of the mountains, while Sebastian,"
1448 "glad of having no tiring and dangerous journey on foot before"
1448 "him, sat down in the station and awaited the return train."
1448 ""
1448 "The driver of the car was the miller at Dorfli and was taking"
1448 "home his sacks of flour. He had never seen Heidi, but like"
1448 "everybody in Dorfli knew all about her. He had known her"
1448 "parents, and felt sure at once that this was the child of whom he"
1448 "had heard so much. He began to wonder why she had come back, and"
1448 "as they drove along he entered into conversation with her. \"You"
1448 "are the child who lived with your grandfather, Alm-Uncle, are you"
1448 "not?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Didn't they treat you well down there that you have come back"
1448 "so soon?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, it was not that; everything in Frankfurt is as nice as it"
1448 "could be.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Then why are you running home again?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Only because Herr Sesemann gave me leave, or else I should not"
1448 "have come.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"If they were willing to let you stay, why did you not remain"
1448 "where you were better off than at home?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Because I would a thousand times rather be with grandfather on"
1448 "the mountain than anywhere else in the world.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"You will think differently perhaps when you get back there,\""
1448 "grumbled the miller; and then to himself, \"It's strange of her,"
1448 "for she must know what it's like.\""
1448 ""
1448 "He began whistling and said no more, while Heidi looked around"
1448 "her and began to tremble with excitement, for she knew every"
1448 "tree along the way, and there overhead were the high jagged peaks"
1448 "of the mountain looking down on her like old friends. And Heidi"
1448 "nodded back to them, and grew every moment more wild with her"
1448 "joy and longing, feeling as if she must jump down from the cart"
1448 "and run with all her might till she reached the top. But she sat"
1448 "quite still and did not move, although inwardly in such"
1448 "agitation. The clock was striking five as they drove into"
1448 "Dorfli. A crowd of women and children immediately surrounded the"
1448 "cart, for the box and the child arriving with the miller had"
1448 "excited the curiosity of everybody in the neighborhood,"
1448 "inquisitive to know whence they came and whither they were going"
1448 "and to whom they belonged. As the miller lifted Heidi down, she"
1448 "said hastily, \"Thank you, grandfather will send for the trunk,\""
1448 "and was just going to run off, when first one and then another of"
1448 "the bystanders caught hold of her, each one having a different"
1448 "question to put to her. But Heidi pushed her way through them"
1448 "with such an expression of distress on her face that they were"
1448 "forced to let her go. \"You see,\" they said to one another, \"how"
1448 "frightened she is, and no wonder,\" and then they went on to talk"
1448 "of Alm-Uncle, how much worse he had grown that last year, never"
1448 "speaking a word and looking as if he would like to kill"
1448 "everybody he met, and if the child had anywhere else to go to she"
1448 "certainly would not run back to the old dragon's den. But here"
1448 "the miller interrupted them, saying he knew more about it than"
1448 "they did, and began telling them how a kind gentleman had brought"
1448 "her to Mayenfeld and seen her off, and had given him his fare"
1448 "without any bargaining, and extra money for himself; what was"
1448 "more, the child had assured him that she had had everything she"
1448 "wanted where she had been, and that it was her own wish to return"
1448 "to her grandfather. This information caused great surprise and"
1448 "was soon repeated all over Dorfli, and that evening there was not"
1448 "a house in the place in which the astounding news was not"
1448 "discussed, of how Heidi had of her own accord given up a"
1448 "luxurious home to return to her grandfather."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi climbed up the steep path from Dorfli as quickly as she"
1448 "could; she was obliged, however, to pause now and again to take"
1448 "breath, for the basket she carried was rather heavy, and the way"
1448 "got steeper as she drew nearer the top. One thought alone filled"
1448 "Heidi's mind, \"Would she find the grandmother sitting in her"
1448 "usual corner by the spinning-wheel, was she still alive?\" At"
1448 "last Heidi caught sight of the grandmother's house in the hollow"
1448 "of the mountain and her heart began to beat; she ran faster and"
1448 "faster and her heart beat louder and louder--and now she had"
1448 "reached the house, but she trembled so she could hardly open the"
1448 "door--and then she was standing inside, unable in her"
1448 "breathlessness to utter a sound."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Ah, my God!\" cried a voice from the corner, \"that was how Heidi"
1448 "used to run in; if only I could have her with me once again! Who"
1448 "is there?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"It's I, I, grandmother,\" cried Heidi as she ran and flung"
1448 "herself on her knees beside the old woman, and seizing her"
1448 "hands, clung to her, unable to speak for joy. And the grandmother"
1448 "herself could not say a word for some time, so unexpected was"
1448 "this happiness; but at last she put out her hand and stroked"
1448 "Heidi's curly hair, and said, \"Yes, yes, that is her hair, and"
1448 "her voice; thank God that He has granted my prayer!\" And tears"
1448 "of joy fell from the blind eyes on to Heidi's hand. \"Is it really"
1448 "you, Heidi; have you really come back to me?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, grandmother, I am really here,\" answered Heidi in a"
1448 "reassuring voice. \"Do not cry, for I have really come back and I"
1448 "am never going away again, and I shall come every day to see"
1448 "you, and you won't have any more hard bread to eat for some days,"
1448 "for look, look!\""
1448 ""
1448 "And Heidi took the rolls from the basket and piled the whole"
1448 "twelve up on grandmother's lap."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Ah, child! child! what a blessing you bring with you!\" the old"
1448 "woman exclaimed, as she felt and seemed never to come to the end"
1448 "of the rolls. \"But you yourself are the greatest blessing,"
1448 "Heidi,\" and again she touched the child's hair and passed her"
1448 "hand over her hot cheeks, and said, \"Say something, child, that"
1448 "I may hear your voice.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Then Heidi told her how unhappy she had been, thinking that the"
1448 "grandmother might die while she was away and would never have"
1448 "her white rolls, and that then she would never, never see her"
1448 "again."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter's mother now came in and stood for a moment overcome with"
1448 "astonishment. \"Why, it's Heidi,\" she exclaimed, \"and yet can it"
1448 "be?\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi stood up, and Brigitta now could not say enough in her"
1448 "admiration of the child's dress and appearance; she walked round"
1448 "her, exclaiming all the while, \"Grandmother, if you could only"
1448 "see her, and see what a pretty frock she has on; you would"
1448 "hardly know her again. And the hat with the feather in it is"
1448 "yours too, I suppose? Put it on that I may see how you look in"
1448 "it?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"No, I would rather not,\" replied Heidi firmly. \"You can have it"
1448 "if you like; I do not want it; I have my own still.\" And Heidi"
1448 "so saying undid her red bundle and took out her own old hat,"
1448 "which had become a little more battered still during the journey."
1448 "But this was no trouble to Heidi; she had not forgotten how her"
1448 "grandfather had called out to Dete that he never wished to see"
1448 "her and her hat and feathers again, and this was the reason she"
1448 "had so anxiously preserved her old hat, for she had never ceased"
1448 "to think about going home to her grandfather. But Brigitta told"
1448 "her not to be so foolish as to give it away; she would not think"
1448 "of taking such a beautiful hat; if Heidi did not want to wear it"
1448 "she might sell it to the schoolmaster's daughter in Dorfli and"
1448 "get a good deal of money for it. But Heidi stuck to her"
1448 "intention and hid the hat quietly in a corner behind the"
1448 "grandmother's chair. Then she took off her pretty dress and put"
1448 "her red shawl on over her under-petticoat, which left her arms"
1448 "bare; and now she clasped the old woman's hand. \"I must go home"
1448 "to grandfather,\" she said, \"but to-morrow I shall come again. Good-"
1448 "night, grandmother.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, come again, be sure you come again tomorrow,\" begged the"
1448 "grandmother, as she pressed Heidi's hands in hers, unwilling to"
1448 "let her go."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Why have you taken off that pretty dress?\" asked Brigitta."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Because I would rather go home to grandfather as I am or else"
1448 "perhaps he would not know me; you hardly did at first.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Brigitta went with her to the door, and there said in rather a"
1448 "mysterious voice, \"You might have kept on your dress, he would"
1448 "have known you all right; but you must be careful, for Peter"
1448 "tells me that Alm-Uncle is always now in a bad temper and never"
1448 "speaks.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi bid her good-night and continued her way up the mountain,"
1448 "her basket on her arm. All around her the steep green slopes"
1448 "shone bright in the evening sun, and soon the great gleaming snow-"
1448 "field up above came in sight. Heidi was obliged to keep on"
1448 "pausing to look behind her, for the higher peaks were behind her"
1448 "as she climbed. Suddenly a warm red glow fell on the grass at"
1448 "her feet; she looked back again--she had not remembered how"
1448 "splendid it was, nor seen anything to compare to it in her dreams--"
1448 "for there the two high mountain peeks rose into the air like two"
1448 "great flames, the whole snow-field had turned crimson, and rosy-"
1448 "colored clouds floated in the sky above. The grass upon the"
1448 "mountain sides had turned to gold, the rocks were all aglow, and"
1448 "the whole valley was bathed in golden mist. And as Heidi stood"
1448 "gazing around her at all this splendor the tears ran down her"
1448 "cheeks for very delight and happiness, and impulsively she put"
1448 "her hands together, and lifting her eyes to heaven, thanked God"
1448 "aloud for having brought her home, thanked Him that everything"
1448 "was as beautiful as ever, more beautiful even than she had"
1448 "thought, and that it was all hers again once more. And she was so"
1448 "overflowing with joy and thankfulness that she could not find"
1448 "words to thank Him enough. Not until the glory began to fade"
1448 "could she tear herself away. Then she ran on so quickly that in"
1448 "a very little while she caught sight of the tops of the fir trees"
1448 "above the hut roof, then the roof itself, and at last the whole"
1448 "hut, and there was grandfather sitting as in old days smoking"
1448 "his pipe, and she could see the fir trees waving in the wind."
1448 "Quicker and quicker went her little feet, and before Alm-Uncle"
1448 "had time to see who was coming, Heidi had rushed up to him,"
1448 "thrown down her basket and flung her arms round his neck, unable"
1448 "in the excitement of seeing him again to say more than"
1448 "\"Grandfather! grandfather! grandfather!\" over and over again."
1448 ""
1448 "And the old man himself said nothing. For the first time for"
1448 "many years his eyes were wet, and he had to pass his hand across"
1448 "them. Then he unloosed Heidi's arms, put her on his knee, and"
1448 "after looking at her for a moment, \"So you have come back to me,"
1448 "Heidi,\" he said, \"how is that? You don't look much of a grand"
1448 "lady. Did they send you away?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh, no, grandfather,\" said Heidi eagerly, \"you must not think"
1448 "that; they were all so kind--Clara, and grandmamma, and Herr"
1448 "Sesemann. But you see, grandfather, I did not know how to bear"
1448 "myself till I got home again to you. I used to think I should"
1448 "die, for I felt as if I could not breathe; but I never said"
1448 "anything because it would have been ungrateful. And then"
1448 "suddenly one morning quite early Herr Sesemann said to me--but I"
1448 "think it was partly the doctor's doing--but perhaps it's all in"
1448 "the letter--\" and Heidi jumped down and fetched the roll and the"
1448 "letter and handed them both to her grandfather."
1448 ""
1448 "\"That belongs to you,\" said the latter, laying the roll down on"
1448 "the bench beside him. Then he opened the letter, read it through"
1448 "and without a word put it in his pocket."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Do you think you can still drink milk with me, Heidi?\" he"
1448 "asked, taking the child by the hand to go into the hut. \"But"
1448 "bring your money with you; you can buy a bed and bedclothes and"
1448 "dresses for a couple of years with it.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I am sure I do not want it,\" replied Heidi. \"I have got a bed"
1448 "already, and Clara has put such a lot of clothes in my box that"
1448 "I shall never want any more.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Take it and put it in the cupboard; you will want it some day I"
1448 "have no doubt.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi obeyed and skipped happily after her grandfather into the"
1448 "house; she ran into all the corners, delighted to see everything"
1448 "again, and then went up the ladder--but there she came to a"
1448 "pause and called down in a tone of surprise and distress, \"Oh,"
1448 "grandfather, my bed's gone.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"We can soon make it up again,\" he answered her from below. \"I"
1448 "did not know that you were coming back; come along now and have"
1448 "your milk.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi came down, sat herself on her high stool in the old place,"
1448 "and then taking up her bowl drank her milk eagerly, as if she"
1448 "had never come across anything so delicious, and as she put down"
1448 "her bowl, she exclaimed, \"Our milk tastes nicer than anything"
1448 "else in the world, grandfather.\""
1448 ""
1448 "A shrill whistle was heard outside. Heidi darted out like a"
1448 "flash of lightning. There were the goats leaping and springing"
1448 "among the rocks, with Peter in their midst. When he caught sight"
1448 "of Heidi he stood still with astonishment and gazed speechlessly"
1448 "at her. Heidi called out, \"Good-evening, Peter,\" and then ran in"
1448 "among the goats. \"Little Swan! Little Bear! do you know me"
1448 "again?\" And the animals evidently recognized her voice at once,"
1448 "for they began rubbing their heads against her and bleating"
1448 "loudly as if for joy, and as she called the other goats by name"
1448 "one after the other, they all came scampering towards her helter-"
1448 "skelter and crowding round her. The impatient Greenfinch sprang"
1448 "into the air and over two of her companions in order to get"
1448 "nearer, and even the shy little Snowflake butted the Great Turk"
1448 "out of her way in quite a determined manner, which left him"
1448 "standing taken aback by her boldness, and lifting his beard in"
1448 "the air as much as to say, You see who I am."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi was out of her mind with delight at being among all her"
1448 "old friends again; she flung her arms round the pretty little"
1448 "Snowflake, stroked the obstreperous Greenfinch, while she"
1448 "herself was thrust at from all sides by the affectionate and"
1448 "confiding goats; and so at last she got near to where Peter was"
1448 "still standing, not having yet got over his surprise."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Come down, Peter,\" cried Heidi, \"and say good-evening to me.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"So you are back again?\" he found words to say at last, and now"
1448 "ran down and took Heidi's hand which she was holding out in"
1448 "greeting, and immediately put the same question to her which he"
1448 "had been in the habit of doing in the old days when they"
1448 "returned home in the evening, \"Will you come out with me again to-"
1448 "morrow?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Not to-morrow, but the day after perhaps, for to-morrow I must"
1448 "go down to grandmother.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I am glad you are back,\" said Peter, while his whole face"
1448 "beamed with pleasure, and then he prepared to go on with his"
1448 "goats; but he never had had so much trouble with them before, for"
1448 "when at last, by coaxing and threats, he had got them all"
1448 "together, and Heidi had gone off with an arm over either head of"
1448 "her grandfather's two, the whole flock suddenly turned and ran"
1448 "after her. Heidi had to go inside the stall with her two and shut"
1448 "the door, or Peter would never have got home that night. When"
1448 "Heidi went indoors after this she found her bed already made up"
1448 "for her; the hay had been piled high for it and smelt"
1448 "deliciously, for it had only just been got in, and the"
1448 "grandfather had carefully spread and tucked in the clean sheets."
1448 "It was with a happy heart that Heidi lay down in it that night,"
1448 "and her sleep was sounder than it had been for a whole year past."
1448 "The grandfather got up at least ten times during the night and"
1448 "mounted the ladder to see if Heidi was all right and showing no"
1448 "signs of restlessness, and to feel that the hay he had stuffed"
1448 "into the round window was keeping the moon from shining too"
1448 "brightly upon her. But Heidi did not stir; she had no need now"
1448 "to wander about, for the great burning longing of her heart was"
1448 "satisfied; she had seen the high mountains and rocks alight in"
1448 "the evening glow, she had heard the wind in the fir trees, she"
1448 "was at home again on the mountain."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER XIV. SUNDAY BELLS>"
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi was standing under the waving fir trees waiting for her"
1448 "grandfather, who was going down with her to grandmother's, and"
1448 "then on to Dorfli to fetch her box. She was longing to know how"
1448 "grandmother had enjoyed her white bread and impatient to see and"
1448 "hear her again; but no time seemed weary to her now, for she"
1448 "could not listen long enough to the familiar voice of the trees,"
1448 "or drink in too much of the fragrance wafted to her from the"
1448 "green pastures where the golden-headed flowers were glowing in"
1448 "the sun, a very feast to her eyes. The grandfather came out,"
1448 "gave a look round, and then called to her in a cheerful voice,"
1448 "\"Well, now we can be off.\""
1448 ""
1448 "It was Saturday, a day when Alm-Uncle made everything clean and"
1448 "tidy inside and outside the house; he had devoted his morning to"
1448 "this work so as to be able to accompany Heidi in the afternoon,"
1448 "and the whole place was now as spick and span as he liked to see"
1448 "it. They parted at the grandmother's cottage and Heidi ran in."
1448 "The grandmother had heard her steps approaching and greeted her"
1448 "as she crossed the threshold, \"Is it you, child? Have you come"
1448 "again?\""
1448 ""
1448 "Then she took hold of Heidi's hand and held it fast in her own,"
1448 "for she still seemed to fear that the child might be torn from"
1448 "her again. And now she had to tell Heidi how much she had"
1448 "enjoyed the white bread, and how much stronger she felt already"
1448 "for having been able to eat it, and then Peter's mother went on"
1448 "and said she was sure that if her mother could eat like that for"
1448 "a week she would get back some of her strength, but she was so"
1448 "afraid of coming to the end of the rolls, that she had only"
1448 "eaten one as yet. Heidi listened to all Brigitta said, and sat"
1448 "thinking for a while. Then she suddenly thought of a way."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I know, grandmother, what I will do,\" she said eagerly, \"I will"
1448 "write to Clara, and she will send me as many rolls again, if not"
1448 "twice as many as you have already, for I had ever such a large"
1448 "heap in the wardrobe, and when they were all taken away she"
1448 "promised to give me as many back, and she would do so I am"
1448 "sure.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"That is a good idea,\" said Brigitta; \"but then, they would get"
1448 "hard and stale. The baker in Dorfli makes the white rolls, and"
1448 "if we could get some of those he has over now and then--but I can"
1448 "only just manage to pay for the black bread.\""
1448 ""
1448 "A further bright thought came to Heidi, and with a look of joy,"
1448 "\"Oh, I have lots of money, grandmother,\" she cried gleefully,"
1448 "skipping about the room in her delight, \"and I know now what I"
1448 "will do with it. You must have a fresh white roll every day, and"
1448 "two on Sunday, and Peter can bring them up from Dorfli.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"No, no, child!\" answered the grandmother, \"I cannot let you do"
1448 "that; the money was not given to you for that purpose; you must"
1448 "give it to your grandfather, and he will tell you how you are to"
1448 "spend it.\""
1448 ""
1448 "But Heidi was not to be hindered in her kind intentions, and she"
1448 "continued to jump about, saying over and over again in a tone of"
1448 "exultation, \"Now, grandmother can have a roll every day and will"
1448 "grow quite strong again--and, Oh, grandmother,\" she suddenly"
1448 "exclaimed with an increase of jubilation in her voice, \"if you"
1448 "get strong everything will grow light again for you; perhaps"
1448 "it's only because you are weak that it is dark.\" The grandmother"
1448 "said nothing, she did not wish to spoil the child's pleasure. As"
1448 "she went jumping about Heidi suddenly caught sight of the"
1448 "grandmother's song book, and another happy idea struck her,"
1448 "\"Grandmother, I can also read now, would you like me to read you"
1448 "one of your hymns from your old book?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh, yes,\" said the grandmother, surprised and delighted; \"but"
1448 "can you really read, child, really?\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi had climbed on to a chair and had already lifted down the"
1448 "book, bringing a cloud of dust with it, for it had lain"
1448 "untouched on the shelf for a long time. Heidi wiped it, sat"
1448 "herself down on a stool beside the old woman, and asked her which"
1448 "hymn she should read."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What you like, child, what you like,\" and the grandmother"
1448 "pushed her spinning-wheel aside and sat in eager expectation"
1448 "waiting for Heidi to begin. Heidi turned over the leaves and read"
1448 "a line out softly to herself here and there. At last she said,"
1448 ""
1448 "\"Here is one about the sun, grandmother, I will read you that.\""
1448 "And Heidi began, reading with more and more warmth of expression"
1448 "as she went on,--"
1448 ""
1448 "     The morning breaks,"
1448 "      And warm and bright"
1448 "      The earth lies still"
1448 "      In the golden light--"
1448 "  For Dawn has scattered the clouds of night."
1448 ""
1448 "     God's handiwork"
1448 "      Is seen around,"
1448 "      Things great and small"
1448 "      To His praise abound--"
1448 "  Where are the signs of His love not found?"
1448 ""
1448 "     All things must pass,"
1448 "      But God shall still"
1448 "      With steadfast power"
1448 "      His will fulfil--"
1448 "  Sure and unshaken is His will."
1448 ""
1448 "     His saving grace"
1448 "      Will never fail,"
1448 "      Though grief and fear"
1448 "      The heart assail--"
1448 "  O'er life's wild seas He will prevail."
1448 ""
1448 "     Joy shall be ours"
1448 "      In that garden blest,"
1448 "      Where after storm"
1448 "      We find our rest--"
1448 "  I wait in peace--God's time is best."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "The grandmother sat with folded hands and a look of indescribable"
1448 "joy on her face, such as Heidi had never seen there before,"
1448 "although at the same time the tears were running down her cheeks."
1448 "As Heidi finished, she implored her, saying, \"Read it once again,"
1448 "child, just once again.\""
1448 ""
1448 "And the child began again, with as much pleasure in the verses"
1448 "as the grandmother,--"
1448 ""
1448 "     Joy shall be ours"
1448 "      In that garden blest,"
1448 "      Where after storm"
1448 "      We find our rest--"
1448 "  I wait in peace--God's time is best."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Ah, Heidi, that brings light to the heart! What comfort you"
1448 "have brought me!\""
1448 ""
1448 "And the old woman kept on repeating the glad words, while Heidi"
1448 "beamed with happiness, and she could not take her eyes away from"
1448 "the grandmother's face, which had never looked like that before."
1448 "It had no longer the old troubled expression, but was alight"
1448 "with peace and joy as if she were already looking with clear new"
1448 "eyes into the garden or Paradise."
1448 ""
1448 "Some one now knocked at the window and Heidi looked up and saw"
1448 "her grandfather beckoning her to come home with him. She"
1448 "promised the grandmother before leaving her that she would be"
1448 "with her the next day, and even if she went out with Peter she"
1448 "would only spend half the day with him, for the thought that she"
1448 "might make it light and happy again for the grandmother gave her"
1448 "the greatest pleasure, greater even than being out on the sunny"
1448 "mountain with the flowers and goats. As she was going out"
1448 "Brigitta ran to her with the frock and hat she had left. Heidi"
1448 "put the dress over her arm, for, as she thought to herself, the"
1448 "grandfather had seen that before, but she obstinately refused to"
1448 "take back the hat; Brigitta could keep it, for she should never"
1448 "put it on her head again. Heidi was so full of her morning's"
1448 "doings that she began at once to tell her grandfather all about"
1448 "them: how the white bread could be fetched every day from Dorfli"
1448 "if there was money for it, and how the grandmother had all at"
1448 "once grown stronger and happier, and light had come to her. Then"
1448 "she returned to the subject of the rolls. \"If the grandmother"
1448 "won't take the money, grandfather, will you give it all to me,"
1448 "and I can then give Peter enough every day to buy a roll and two"
1448 "on Sunday?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"But how about the bed?\" said her grandfather. \"It would be nice"
1448 "for you to have a proper bed, and there would then be plenty for"
1448 "the bread.\""
1448 ""
1448 "But Heidi gave her grandfather no peace till he consented to do"
1448 "what she wanted; she slept a great deal better, she said, on her"
1448 "bed of hay than on her fine pillowed bed in Frankfurt. So at"
1448 "last he said, \"The money is yours, do what you like with it; you"
1448 "can buy bread for grandmother for years to come with it.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi shouted for joy at the thought that grandmother would"
1448 "never need any more to eat hard black bread, and \"Oh,"
1448 "grandfather!\" she said, \"everything is happier now than it has"
1448 "ever been in our lives before!\" and she sang and skipped along,"
1448 "holding her grandfather's hand as light-hearted as a bird. But"
1448 "all at once she grew quiet and said, \"If God had let me come at"
1448 "once, as I prayed, then everything would have been different, I"
1448 "should only have had a little bread to bring to grandmother, and"
1448 "I should not have been able to read, which is such a comfort to"
1448 "her; but God has arranged it all so much better than I knew how"
1448 "to; everything has happened just as the other grandmother said it"
1448 "would. Oh, how glad I am that God did not let me have at once all"
1448 "I prayed and wept for! And now I shall always pray to God as she"
1448 "told me, and always thank Him, and when He does not do anything I"
1448 "ask for I shall think to myself, It's just like it was in"
1448 "Frankfurt: God, I am sure, is going to do something better still."
1448 "So we will pray every day, won't we, grandfather, and never"
1448 "forget Him again, or else He may forget us.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"And supposing one does forget Him?\" said the grandfather in a"
1448 "low voice."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Then everything goes wrong, for God lets us then go where we"
1448 "like, and when we get poor and miserable and begin to cry about"
1448 "it no one pities us, but they say, You ran away from God, and so"
1448 "God, who could have helped you, left you to yourself.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"That is true, Heidi; where did you learn that?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"From grandmamma; she explained it all to me.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The grandfather walked on for a little while without speaking,"
1448 "then he said, as if following his own train of thought: \"And if"
1448 "it once is so, it is so always; no one can go back, and he whom"
1448 "God has forgotten, is forgotten for ever.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh, no, grandfather, we can go back, for grandmamma told me so,"
1448 "and so it was in the beautiful tale in my book--but you have not"
1448 "heard that yet; but we shall be home directly now, and then I"
1448 "will read it you, and you will see how beautiful it is.\" And in"
1448 "her eagerness Heidi struggled faster and faster up the steep"
1448 "ascent, and they were no sooner at the top than she let go her"
1448 "grandfather's hand and ran into the hut. The grandfather slung"
1448 "the basket off his shoulders in which he had brought up a part"
1448 "of the contents of the trunk which was too heavy to carry up as"
1448 "it was. Then he sat down on his seat and began thinking."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi soon came running out with her book under her arm. \"That's"
1448 "right, grandfather,\" she exclaimed as she saw he had already"
1448 "taken his seat, and in a second she was beside him and had her"
1448 "book open at the particular tale, for she had read it so often"
1448 "that the leaves fell open at it of their own accord. And now in"
1448 "a sympathetic voice Heidi began to read of the son when he was"
1448 "happily at home, and went out into the fields with his father's"
1448 "flocks, and was dressed in a fine cloak, and stood leaning on"
1448 "his shepherd's staff watching as the sun went down, just as he"
1448 "was to be seen in the picture. But then all at once he wanted to"
1448 "have his own goods and money and to be his own master, and so he"
1448 "asked his father to give him his portion, and he left his home"
1448 "and went and wasted all his substance. And when he had nothing"
1448 "left he hired himself out to a master who had no flocks and"
1448 "fields like his father, but only swine to keep; and so he was"
1448 "obliged to watch these, and he only had rags to wear and a few"
1448 "husks to eat such as the swine fed upon. And then he thought of"
1448 "his old happy life at home and of how kindly his father had"
1448 "treated him and how ungrateful he had been, and he wept for"
1448 "sorrow and longing. And he thought to himself, \"I will arise and"
1448 "go to my father, and will say to him, 'Father, I am not worthy to"
1448 "be called thy son; make me as one of thy hired servants.'\" And"
1448 "when he was yet a great way off his father saw him . . . Here"
1448 "Heidi paused in her reading. \"What do you think happens now,"
1448 "grandfather?\" she said. \"Do you think the father is still angry"
1448 "and will say to him, 'I told you so!' Well, listen now to what"
1448 "comes next.\" His father saw him, and had compassion, and ran, and"
1448 "fell on his neck and kissed him. And the son said to him,"
1448 "\"Father, I have sinned against heaven and in thy sight, and am no"
1448 "more worthy to be called thy son.\" But the father said to his"
1448 "servants, \"Bring forth the best robe, and put it on him; and put"
1448 "a ring on his hand and shoes on his feet: and bring hither the"
1448 "fatted calf and kill it; and let us eat and be merry, for this my"
1448 "son was dead and is alive again; he was lost and is found.\" And"
1448 "they began to be merry."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Isn't that a beautiful tale, grandfather,\" said Heidi, as the"
1448 "latter continued to sit without speaking, for she had expected"
1448 "him to express pleasure and astonishment."
1448 ""
1448 "\"You are right, Heidi; it is a beautiful tale,\" he replied, but"
1448 "he looked so grave as he said it that Heidi grew silent herself"
1448 "and sat looking quietly at her pictures. Presently she pushed"
1448 "her book gently in front of him and said, \"See how happy he is"
1448 "there,\" and she pointed with her finger to the figure of the"
1448 "returned prodigal, who was standing by his father clad in fresh"
1448 "raiment as one of his own sons again."
1448 ""
1448 "A few hours later, as Heidi lay fast asleep in her bed, the"
1448 "grandfather went up the ladder and put his lamp down near her"
1448 "bed so that the light fell on the sleeping child. Her hands were"
1448 "still folded as if she had fallen asleep saying her prayers, an"
1448 "expression of peace and trust lay on the little face, and"
1448 "something in it seemed to appeal to the grandfather, for he"
1448 "stood a long time gazing down at her without speaking. At last he"
1448 "too folded his hands, and with bowed head said in a low voice,"
1448 "\"Father, I have sinned against heaven and before thee and am not"
1448 "worthy to be called thy son.\" And two large tears rolled down"
1448 "the old man's cheeks."
1448 ""
1448 "Early the next morning he stood in front of his hut and gazed"
1448 "quietly around him. The fresh bright morning sun lay on mountain"
1448 "and valley. The sound of a few early bells rang up from the"
1448 "valley, and the birds were singing their morning song in the fir"
1448 "trees. He stepped back into the hut and called up, \"Come along,"
1448 "Heidi! the sun is up! Put on your best frock, for we are going"
1448 "to church together!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi was not long getting ready; it was such an unusual summons"
1448 "from her grandfather that she must make haste. She put on her"
1448 "smart Frankfurt dress and soon went down, but when she saw her"
1448 "grandfather she stood still, gazing at him in astonishment."
1448 "\"Why, grandfather!\" she exclaimed, \"I never saw you look like"
1448 "that before! and the coat with the silver buttons! Oh, you do"
1448 "look nice in your Sunday coat!\""
1448 ""
1448 "The old man smiled and replied, \"And you too; now come along!\""
1448 "He took Heidi's hand in his and together they walked down the"
1448 "mountain side. The bells were ringing in every direction now,"
1448 "sounding louder and fuller as they neared the valley, and Heidi"
1448 "listened to them with delight. \"Hark at them, grandfather! it's"
1448 "like a great festival!\""
1448 ""
1448 "The congregation had already assembled and the singing had begun"
1448 "when Heidi and her grandfather entered the church at Dorfli and"
1448 "sat down at the back. But before the hymn was over every one was"
1448 "nudging his neighbor and whispering, \"Do you see? Alm-Uncle is"
1448 "in church!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Soon everybody in the church knew of Alm-Uncle's presence, and"
1448 "the women kept on turning round to look and quite lost their"
1448 "place in the singing. But everybody became more attentive when"
1448 "the sermon began, for the preacher spoke with such warmth and"
1448 "thankfulness that those present felt the effect of his words, as"
1448 "if some great joy had come to them all. At the close of the"
1448 "service Alm-Uncle took Heidi by the hand, and on leaving the"
1448 "church made his way towards the pastor's house; the rest of the"
1448 "congregation looked curiously after him, some even following to"
1448 "see whether he went inside the pastor's house, which he did."
1448 "Then they collected in groups and talked over this strange event,"
1448 "keeping their eyes on the pastor's door, watching to see whether"
1448 "Alm-Uncle came out looking angry and quarrelsome, or as if the"
1448 "interview had been a peaceful one, for they could not imagine"
1448 "what had brought the old man down, and what it all meant. Some,"
1448 "however, adopted a new tone and expressed their opinion that Alm-"
1448 "Uncle was not so bad after all as they thought, \"for see how"
1448 "carefully he took the little one by the hand.\" And others"
1448 "responded and said they had always thought people had"
1448 "exaggerated about him, that if he was so downright bad he would"
1448 "be afraid to go inside the pastor's house. Then the miller put in"
1448 "his word, \"Did I not tell you so from the first? What child is"
1448 "there who would run away from where she had plenty to eat and"
1448 "drink and everything of the best, home to a grandfather who was"
1448 "cruel and unkind, and of whom she was afraid?\""
1448 ""
1448 "And so everybody began to feel quite friendly towards Alm-Uncle,"
1448 "and the women now came up and related all they had been told by"
1448 "Peter and his grandmother, and finally they all stood there like"
1448 "people waiting for an old friend whom they had long missed from"
1448 "among their number."
1448 ""
1448 "Meanwhile Alm-Uncle had gone into the pastor's house and knocked"
1448 "at the study door. The latter came out and greeted him, not as"
1448 "if he was surprised to see him, but as if he had quite expected"
1448 "to see him there; he probably had caught sight of the old man in"
1448 "church. He shook hands warmly with him, and Alm-Uncle was unable"
1448 "at first to speak, for he had not expected such a friendly"
1448 "reception. At last he collected himself and said, \"I have come"
1448 "to ask you, pastor, to forget the words I spoke to you when you"
1448 "called on me, and to beg you not to owe me ill-will for having"
1448 "been so obstinately set against your well-meant advice. You were"
1448 "right, and I was wrong, but I have now made up my mind to follow"
1448 "your advice and to find a place for myself at Dorfli for the"
1448 "winter, for the child is not strong enough to stand the bitter"
1448 "cold up on the mountain. And if the people down here look"
1448 "askance at me, as at a person not to be trusted, I know it is my"
1448 "own fault, and you will, I am sure, not do so.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The pastor's kindly eyes shone with pleasure. He pressed the old"
1448 "man's hand in his, and said with emotion, \"Neighbor, you went"
1448 "into the right church before you came to mine; I am greatly"
1448 "rejoiced. You will not repent coming to live with us again; as"
1448 "for myself you will always be welcome as a dear friend and"
1448 "neighbor, and I look forward to our spending many a pleasant"
1448 "winter evening together, for I shall prize your companionship,"
1448 "and we will find some nice friends too for the little one.\" And"
1448 "the pastor laid his hand kindly on the child's curly head and"
1448 "took her by the hand as he walked to the door with the old man."
1448 "He did not say good-bye to him till they were standing outside,"
1448 "so that all the people standing about saw him shake hands as if"
1448 "parting reluctantly from his best friend. The door had hardly"
1448 "shut behind him before the whole congregation now came forward"
1448 "to greet Alm-Uncle, every one striving to be the first to shake"
1448 "hands with him, and so many were held out that Alm-Uncle did not"
1448 "know with which to begin; and some said, \"We are so pleased to"
1448 "see you among us again,\" and another, \"I have long been wishing"
1448 "we could have a talk together again,\" and greetings of all kinds"
1448 "echoed from every side, and when Alm-Uncle told them he was"
1448 "thinking of returning to his old quarters in Dorfli for the"
1448 "winter, there was such a general chorus of pleasure that any one"
1448 "would have thought he was the most beloved person in all Dorfli,"
1448 "and that they had hardly known how to live without him. Most of"
1448 "his friends accompanied him and Heidi some way up the mountain,"
1448 "and each as they bid him good-bye made him promise that when he"
1448 "next came down he would without fail come and call. As the old"
1448 "man at last stood alone with the child, watching their"
1448 "retreating figures, there was a light upon his face as if"
1448 "reflected from some inner sunshine of heart. Heidi, looking up at"
1448 "him with her clear steady eyes, said, \"Grandfather, you look"
1448 "nicer and nicer to-day, I never saw you quite like that before.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Do you think so?\" he answered with a smile. \"Well, yes, Heidi,"
1448 "I am happier to-day than I deserve, happier than I had thought"
1448 "possible; it is good to be at peace with God and man! God was"
1448 "good to me when He sent you to my hut.\""
1448 ""
1448 "When they reached Peter's home the grandfather opened the door"
1448 "and walked straight in. \"Good-morning, grandmother,\" he said. \"I"
1448 "think we shall have to do some more patching, up before the"
1448 "autumn winds come.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Dear God, if it is not Uncle!\" cried the grandmother in pleased"
1448 "surprise. \"That I should live to see such a thing! and now I can"
1448 "thank you for all that you have done for me. May God reward you!"
1448 "may God reward you!\" She stretched out a trembling hand to him,"
1448 "and when the grandfather shook it warmly, she went on, still"
1448 "holding his, \"And I have something on my heart I want to say, a"
1448 "prayer to make to you! If I have injured you in any way, do not"
1448 "punish me by sending the child away again before I lie under the"
1448 "grass. Oh, you do not know what that child is to me!\" and she"
1448 "clasped the child to her, for Heidi had already taken her usual"
1448 "stand close to the grandmother."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Have no fear, grandmother,\" said Uncle in a reassuring voice,"
1448 "\"I shall not punish either you or myself by doing so. We are all"
1448 "together now, and pray God we may continue so for long.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Brigitta now drew the Uncle aside towards a corner of the room"
1448 "and showed him the hat with the feathers, explaining to him how"
1448 "it came there, and adding that of course she could not take such"
1448 "a thing from a child."
1448 ""
1448 "But the grandfather looked towards Heidi without any displeasure"
1448 "of countenance and said, \"The hat is hers, and if she does not"
1448 "wish to wear it any more she has a right to say so and to give"
1448 "it to you, so take it, pray.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Brigitta was highly delighted at this. \"It is well worth more"
1448 "than ten shillings!\" she said as she held it up for further"
1448 "admiration. \"And what a blessing Heidi has brought home with her"
1448 "from Frankfurt! I have thought sometimes that it might be good"
1448 "to send Peter there for a little while; what do you think,"
1448 "Uncle?\""
1448 ""
1448 "A merry look came into the grandfather's eye. He thought it"
1448 "would do Peter no harm, but he had better wait for a good"
1448 "opportunity before starting. At this moment the subject of their"
1448 "conversation himself rushed in, evidently in a great hurry,"
1448 "knocking his head violently against the door in his haste, so"
1448 "that everything in the room rattled. Gasping and breathless he"
1448 "stood still after this and held out a letter. This was another"
1448 "great event, for such a thing had never happened before; the"
1448 "letter was addressed to Heidi and had been delivered at the post-"
1448 "office in Dorfli. They all sat down round the table to hear what"
1448 "was in it, for Heidi opened it at once and read it without"
1448 "hesitation. The letter was from Clara. The latter wrote that the"
1448 "house had been so dull since Heidi left that she did not know how"
1448 "to bear herself, and she had at last persuaded her father to take"
1448 "her to the baths at Ragatz in the coming autumn; grandmamma had"
1448 "arranged to join them there, and they both were looking forward"
1448 "to paying her and her grandfather a visit. And grandmamma sent a"
1448 "further message to Heidi which was that the latter had done quite"
1448 "right to take the rolls to the grandmother, and so that she might"
1448 "not have to eat them dry, she was sending some coffee, which was"
1448 "already on its way, and grandmamma hoped when she came to the"
1448 "Alm in the autumn that Heidi would take her to see her old"
1448 "friend."
1448 ""
1448 "There were exclamations of pleasure and astonishment on hearing"
1448 "all this news, and so much to talk and ask about that even the"
1448 "grandfather did not notice how the time was passing; there was"
1448 "general delight at the thought of the coming days, and even more"
1448 "at the meeting which had taken place on this one, and the"
1448 "grandmother spoke and said, \"The happiest of all things is when"
1448 "an old friend comes and greets us as in former times; the heart"
1448 "is comforted with the assurance that some day everything that we"
1448 "have loved will be given back to us.--You will come soon again,"
1448 "uncle, and you child, to-morrow?\""
1448 ""
1448 "The old man and Heidi promised her faithfully to do so; then it"
1448 "was time to break up the party, and these two went back up the"
1448 "mountain. As they had been greeted with bells when they made"
1448 "their journey down in the morning, so now they were accompanied"
1448 "by the peaceful evening chimes as they climbed to the hut, which"
1448 "had quite a Sunday-like appearance as it stood bathed in the"
1448 "light of the low evening sun."
1448 ""
1448 "But when grandmamma comes next autumn there will be many fresh"
1448 "joys and surprises both for Heidi and grandmother; without doubt"
1448 "a proper bed will be put up in the hay-loft, for wherever"
1448 "grandmamma steps in, there everything is soon in right order,"
1448 "outside and in."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER XV. PREPARATIONS FOR A JOURNEY>"
1448 ""
1448 "The kind doctor who had given the order that Heidi was to be"
1448 "sent home was walking along one of the broad streets towards Herr"
1448 "Sesemann's house. It was a sunny September morning, so full of"
1448 "light and sweetness that it seemed as if everybody must rejoice."
1448 "But the doctor walked with his eyes fastened to the ground and"
1448 "did not once lift them to the blue sky above him. There was an"
1448 "expression of sadness on his face, formerly so cheerful, and his"
1448 "hair had grown greyer since the spring. The doctor had had an"
1448 "only daughter, who, after his wife's death, had been his sole"
1448 "and constant companion, but only a few months previously death"
1448 "had deprived him of his dear child, and he had never been the"
1448 "same bright and cheery man since."
1448 ""
1448 "Sebastian opened the door to him, greeting him with every mark"
1448 "of respectful civility, for the doctor was not only the most"
1448 "cherished friend of the master and his daughter, but had by his"
1448 "kindness won the hearts of the whole household."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Everything as usual, Sebastian?\" asked the doctor in his"
1448 "pleasant voice as he preceded Sebastian up the stairs."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I am glad you have come, doctor,\" exclaimed Herr Sesemann as"
1448 "the latter entered. \"We must really have another talk over this"
1448 "Swiss journey; do you still adhere to your decision, even though"
1448 "Clara is decidedly improving in health?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"My dear Sesemann, I never knew such a man as you!\" said the"
1448 "doctor as he sat down beside his friend. \"I really wish your"
1448 "mother was here; everything would be clear and straightforward"
1448 "then and she would soon put things in right train. You sent for"
1448 "me three times yesterday only to ask me the same question,"
1448 "though you know what I think.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, I know, it's enough to make you out of patience with me;"
1448 "but you must understand, dear friend\"--and Herr Sesemann laid"
1448 "his hand imploringly on the doctor's shoulder--\"that I feel I"
1448 "have not the courage to refuse the child what I have been"
1448 "promising her all along, and for months now she has been living"
1448 "on the thought of it day and night. She bore this last bad attack"
1448 "so patiently because she was buoyed up with the hope that she"
1448 "should soon start on her Swiss journey, and see her friend Heidi"
1448 "again; and now must I tell the poor child, who has to give up so"
1448 "many pleasures, that this visit she has so long looked forward to"
1448 "must also be cancelled? I really have not the courage to do it.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"You must make up your mind to it, Sesemann,\" said the doctor"
1448 "with authority, and as his friend continued silent and dejected"
1448 "he went on after a pause, \"Consider yourself how the matter"
1448 "stands. Clara has not had such a bad summer as this last one for"
1448 "years. Only the worst results would follow from the fatigue of"
1448 "such a journey, and it is out of the question for her. And then"
1448 "we are already in September, and although it may still be warm"
1448 "and fine up there, it may just as likely be already very cold."
1448 "The days too are growing short, and as Clara cannot spend the"
1448 "night up there she would only have a two hours' visit at the"
1448 "outside. The journey from Ragatz would take hours, for she would"
1448 "have to be carried up the mountain in a chair. In short,"
1448 "Sesemann, it is impossible. But I will go in with you and talk"
1448 "to Clara; she is a reasonable child, and I will tell her what my"
1448 "plans are. Next May she shall be taken to the baths and stay"
1448 "there for the cure until it is quite hot weather. Then she can"
1448 "be carried up the mountain from time to time, and when she is"
1448 "stronger she will enjoy these excursions far more than she would"
1448 "now. Understand, Sesemann, that if we want to give the child a"
1448 "chance of recovery we must use the utmost care and"
1448 "watchfulness.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Herr Sesemann, who had listened to the doctor in sad and"
1448 "submissive silence, now suddenly jumped up. \"Doctor,\" he said,"
1448 "\"tell me truly: have you really any hope of her final recovery?\""
1448 ""
1448 "The doctor shrugged his shoulders. \"Very little,\" he replied"
1448 "quietly. \"But, friend, think of my trouble. You have still a"
1448 "beloved child to look for you and greet you on your return home."
1448 "You do not come back to an empty house and sit down to a"
1448 "solitary meal. And the child is happy and comfortable at home"
1448 "too. If there is much that she has to give up, she has on the"
1448 "other hand many advantages. No, Sesemann, you are not so greatly"
1448 "to be pitied--you have still the happiness of being together."
1448 "Think of my lonely house!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Herr Sesemann was now striding up and down the room as was his"
1448 "habit when deeply engaged in thought. Suddenly he came to a"
1448 "pause beside his friend and laid his hand on his shoulder."
1448 "\"Doctor, I have an idea; I cannot bear to see you look as you do;"
1448 "you are no longer the same man. You must be taken out of yourself"
1448 "for a while, and what do you think I propose? That you shall take"
1448 "the journey and go and pay Heidi a visit in our name.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The doctor was taken aback at this sudden proposal and wanted to"
1448 "make objections, but his friend gave him no time to say"
1448 "anything. He was so delighted with his idea, that he seized the"
1448 "doctor by the arm and drew him into Clara's room. The kind doctor"
1448 "was always a welcome visitor to Clara, for he generally had"
1448 "something amusing to tell her. Lately, it is true, he had been"
1448 "graver, but Clara knew the reason why and would have given much"
1448 "to see him his old lively self again. She held out her hand to"
1448 "him as he came up to her; he took a seat beside her, and her"
1448 "father also drew up his chair, and taking Clara's hand in his"
1448 "began to talk to her of the Swiss journey and how he himself had"
1448 "looked forward to it. He passed as quickly as he could over the"
1448 "main point that it was now impossible for her to undertake it,"
1448 "for he dreaded the tears that would follow; but he went on"
1448 "without pause to tell her of his new plan, and dwelt on the great"
1448 "benefit it would be to his friend if he could be persuaded to"
1448 "take this holiday."
1448 ""
1448 "The tears were indeed swimming in the blue eyes, although Clara"
1448 "struggled to keep them down for her father's sake, but it was a"
1448 "bitter disappointment to give up the journey, the thought of"
1448 "which had been her only joy and solace during the lonely hours"
1448 "of her long illness. She knew, however, that her father would"
1448 "never refuse her a thing unless he was certain that it would be"
1448 "harmful for her. So she swallowed her tears as well as she could"
1448 "and turned her thoughts to the one hope still left her. Taking"
1448 "the doctor's hand and stroking it, she said pleadingly,--"
1448 ""
1448 "\"Dear doctor, you will go and see Heidi, won't you? and then you"
1448 "can come and tell me all about it, what it is like up there, and"
1448 "what Heidi and the grandfather, and Peter and the goats do all"
1448 "day. I know them all so well! And then you can take what I want"
1448 "to send to Heidi; I have thought about it all, and also"
1448 "something for the grandmother. Do pray go, dear doctor, and I"
1448 "will take as much cod liver oil as you like.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Whether this promise finally decided the doctor it is impossible"
1448 "to say, but it is certain that he smiled and said,--"
1448 ""
1448 "\"Then I must certainly go, Clara, for you will then get as plump"
1448 "and strong as your father and I wish to see you. And have you"
1448 "decided when I am to start?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"To-morrow morning--early if possible,\" replied Clara."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, she is right,\" put in Herr Sesemann; \"the sun is shining"
1448 "and the sky is blue, and there is no time to be lost; it is a"
1448 "pity to miss a single one of these days on the mountain.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The doctor could not help laughing. \"You will be reproaching me"
1448 "next for not being there already; well, I must go and make"
1448 "arrangements for getting off.\""
1448 ""
1448 "But Clara would not let him go until she had given him endless"
1448 "messages for Heidi, and had explained all he was to look at so"
1448 "as to give her an exact description on his return. Her presents"
1448 "she would send round later, as Fraulein Rottenmeier must first"
1448 "help her to pack them up; at that moment she was out on one of"
1448 "her excursions into the town which always kept her engaged for"
1448 "some time. The doctor promised to obey Clara's directions in"
1448 "every particular; he would start some time during the following"
1448 "day if not the first thing in the morning, and would bring back a"
1448 "faithful account of his experiences and of all he saw and heard."
1448 ""
1448 "The servants of a household have a curious faculty of divining"
1448 "what is going on before they are actually told about anything."
1448 "Sebastian and Tinette must have possessed this faculty in a high"
1448 "degree, for even as the doctor was going downstairs, Tinette,"
1448 "who had been rung for, entered Clara's room."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Take that box and bring it back filled with the soft cakes"
1448 "which we have with coffee,\" said Clara, pointing to a box which"
1448 "had been brought long before in preparation for this. Tinette"
1448 "took it up, and carried it out, dangling it contemptuously in her"
1448 "hand."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Hardly worth the trouble I should have thought,\" she said"
1448 "pertly as she left the room."
1448 ""
1448 "As Sebastian opened the door for the doctor he said with a bow,"
1448 "\"Will the Herr Doctor be so kind as to give the little miss my"
1448 "greetings?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I see,\" said the doctor, \"you know then already that I am off"
1448 "on a journey.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Sebastian hesitated and gave an awkward little cough. \"I am--I"
1448 "have--I hardly know myself. O yes, I remember; I happened to"
1448 "pass through the dining-room and caught little miss's name, and I"
1448 "put two and two together--and so I thought--\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I see, I see,\" smiled the doctor, \"one can find out a great"
1448 "many thinks by thinking. Good-bye till I see you again,"
1448 "Sebastian, I will be sure and give your message.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The doctor was hastening off when he met with a sudden obstacle;"
1448 "the violent wind had prevented Fraulein Rottenmeier prosecuting"
1448 "her walk any farther, and she was just returning and had reached"
1448 "the door as he was coming out. The white shawl she wore was so"
1448 "blown out by the wind that she looked like a ship in full sail."
1448 "The doctor drew back, but Fraulein Rottenmeier had always"
1448 "evinced peculiar appreciation and respect for this man, and she"
1448 "also drew back with exaggerated politeness to let him pass. The"
1448 "two stood for a few seconds, each anxious to make way for the"
1448 "other, but a sudden gust of wind sent Fraulein Rottenmeier flying"
1448 "with all her sails almost into the doctor's arms, and she had to"
1448 "pause and recover herself before she could shake hands with the"
1448 "doctor with becoming decorum. She was put out at having been"
1448 "forced to enter in so undignified a manner, but the doctor had a"
1448 "way of smoothing people's ruffled feathers, and she was soon"
1448 "listening with her usual composure while he informed her of his"
1448 "intended journey, begging her in his most conciliatory voice to"
1448 "pack up the parcels for Heidi as she alone knew how to pack. And"
1448 "then he took his leave."
1448 ""
1448 "Clara quite expected to have a long tussle with Fraulein"
1448 "Rottenmeier before she would get the latter to consent to"
1448 "sending all the things that she had collected as presents for"
1448 "Heidi. But this time she was mistaken, for Fraulein Rottenmeier"
1448 "was in a more than usually good temper. She cleared the large"
1448 "table so that all the things for Heidi could be spread out upon"
1448 "it and packed under Clara's own eyes. It was no light job, for"
1448 "the presents were of all shapes and sizes. First there was the"
1448 "little warm cloak with a hood, which had been designed by Clara"
1448 "herself, in order that Heidi during the coming winter might be"
1448 "able to go and see grandmother when she liked, and not have to"
1448 "wait till her grandfather could take her wrapped up in a sack to"
1448 "keep her from freezing. Then came a thick warm shawl for the"
1448 "grandmother, in which she could wrap herself well up and not feel"
1448 "the cold when the wind came sweeping in such terrible gusts round"
1448 "the house. The next object was the large box full of cakes; these"
1448 "were also for the grandmother, that she might have something to"
1448 "eat with her coffee besides bread. An immense sausage was the"
1448 "next article; this had been originally intended for Peter, who"
1448 "never had anything but bread and cheese, but Clara had altered"
1448 "her mind, fearing that in his delight he might eat it all up at"
1448 "once and make himself ill. So she arranged to send it to"
1448 "Brigitta, who could take some for herself and the grandmother and"
1448 "give Peter his portion out by degrees. A packet of tobacco was a"
1448 "present for grandfather, who was fond of his pipe as he sat"
1448 "resting in the evening. Finally there was a whole lot of"
1448 "mysterious little bags, and parcels, and boxes, which Clara had"
1448 "had especial pleasure in collecting, as each was to be a joyful"
1448 "surprise for Heidi as she opened it. The work came to an end at"
1448 "last, and an imposing-looking package lay on the floor ready for"
1448 "transport. Fraulein Rottenmeier looked at it with satisfaction,"
1448 "lost in the consideration of the art of packing. Clara eyed it"
1448 "too with pleasure, picturing Heidi's exclamations and jumps of"
1448 "joy and surprise when the huge parcel arrived at the hut."
1448 ""
1448 "And now Sebastian came in, and lifting the package on to his"
1448 "shoulder, carried it off to be forwarded at once to the doctor's"
1448 "house."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER XVI. A VISITOR>"
1448 ""
1448 "The early light of morning lay rosy red upon the mountains, and"
1448 "a fresh breeze rustled through the fir trees and set their"
1448 "ancient branches waving to and fro. The sound awoke Heidi and she"
1448 "opened her eyes. The roaring in the trees always stirred a strong"
1448 "emotion within her and seemed to drew her irresistibly to them."
1448 "So she jumped out of bed and dressed herself as quickly as she"
1448 "could, but it took her some time even then, for she was careful"
1448 "now to be always clean and tidy."
1448 ""
1448 "When she went down her ladder she found her grandfather had"
1448 "already left the hut. He was standing outside looking at the sky"
1448 "and examining the landscape as he did every morning, to see what"
1448 "sort of weather it was going to be."
1448 ""
1448 "Little pink clouds were floating over the sky, that was growing"
1448 "brighter and bluer with every minute, while the heights and the"
1448 "meadow lands were turning gold under the rising sun, which was"
1448 "just appearing above the topmost peaks."
1448 ""
1448 "\"O how beautiful! how beautiful! Good-morning, grandfather!\""
1448 "cried Heidi, running out."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What, you are awake already, are you?\" he answered, giving her"
1448 "a morning greeting."
1448 ""
1448 "Then Heidi ran round to the fir trees to enjoy the sound she"
1448 "loved so well, and with every fresh gust of wind which came"
1448 "roaring through their branches she gave a fresh jump and cry of"
1448 "delight."
1448 ""
1448 "Meanwhile the grandfather had gone to milk the goats; this done"
1448 "he brushed and washed them, ready for their mountain excursion,"
1448 "and brought them out of their shed. As soon as Heidi caught"
1448 "sight of her two friends she ran and embraced them, and they"
1448 "bleated in return, while they vied with each other in showing"
1448 "their affection by poking their heads against her and trying"
1448 "which could get nearest her, so that she was almost crushed"
1448 "between them. But Heidi was not afraid of them, and when the"
1448 "lively Little Bear gave rather too violent a thrust, she only"
1448 "said, \"No, Little Bear, you are pushing like the Great Turk,\" and"
1448 "Little Bear immediately drew back his head and left off his rough"
1448 "attentions, while Little Swan lifted her head and put on an"
1448 "expression as much as to say, \"No one shall ever accuse me of"
1448 "behaving like the Great Turk.\" For White Swan was a rather more"
1448 "distinguished person than Brown Bear."
1448 ""
1448 "And now Peter's whistle was heard and all the goats came along,"
1448 "leaping and springing, and Heidi soon found herself surrounded"
1448 "by the whole flock, pushed this way and that by their"
1448 "obstreperous greetings, but at last she managed to get through"
1448 "them to where Snowflake was standing, for the young goat had in"
1448 "vain striven to reach her."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter now gave a last tremendous whistle, in order to startle"
1448 "the goats and drive them off, for he wanted to get near himself"
1448 "to say something to Heidi. The goats sprang aside and he came up"
1448 "to her."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Can you come out with me to-day?\" he asked, evidently unwilling"
1448 "to hear her refuse."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I am afraid I cannot, Peter,\" she answered. \"I am expecting"
1448 "them every minute from Frankfurt, and I must be at home when they"
1448 "come.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"You have said the same thing for days now,\" grumbled Peter."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I must continue to say it till they come,\" replied Heidi. \"How"
1448 "can you think, Peter, that I would be away when they came? As if"
1448 "I could do such a thing?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"They would find Uncle at home,\" he answered with a snarling"
1448 "voice."
1448 ""
1448 "But at this moment the grandfather's stentorian voice was heard."
1448 "\"Why is the army not marching forward? Is it the field-marshal"
1448 "who is missing or some of the troops?\""
1448 ""
1448 "Whereupon Peter turned and went off, swinging his stick round so"
1448 "that it whistled through the air, and the goats, who understood"
1448 "the signal, started at full trot for their mountain pasture,"
1448 "Peter following in their wake."
1448 ""
1448 "Since Heidi had been back with her grandfather things came now"
1448 "and then into her mind of which she had never thought in former"
1448 "days. So now, with great exertion, she put her bed in order"
1448 "every morning, patting and stroking it till she had got it"
1448 "perfectly smooth and flat. Then she went about the room"
1448 "downstairs, put each chair back in its place, and if she found"
1448 "anything lying about she put it in the cupboard. After that she"
1448 "fetched a duster, climbed on a chair, and rubbed the table till"
1448 "it shone again. When the grandfather came in later he would look"
1448 "round well pleased and say to himself, \"We look like Sunday every"
1448 "day now; Heidi did not go abroad for nothing.\""
1448 ""
1448 "After Peter had departed and she and her grandfather had"
1448 "breakfasted, Heidi began her daily work as usual, but she did"
1448 "not get on with it very fast. It was so lovely out of doors to-"
1448 "day, and every minute something happened to interrupt her in her"
1448 "work. Now it was a bright beam of sun shining cheerfully through"
1448 "the open window, and seeming to say, \"Come out, Heidi, come out!\""
1448 "Heidi felt she could not stay indoors, and she ran out in answer"
1448 "to the call. The sunlight lay sparkling on everything around the"
1448 "hut and on all the mountains and far away along the valley, and"
1448 "the grass slope looked so golden and inviting that she was"
1448 "obliged to sit down for a few minutes and look about her. Then"
1448 "she suddenly remembered that her stool was left standing in the"
1448 "middle of the floor and that the table had not been rubbed, and"
1448 "she jumped up and ran inside again. But it was not long before"
1448 "the fir trees began their old song; Heidi felt it in all her"
1448 "limbs, and again the desire to run outside was irresistible, and"
1448 "she was off to play and leap to the tune of the waving branches."
1448 "The grandfather, who was busy in his work-shed, stepped out from"
1448 "time to time smiling to watch her at her gambols. He had just"
1448 "gone back to his work on one of these occasions when Heidi"
1448 "called out, \"Grandfather! grandfather! Come, come!\""
1448 ""
1448 "He stepped quickly out, almost afraid something had happened to"
1448 "the child, but he saw her running towards where the mountain"
1448 "path descended, crying, \"They are coming! they are coming! and"
1448 "the doctor is in front of them!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi rushed forward to welcome her old friend, who held out his"
1448 "hands in greeting to her. When she came up to him she clung to"
1448 "his outstretched arm, and exclaimed in the joy of her heart,"
1448 "\"Good-morning, doctor, and thank you ever so many times.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"God bless you, child! what have you got to thank me for?\" asked"
1448 "the doctor, smiling."
1448 ""
1448 "\"For being at home again with grandfather,\" the child explained."
1448 ""
1448 "The doctor's face brightened as if a sudden ray of sunshine had"
1448 "passed across it; he had not expected such a reception as this."
1448 "Lost in the sense of his loneliness he had climbed the mountain"
1448 "without heeding how beautiful it was on every side, and how more"
1448 "and more beautiful it became the higher he got. He had quite"
1448 "thought that Heidi would have forgotten him; she had seen so"
1448 "little of him, and he had felt rather like one bearing a message"
1448 "of disappointment, anticipating no great show of favor, coming"
1448 "as he did without the expected friends. But instead, here was"
1448 "Heidi, her eyes dancing for joy, and full of gratitude and"
1448 "affection, clinging to the arm of her kind friend."
1448 ""
1448 "He took her by the hand with fatherly tenderness."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Take me now to your grandfather, Heidi, and show me where you"
1448 "live.\""
1448 ""
1448 "But Heidi still remained standing, looking down the path with a"
1448 "questioning gaze. \"Where are Clara and grandmother?\" she asked."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Ah, now I have to tell you something which you will be as sorry"
1448 "about as I am,\" answered the doctor. \"You see, Heidi, I have"
1448 "come alone. Clara was very ill and could not travel, and so the"
1448 "grandmother stayed behind too. But next spring, when the days"
1448 "grow warm and long again, they are coming here for certain.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi was greatly concerned; she could not at first bring"
1448 "herself to believe that what she had for so long been picturing"
1448 "to herself was not going to happen after all. She stood"
1448 "motionless for a second or two, overcome by the unexpected"
1448 "disappointment. The doctor said nothing further; all around lay"
1448 "the silence, only the sighing of the fir trees could be heard"
1448 "from where they stood. Then Heidi suddenly remembered why she had"
1448 "run down there, and that the doctor had really come. She lifted"
1448 "her eyes and saw the sad expression in his as he looked down at"
1448 "her; she had never seen him with that look on his face when she"
1448 "was in Frankfurt. It went to Heidi's heart; she could not bear to"
1448 "see anybody unhappy, especially her dear doctor. No doubt it was"
1448 "because Clara and grandmother could not come, and so she began to"
1448 "think how best she might console him."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh, it won't be very long to wait for spring, and then they"
1448 "will be sure to come,\" she said in a reassuring voice. \"Time"
1448 "passes very quickly with us, and then they will be able to stay"
1448 "longer when they are here, and Clara will be pleased at that. Now"
1448 "let us go and find grandfather.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Hand in hand with her friend she climbed up to the hut. She was"
1448 "so anxious to make the doctor happy again that she began once"
1448 "more assuring him that the winter passed so quickly on the"
1448 "mountain that it was hardly to be taken account of, and that"
1448 "summer would be back again before they knew it, and she became"
1448 "so convinced of the truth of her own words that she called out"
1448 "quite cheerfully to her grandfather as they approached, \"They"
1448 "have not come to-day, but they will be here in a very short"
1448 "time.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The doctor was no stranger to the grandfather, for the child had"
1448 "talked to him so much about her friend. The old man held out his"
1448 "hand to his guest in friendly greeting. Then the two men sat"
1448 "down in front of the hut, and Heidi had her little place too, for"
1448 "the doctor beckoned her to come and sit beside him. The doctor"
1448 "told Uncle how Herr Sesemann had insisted on his taking this"
1448 "journey, and he felt himself it would do him good as he had not"
1448 "been quite the thing for a long time. Then he whispered to Heidi"
1448 "that there was something being brought up the mountain which had"
1448 "travelled with him from Frankfurt, and which would give her even"
1448 "more pleasure than seeing the old doctor. Heidi got into a great"
1448 "state of excitement on hearing this, wondering what it could be,"
1448 "The old man urged the doctor to spend as many of the beautiful"
1448 "autumn days on the mountain as he could, and at least to come up"
1448 "whenever it was fine; he could not offer him a lodging, as he had"
1448 "no place to put him; he advised the doctor, however, not to go"
1448 "back to Ragatz, but to stay at Dorfli, where there was a clean"
1448 "tidy little inn. Then the doctor could come up every morning,"
1448 "which would do him no end of good, and if he liked, he, the"
1448 "grandfather, would act as his guide to any part of the mountains"
1448 "he would like to see. The doctor was delighted with this"
1448 "proposal, and it was settled that it should be as the"
1448 "grandfather suggested."
1448 ""
1448 "Meanwhile the sun had been climbing up the sky, and it was now"
1448 "noon. The wind had sunk and the fir trees stood motionless. The"
1448 "air was still wonderfully warm and mild for that height, while a"
1448 "delicious freshness was mingled with the warmth of the sun."
1448 ""
1448 "Alm-Uncle now rose and went indoors, returning in a few minutes"
1448 "with a table which he placed in front of the seat."
1448 ""
1448 "\"There, Heidi, now run in and bring us what we want for the"
1448 "table,\" he said. \"The doctor must take us as he finds us; if the"
1448 "food is plain, he will acknowledge that the dining-room is"
1448 "pleasant.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I should think so indeed,\" replied the doctor as he looked down"
1448 "over the sun-lit valley, \"and I accept the kind invitation;"
1448 "everything must taste good up here.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi ran backwards and forwards as busy as a bee and brought"
1448 "out everything she could find in the cupboard, for she did not"
1448 "know how to be pleased enough that she could help to entertain"
1448 "the doctor. The grandfather meanwhile had been preparing the"
1448 "meal, and now appeared with a steaming jug of milk and golden-"
1448 "brown toasted cheese. Then he cut some thin slices from the meat"
1448 "he had cured himself in the pure air, and the doctor enjoyed his"
1448 "dinner better than he had for a whole year past."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Our Clara must certainly come up here,\" he said, \"it would make"
1448 "her quite a different person, and if she ate for any length of"
1448 "time as I have to-day, she would grow plumper than any one has"
1448 "ever known her before.\""
1448 ""
1448 "As he spoke a man was seen coming up the path carrying a large"
1448 "package on his back. When he reached the hut he threw it on the"
1448 "ground and drew in two or three good breaths of the mountain"
1448 "air."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Ah, here's what travelled with me from Frankfurt,\" said the"
1448 "doctor, rising, and he went up to the package and began undoing"
1448 "it, Heidi looking on in great expectation. After he had released"
1448 "it from its heavy outer covering, \"There, child,\" he said, \"now"
1448 "you can go on unpacking your treasures yourself.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi undid her presents one by one until they were all"
1448 "displayed; she could not speak the while for wonder and delight."
1448 "Not till the doctor went up to her again and opened the large"
1448 "box to show Heidi the cakes that were for the grandmother to eat"
1448 "with her coffee, did she at last give a cry of joy, exclaiming,"
1448 "\"Now grandmother will have nice things to eat,\" and she wanted to"
1448 "pack everything up again and start at once to give them to her."
1448 "But the grandfather said he should walk down with the doctor that"
1448 "evening and she could go with them and take the things. Heidi"
1448 "now found the packet of tobacco which she ran and gave to her"
1448 "grandfather; he was so pleased with it that he immediately"
1448 "filled his pipe with some, and the two men then sat down together"
1448 "again, the smoke curling up from their pipes as they talked of"
1448 "all kinds of things, while Heidi continued to examine first one"
1448 "and then another of her presents. Suddenly she ran up to them,"
1448 "and standing in front of the doctor waited till there was a pause"
1448 "in the conversation, and then said, \"No, the other thing has not"
1448 "given me more pleasure than seeing you, doctor.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The two men could not help laughing, and the doctor answered"
