1448 "that he should never have thought it."
1448 ""
1448 "As the sun began to sink behind the mountains the doctor rose,"
1448 "thinking it was time to return to Dorfli and seek for quarters."
1448 "The grandfather carried the cakes and the shawl and the large"
1448 "sausage, and the doctor took Heidi's hand, so they all three"
1448 "started down the mountain. Arrived at Peter's home Heidi bid the"
1448 "others good-bye; she was to wait at grandmother's till her"
1448 "grandfather, who was going on to Dorfli with his guest, returned"
1448 "to fetch her. As the doctor shook hands with her she asked,"
1448 "\"Would you like to come out with the goats to-morrow morning?\""
1448 "for she could think of no greater treat to offer him."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Agreed!\" answered the doctor, \"we will go together,\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi now ran in to the grandmother; she first, with some"
1448 "effort, managed to carry in the box of cakes; then she ran out"
1448 "again and brought in the sausage--for her grandfather had put the"
1448 "presents down by the door--and then a third time for the shawl."
1448 "She had placed them as close as she could to the grandmother, so"
1448 "that the latter might be able to feel them and understand what"
1448 "was there. The shawl she laid over the old woman's knees."
1448 ""
1448 "\"They are all from Frankfurt, from Clara and grandmamma,\" she"
1448 "explained to the astonished grandmother and Brigitta, the latter"
1448 "having watched her dragging in all the heavy things, unable to"
1448 "imagine what was happening."
1448 ""
1448 "\"And you are very pleased with the cakes, aren't you,"
1448 "grandmother? taste how soft they are!\" said Heidi over and over"
1448 "again, to which the grandmother continued to answer, \"Yes, yes,"
1448 "Heidi, I should think so! what kind people they must be!\" And"
1448 "then she would pass her hand over the warm thick shawl and add,"
1448 "\"This will be beautiful for the cold winter! I never thought I"
1448 "should ever have such a splendid thing as this to put on.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi could not help feeling some surprise at the grandmother"
1448 "seeming to take more pleasure in the shawl than the cakes."
1448 "Meanwhile Brigitta stood gazing at the sausage with almost an"
1448 "expression of awe. She had hardly in her life seen such a"
1448 "monster sausage, much less owned one, and she could scarcely"
1448 "believe her eyes. She shook her head and said doubtfully, \"I must"
1448 "ask Uncle what it is meant for,\""
1448 ""
1448 "But Heidi answered without hesitation, \"It is meant for eating,"
1448 "not for anything else.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter came tumbling in at this minute. \"Uncle is just behind me,"
1448 "he is coming--\" he began, and then stopped short, for his eye"
1448 "had caught sight of the sausage, and he was too much taken aback"
1448 "to say more. But Heidi understood that her grandfather was near"
1448 "and so said good-bye to grandmother. The old man now never passed"
1448 "the door without going in to wish the old woman good-day, and she"
1448 "liked to hear his footstep approaching, for he always had a"
1448 "cheery word for her. But to-day it was growing late for Heidi,"
1448 "who was always up with the lark, and the grandfather would never"
1448 "let her go to bed after hours; so this evening he only called"
1448 "good-night through the open door and started home at once with"
1448 "the child, and the two climbed under the starlit sky back to"
1448 "their peaceful dwelling."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER XVII. A COMPENSATION>"
1448 ""
1448 "The next morning the doctor climbed up from Dorfli with Peter"
1448 "and the goats. The kindly gentleman tried now and then to enter"
1448 "into conversation with the boy, but his attempts failed, for he"
1448 "could hardly get a word out of Peter in answer to his questions."
1448 "Peter was not easily persuaded to talk. So the party silently"
1448 "made their way up to the hut, where they found Heidi awaiting"
1448 "them with her two goats, all three as fresh and lively as the"
1448 "morning sun among the mountains."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Are you coming to-day?\" said Peter, repeating the words with"
1448 "which he daily greeted her, either in question or in summons."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Of course I am, if the doctor is coming too,\" replied Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter cast a sidelong glance at the doctor. The grandfather now"
1448 "came out with the dinner bag, and after bidding good-day to the"
1448 "doctor he went up to Peter and slung it over his neck. It was"
1448 "heavier than usual, for Alm-Uncle had added some meat to-day, as"
1448 "he thought the doctor might like to have his lunch out and eat"
1448 "it when the children did. Peter gave a grin, for he felt sure"
1448 "there was something more than ordinary in it."
1448 ""
1448 "And so the ascent began. The goats as usual came thronging"
1448 "around Heidi, each trying to be nearest her, until at last she"
1448 "stood still and said, \"Now you must go on in front and behave"
1448 "properly, and not keep on turning back and pushing and poking me,"
1448 "for I want to talk to the doctor,\" and she gave Snowflake a"
1448 "little pat on the back and told her to be good and obedient. By"
1448 "degrees she managed to make her way out from among them and"
1448 "joined the doctor, who took her by the hand. He had no difficulty"
1448 "now in conversing with his companion, for Heidi had a great deal"
1448 "to say about the goats and their peculiarities, and about the"
1448 "flowers and the rocks and the birds, and so they clambered on and"
1448 "reached their resting-place before they were aware. Peter had"
1448 "sent a good many unfriendly glances towards the doctor on the way"
1448 "up, which might have quite alarmed the latter if he had happened"
1448 "to notice them, which, fortunately, he did not."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi now led her friend to her favorite spot where she was"
1448 "accustomed to sit and enjoy the beauty around her; the doctor"
1448 "followed her example and took his seat beside her on the warm"
1448 "grass. Over the heights and over the far green valley hung the"
1448 "golden glory of the autumn day. The great snow-field sparkled in"
1448 "the bright sunlight, and the two grey rocky peaks rose in their"
1448 "ancient majesty against the dark blue sky. A soft, light morning"
1448 "breeze blew deliciously across the mountain, gently stirring the"
1448 "bluebells that still remained of the summer's wealth of flowers,"
1448 "their slender heads nodding cheerfully in the sunshine. Overhead"
1448 "the great bird was flying round and round in wide circles, but to-"
1448 "day he made no sound; poised on his large wings he floated"
1448 "contentedly in the blue ether. Heidi looked about her first at"
1448 "one thing and then at another. The waving flowers, the blue sky,"
1448 "the bright sunshine, the happy bird--everything was so"
1448 "beautiful! so beautiful! Her eyes were alight with joy. And now"
1448 "she turned to her friend to see if he too were enjoying the"
1448 "beauty. The doctor had been sitting thoughtfully gazing around"
1448 "him. As he met her glad bright eyes, \"Yes, Heidi,\" he responded,"
1448 "\"I see how lovely it all is, but tell me--if one brings a sad"
1448 "heart up here, how may it be healed so that it can rejoice in all"
1448 "this beauty?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh, but,\" exclaimed Heidi, \"no one is sad up here, only in"
1448 "Frankfurt.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The doctor smiled and then growing serious again he continued,"
1448 "\"But supposing one is not able to leave all the sadness behind"
1448 "at Frankfurt; can you tell me anything that will help then?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"When you do not know what more to do you must go and tell"
1448 "everything to God,\" answered Heidi with decision."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Ah, that is a good thought of yours, Heidi,\" said the doctor."
1448 "\"But if it is God Himself who has sent the trouble, what can we"
1448 "say to Him then?\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi sat pondering for a while; she was sure in her heart that"
1448 "God could help out of every trouble. She thought over her own"
1448 "experiences and then found her answer."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Then you must wait,\" she said, \"and keep on saying to yourself:"
1448 "God certainly knows of some happiness for us which He is going"
1448 "to bring out of the trouble, only we must have patience and not"
1448 "run away. And then all at once something happens and we see"
1448 "clearly ourselves that God has had some good thought in His mind"
1448 "all along; but because we cannot see things beforehand, and only"
1448 "know how dreadfully miserable we are, we think it is always going"
1448 "to be so.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"That is a beautiful faith, child, and be sure you hold it"
1448 "fast,\" replied the doctor. Then he sat on a while in silence,"
1448 "looking at the great overshadowing mountains and the green,"
1448 "sunlit valley below before he spoke again,--"
1448 ""
1448 "\"Can you understand, Heidi, that a man may sit here with such a"
1448 "shadow over his eyes that he cannot feel and enjoy the beauty"
1448 "around him, while the heart grows doubly sad knowing how"
1448 "beautiful it could be? Can you understand that?\""
1448 ""
1448 "A pain shot through the child's young happy heart. The shadow"
1448 "over the eyes brought to her remembrance the grandmother, who"
1448 "would never again be able to see the sunlight and the beauty up"
1448 "here. This was Heidi's great sorrow, which re-awoke each time"
1448 "she thought about the darkness. She did not speak for a few"
1448 "minutes, for her happiness was interrupted by this sudden pang."
1448 "Then in a grave voice she said,--"
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, I can understand it. And I know this, that then one must"
1448 "say one of grandmother's hymns, which bring the light back a"
1448 "little, and often make it so bright for her that she is quite"
1448 "happy again. Grandmother herself told me this.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Which hymns are they, Heidi?\" asked the doctor."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I only know the one about the sun and the beautiful garden, and"
1448 "some of the verses of the long one, which are favorites with"
1448 "her, and she always likes me to read them to her two or three"
1448 "times over,\" replied Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well, say the verses to me then, I should like to hear them"
1448 "too,\" and the doctor sat up in order to listen better."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi put her hands together and sat collecting her thoughts for"
1448 "a second or two: \"Shall I begin at the verse that grandmother"
1448 "says gives her a feeling of hope and confidence?\""
1448 ""
1448 "The doctor nodded his assent, and Heidi began,--"
1448 ""
1448 "    Let not your heart be troubled"
1448 "    Nor fear your soul dismay,"
1448 "    There is a wise Defender"
1448 "    And He will be your stay."
1448 "    Where you have failed, He conquers,"
1448 "    See, how the foeman flies!"
1448 "    And all your tribulation"
1448 "    Is turned to glad surprise."
1448 ""
1448 "    If for a while it seemeth"
1448 "    His mercy is withdrawn,"
1448 "    That He no longer careth"
1448 "    For His wandering child forlorn,"
1448 "    Doubt not His great compassion,"
1448 "    His love can never tire,"
1448 "    To those who wait in patience"
1448 "    He gives their heart's desire."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi suddenly paused; she was not sure if the doctor was still"
1448 "listening. He was sitting motionless with his hand before his"
1448 "eyes. She thought he had fallen asleep; when he awoke, if he"
1448 "wanted to hear more verses, she would go on. There was no sound"
1448 "anywhere. The doctor sat in silence, but he was certainly not"
1448 "asleep. His thoughts had carried him back to a long past time:"
1448 "he saw himself as a little boy standing by his dear mother's"
1448 "chair; she had her arm round his neck and was saying the very"
1448 "verses to him that Heidi had just recited--words which he had not"
1448 "heard now for years. He could hear his mother's voice and see her"
1448 "loving eyes resting upon him, and as Heidi ceased the old dear"
1448 "voice seemed to be saying other things to him; and the words he"
1448 "heard again must have carried him far, far away, for it was a"
1448 "long time before he stirred or took his hand from his eyes. When"
1448 "at last he roused himself he met Heidi's eyes looking wonderingly"
1448 "at him."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Heidi,\" he said, taking the child's hand in his, \"that was a"
1448 "beautiful hymn of yours,\" and there was a happier ring in his"
1448 "voice as he spoke. \"We will come out here together another day,"
1448 "and you will let me hear it again.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter meanwhile had had enough to do in giving vent to his"
1448 "anger. It was now some days since Heidi had been out with him,"
1448 "and when at last she did come, there she sat the whole time"
1448 "beside the old gentleman, and Peter could not get a word with"
1448 "her. He got into a terrible temper, and at last went and stood"
1448 "some way back behind the doctor, where the latter could not see"
1448 "him, and doubling his fist made imaginary hits at the enemy."
1448 "Presently he doubled both fists, and the longer Heidi stayed"
1448 "beside the gentleman, the more fiercely did he threaten with"
1448 "them."
1448 ""
1448 "Meanwhile the sun had risen to the height which Peter knew"
1448 "pointed to the dinner hour. All of a sudden he called at the top"
1448 "of his voice, \"It's dinner time.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi was rising to fetch the dinner bag so that the doctor"
1448 "might eat his where he sat. But he stopped her, telling her he"
1448 "was not hungry at all, and only cared for a glass of milk, as he"
1448 "wanted to climb up a little higher. Then Heidi found that she"
1448 "also was not hungry and only wanted milk, and she should like,"
1448 "she said, to take the doctor up to the large moss-covered rock"
1448 "where Greenfinch had nearly jumped down and killed herself. So"
1448 "she ran and explained matters to Peter, telling him to go and get"
1448 "milk for the two. Peter seemed hardly to understand. \"Who is"
1448 "going to eat what is in the bag then?\" he asked."
1448 ""
1448 "\"You can have it,\" she answered, \"only first make haste and get"
1448 "the milk.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter had seldom performed any task more promptly, for he"
1448 "thought of the bag and its contents, which now belonged to him."
1448 "As soon as the other two were sitting quietly drinking their"
1448 "milk, he opened it, and quite trembled for joy at the sight of"
1448 "the meat, and he was just putting his hand in to draw it out when"
1448 "something seemed to hold him back. His conscience smote him at"
1448 "the remembrance of how he had stood with his doubled fists behind"
1448 "the doctor, who was now giving up to him his whole good dinner."
1448 "He felt as if he could not now enjoy it. But all at once he"
1448 "jumped up and ran back to the spot where he had stood before, and"
1448 "there held up his open hands as a sign that he had no longer any"
1448 "wish to use them as fists, and kept them up until he felt he had"
1448 "made amends for his past conduct. Then he rushed back and sat"
1448 "down to the double enjoyment of a clear conscience and an"
1448 "unusually satisfying meal."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi and the doctor climbed and talked for a long while, until"
1448 "the latter said it was time for him to be going back, and no"
1448 "doubt Heidi would like to go and be with her goats. But Heidi"
1448 "would not hear of this, as then the doctor would have to go the"
1448 "whole way down the mountain alone. She insisted on accompanying"
1448 "him as far as the grandfather's hut, or even a little further."
1448 "She kept hold of her friend's hand all the time, and the whole"
1448 "way she entertained him with accounts of this thing and that,"
1448 "showing him the spots where the goats loved best to feed, and"
1448 "others where in summer the flowers of all colors grew in"
1448 "greatest abundance. She could give them all their right names,"
1448 "for her grandfather had taught her these during the summer"
1448 "months. But at last the doctor insisted on her going back; so"
1448 "they bid each other good-night and the doctor continued his"
1448 "descent, turning now and again to look back, and each time he saw"
1448 "Heidi standing on the same spot and waving her hand to him. Even"
1448 "so in the old days had his own dear little daughter watched him"
1448 "when he went from home."
1448 ""
1448 "It was a bright sunny autumn month. The doctor came up to the"
1448 "hut every morning, and thence made excursions over the mountain."
1448 "Alm-Uncle accompanied him on some of his higher ascents, when"
1448 "they climbed up to the ancient storm-beaten fir trees and often"
1448 "disturbed the great bird which rose startled from its nest, with"
1448 "the whirl of wings and croakings, very near their heads. The"
1448 "doctor found great pleasure in his companion's conversation, and"
1448 "was astonished at his knowledge of the plants that grew on the"
1448 "mountain: he knew the uses of them all, from the aromatic fir"
1448 "trees and the dark pines with their scented needles, to the"
1448 "curly moss that sprang up everywhere about the roots of the trees"
1448 "and the smallest plant and tiniest flower. He was as well versed"
1448 "also in the ways of the animals, great and small, and had many"
1448 "amusing anecdotes to tell of these dwellers in caves and holes"
1448 "and in the tops of the fir trees. And so the time passed"
1448 "pleasantly and quickly for the doctor, who seldom said good-bye"
1448 "to the old man at the end of the day without adding, \"I never"
1448 "leave you, friend, without having learnt something new from you.\""
1448 ""
1448 "On some of the very finest days, however, the doctor would"
1448 "wander out again with Heidi, and then the two would sit together"
1448 "as on the first day, and the child would repeat her hymns and"
1448 "tell the doctor things which she alone knew. Peter sat at a"
1448 "little distance from them, but he was now quite reconciled in"
1448 "spirit and gave vent to no angry pantomime."
1448 ""
1448 "September had drawn to its close, and now one morning the doctor"
1448 "appeared looking less cheerful than usual. It was his last day,"
1448 "he said, as he must return to Frankfurt, but he was grieved at"
1448 "having to say good-bye to the mountain, which he had begun to"
1448 "feel quite like home. Alm-Uncle, on his side, greatly regretted"
1448 "the departure of his guest, and Heidi had been now accustomed"
1448 "for so long to see her good friend every day that she could"
1448 "hardly believe the time had suddenly come to separate. She looked"
1448 "up at him in doubt, taken by surprise, but there was no help, he"
1448 "must go. So he bid farewell to the old man and asked that Heidi"
1448 "might go with him part of the return way, and Heidi took his hand"
1448 "and went down the mountain with him, still unable to grasp the"
1448 "idea that he was going for good. After some distance the doctor"
1448 "stood still, and passing his hand over the child's curly head"
1448 "said, \"Now, Heidi, you must go back, and I must say good-bye! If"
1448 "only I could take you with me to Frankfurt and keep you there!\""
1448 ""
1448 "The picture of Frankfurt rose before the child's eyes, its rows"
1448 "of endless houses, its hard streets, and even the vision of"
1448 "Fraulein Rottenmeier and Tinette, and she answered hesitatingly,"
1448 "\"I would rather that you came back to us.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, you are right, that would be better. But now good-bye,"
1448 "Heidi.\" The child put her hand in his and looked up at him; the"
1448 "kind eyes looking down on her had tears in them. Then the doctor"
1448 "tore himself away and quickly continued his descent."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi remained standing without moving. The friendly eyes with"
1448 "the tears in them had gone to her heart. All at once she burst"
1448 "into tears and started running as fast as she could after the"
1448 "departing figure, calling out in broken tones: \"Doctor! doctor!\""
1448 ""
1448 "He turned round and waited till the child reached him. The tears"
1448 "were streaming down her face and she sobbed out: \"I will come to"
1448 "Frankfurt with you, now at once, and I will stay with you as"
1448 "long as you like, only I must just run back and tell"
1448 "grandfather.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The doctor laid his hand on her and tried to calm her"
1448 "excitement. \"No, no, dear child,\" he said kindly, \"not now; you"
1448 "must stay for the present under the fir trees, or I should have"
1448 "you ill again. But hear now what I have to ask you. If I am ever"
1448 "ill and alone, will you come then and stay with me? May I know"
1448 "that there would then be some one to look after me and care for"
1448 "me?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, yes, I will come the very day you send for me, and I love"
1448 "you nearly as much as grandfather,\" replied Heidi, who had not"
1448 "yet got over her distress."
1448 ""
1448 "And so the doctor again bid her good-bye and started on his way,"
1448 "while Heidi remained looking after him and waving her hand as"
1448 "long as a speck of him could be seen. As the doctor turned for"
1448 "the last time and looked back at the waving Heidi and the sunny"
1448 "mountain, he said to himself, \"It is good to be up there, good"
1448 "for body and soul, and a man might learn how to be happy once"
1448 "more.\""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER XVIII. WINTER IN DORFLI>"
1448 ""
1448 "The snow was lying so high around the hut that the windows"
1448 "looked level with the ground, and the door had entirely"
1448 "disappeared from view. If Alm-Uncle had been up there he would"
1448 "have had to do what Peter did daily, for fresh snow fell every"
1448 "night. Peter had to get out of the window of the sitting-room"
1448 "every morning, and if the frost had not been very hard during the"
1448 "night, he immediately sank up to his shoulders almost in the snow"
1448 "and had to struggle with hands, feet, and head to extricate"
1448 "himself. Then his mother handed him the large broom, and with"
1448 "this he worked hard to make a way to the door. He had to be"
1448 "careful to dig the snow well away, or else as soon as the door"
1448 "was opened the whole soft mass would fall inside, or, if the"
1448 "frost was severe enough, it would have made such a wall of ice in"
1448 "front of the house that no one could have gone in or out, for the"
1448 "window was only big enough for Peter to creep through. The fresh"
1448 "snow froze like this in the night sometimes, and this was an"
1448 "enjoyable time for Peter, for he would get through the window on"
1448 "to the hard, smooth, frozen ground, and his mother would hand him"
1448 "out the little sleigh, and he could then make his descent to"
1448 "Dorfli along any route he chose, for the whole mountain was"
1448 "nothing but one wide, unbroken sleigh road."
1448 ""
1448 "Alm-Uncle had kept his word and was not spending the winter in"
1448 "his old home. As soon as the first snow began to fall, he had"
1448 "shut up the hut and the outside buildings and gone down to"
1448 "Dorfli with Heidi and the goats. Near the church was a straggling"
1448 "half-ruined building, which had once been the house of a person"
1448 "of consequence. A distinguished soldier had lived there at one"
1448 "time; he had taken service in Spain and had there performed many"
1448 "brave deeds and gathered much treasure. When he returned home to"
1448 "Dorfli he spent part of his booty in building a fine house, with"
1448 "the intention of living in it. But he had been too long"
1448 "accustomed to the noise and bustle of arms and the world to care"
1448 "for a quiet country life, and he soon went off again, and this"
1448 "time did not return. When after many long years it seemed"
1448 "certain that he was dead, a distant relative took possession of"
1448 "the house, but it had already fallen into disrepair, and he had"
1448 "no wish to rebuild it. So it was let to poor people, who paid but"
1448 "a small rent, and when any part of the building fell it was"
1448 "allowed to remain. This had now gone on for many years. As long"
1448 "ago as when his son Tobias was a child Alm-Uncle had rented the"
1448 "tumble- down old place. Since then it had stood empty, for no one"
1448 "could stay in it who had not some idea of how to stop up the"
1448 "holes and gaps and make it habitable. Otherwise the wind and rain"
1448 "and snow blew into the rooms, so that it was impossible even to"
1448 "keep a candle alight, and the indwellers would have been frozen"
1448 "to death during the long cold winters. Alm-Uncle, however, knew"
1448 "how to mend matters. As soon as he made up his mind to spend the"
1448 "winter in Dorfli, he rented the old place and worked during the"
1448 "autumn to get it sound and tight. In the middle of October he and"
1448 "Heidi took up their residence there."
1448 ""
1448 "On approaching the house from the back one came first into an"
1448 "open space with a wall on either side, of which one was half in"
1448 "ruins. Above this rose the arch of an old window thickly"
1448 "overgrown with ivy, which spread over the remains of a domed"
1448 "roof that had evidently been part of a chapel. A large hall came"
1448 "next, which lay open, without doors, to the square outside. Here"
1448 "also walls and roof only partially remained, and indeed what was"
1448 "left of the roof looked as if it might fall at any minute had it"
1448 "not been for two stout pillars that supported it. Alm-Uncle had"
1448 "here put up a wooden partition and covered the floor with straw,"
1448 "for this was to be the goats' house. Endless passages led from"
1448 "this, through the rents of which the sky as well as the fields"
1448 "and the road outside could be seen at intervals; but at last one"
1448 "came to a stout oak door that led into a room that still stood"
1448 "intact. Here the walls and the dark wainscoting remained as good"
1448 "as ever, and in the corner was an immense stove reaching nearly"
1448 "to the ceiling, on the white tiles of which were painted large"
1448 "pictures in blue. These represented old castles surrounded with"
1448 "trees, and huntsmen riding out with their hounds; or else a quiet"
1448 "lake scene, with broad oak trees and a man fishing. A seat ran"
1448 "all round the stove so that one could sit at one's ease and study"
1448 "the pictures. These attracted Heidi's attention at once, and she"
1448 "had no sooner arrived with her grandfather than she ran and"
1448 "seated herself and began to examine them. But when she had"
1448 "gradually worked herself round to the back, something else"
1448 "diverted her attention. In the large space between the stove and"
1448 "the wall four planks had been put together as if to make a large"
1448 "receptacle for apples; there were no apples, however, inside, but"
1448 "something Heidi had no difficulty in recognising, for it was her"
1448 "very own bed, with its hay mattress and sheets, and sack for a"
1448 "coverlid, just as she had it up at the hut. Heidi clapped her"
1448 "hands for joy and exclaimed, \"O grandfather, this is my room, how"
1448 "nice! But where are you going to sleep?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Your room must be near the stove or you will freeze,\" he"
1448 "replied, \"but you can come and see mine too.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi got down and skipped across the large room after her"
1448 "grandfather, who opened a door at the farther end leading into a"
1448 "smaller one which was to be his bedroom. Then came another door."
1448 "Heidi pushed it open and stood amazed, for here was an immense"
1448 "room like a kitchen, larger than anything of the kind that Heidi"
1448 "had seen before. There was still plenty of work for the"
1448 "grandfather before this room could be finished, for there were"
1448 "holes and cracks in the walls through which the wind whistled,"
1448 "and yet he had already nailed up so many new planks that it"
1448 "looked as if a lot of small cupboards had been set up round the"
1448 "room. He had, however, made the large old door safe with many"
1448 "screws and nails, as a protection against the outside air, and"
1448 "this was very necessary, for just beyond was a mass of ruined"
1448 "buildings overgrown with tall weeds, which made a dwelling-place"
1448 "for endless beetles and lizards."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi was very delighted with her new home, and by the morning"
1448 "after their arrival she knew every nook and corner so thoroughly"
1448 "that she could take Peter over it and show him all that was to"
1448 "be seen; indeed she would not let him go till he had examined"
1448 "every single wonderful thing contained in it."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi slept soundly in her corner by the stove; but every"
1448 "morning when she first awoke she still thought she was on the"
1448 "mountain, and that she must run outside at once to see if the fir"
1448 "trees were so quiet because their branches were weighed down with"
1448 "the thick snow. She had to look about her for some minutes before"
1448 "she felt quite sure where she was, and a certain sensation of"
1448 "trouble and oppression would come over her as she grew aware that"
1448 "she was not at home in the hut. But then she would hear her"
1448 "grandfather's voice outside, attending to the goats, and these"
1448 "would give one or two loud bleats, as if calling to her to make"
1448 "haste and go to them, and then Heidi was happy again, for she"
1448 "knew she was still at home, and she would jump gladly out of bed"
1448 "and run out to the animals as quickly as she could. On the fourth"
1448 "morning, as soon as she saw her grandfather, she said, \"I must go"
1448 "up to see grandmother to-day; she ought not to be alone so long.\""
1448 ""
1448 "But the grandfather would not agree to this. \"Neither to-day nor"
1448 "to-morrow can you go,\" he said; \"the mountain is covered fathom-"
1448 "deep in snow, and the snow is still falling; the sturdy Peter can"
1448 "hardly get along. A little creature like you would soon be"
1448 "smothered by it, and we should not be able to find you again."
1448 "Wait a bit till it freezes, then you will be able to walk over"
1448 "the hard snow.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi did not like the thought of having to wait, but the days"
1448 "were so busy that she hardly knew how they went by."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi now went to school in Dorfli every morning and afternoon,"
1448 "and eagerly set to work to learn all that was taught her. She"
1448 "hardly ever saw Peter there, for as a rule he was absent. The"
1448 "teacher was an easy-going man who merely remarked now and then,"
1448 "\"Peter is not turning up to-day again, it seems, but there is a"
1448 "lot of snow up on the mountain and I daresay he cannot get"
1448 "along.\" Peter, however, always seemed able to make his way"
1448 "through the snow in the evening when school was over, and he"
1448 "then generally paid Heidi a visit."
1448 ""
1448 "At last, after some days, the sun again appeared and shone"
1448 "brightly over the white ground, but he went to bed again behind"
1448 "the mountains at a very early hour, as if he did not find such"
1448 "pleasure in looking down on the earth as when everything was"
1448 "green and flowery. But then the moon came out clear and large"
1448 "and lit up the great white snowfield all through the night, and"
1448 "the next morning the whole mountain glistened and sparkled like a"
1448 "huge crystal. When Peter got out of his window as usual, he was"
1448 "taken by surprise, for instead of sinking into the soft snow he"
1448 "fell on the hard ground and went sliding some way down the"
1448 "mountain side like a sleigh before he could stop himself. He"
1448 "picked himself up and tested the hardness of the ground by"
1448 "stamping on it and trying with all his might to dig his heels"
1448 "into it, but even then he could not break off a single little"
1448 "splinter of ice; the Alm was frozen hard as iron. This was just"
1448 "what Peter had been hoping for, as he knew now that Heidi would"
1448 "be able to come up to them. He quickly got back into the house,"
1448 "swallowed the milk which his mother had put ready for him,"
1448 "thrust a piece of bread in his pocket, and said, \"I must be off"
1448 "to school.\" \"That's right, go and learn all you can,\" said the"
1448 "grandmother encouragingly. Peter crept through the window again--"
1448 "the door was quite blocked by the frozen snow outside--pulling"
1448 "his little sleigh after him, and in another minute was shooting"
1448 "down the mountain."
1448 ""
1448 "He went like lightning, and when he reached Dorfli, which stood"
1448 "on the direct road to Mayenfeld, he made up his mind to go on"
1448 "further, for he was sure he could not stop his rapid descent"
1448 "without hurting himself and the sleigh too. So down he still"
1448 "went till he reached the level ground, where the sleigh came to a"
1448 "pause of its own accord. Then he got out and looked round. The"
1448 "impetus with which he had made his journey down had carried him"
1448 "some little way beyond Mayenfeld. He bethought himself that it"
1448 "was too late to get to school now, as lessons would already have"
1448 "begun, and it would take him a good hour to walk back to Dorfli."
1448 "So he might take his time about returning, which he did, and"
1448 "reached Dorfli just as Heidi had got home from school and was"
1448 "sitting at dinner with her grandfather. Peter walked in, and as"
1448 "on this occasion he had something particular to communicate, he"
1448 "began without a pause, exclaiming as he stood still in the"
1448 "middle of the room, \"She's got it now.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Got it? what?\" asked the Uncle. \"Your words sound quite"
1448 "warlike, general.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"The frost,\" explained Peter."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh! then now I can go and see grandmother!\" said Heidi"
1448 "joyfully, for she had understood Peter's words at once. \"But why"
1448 "were you not at school then? You could have come down in the"
1448 "sleigh,\" she added reproachfully, for it did not agree with"
1448 "Heidi's ideas of good behavior to stay away when it was possible"
1448 "to be there."
1448 ""
1448 "\"It carried me on too far and I was too late,\" Peter replied."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I call that being a deserter,\" said the Uncle, \"and deserters"
1448 "get their ears pulled, as you know.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter gave a tug to his cap in alarm, for there was no one of"
1448 "whom he stood in so much awe as Alm-Uncle."
1448 ""
1448 "\"And an army leader like yourself ought to be doubly ashamed of"
1448 "running away,\" continued Alm-Uncle. \"What would you think of"
1448 "your goats if one went off this way and another that, and refused"
1448 "to follow and do what was good for them? What would you do then?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I should beat them,\" said Peter promptly."
1448 ""
1448 "\"And if a boy behaved like these unruly goats, and he got a"
1448 "beating for it, what would you say then?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Serve him right,\" was the answer."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Good, then understand this: next time you let your sleigh carry"
1448 "you past the school when you ought to be inside at your lessons,"
1448 "come on to me afterwards and receive what you deserve.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter now understood the drift of the old man's questions and"
1448 "that he was the boy who behaved like the unruly goats, and he"
1448 "looked somewhat fearfully towards the corner to see if anything"
1448 "happened to be there such as he used himself on such occasions"
1448 "for the punishment of his animals."
1448 ""
1448 "But now the grandfather suddenly said in a cheerful voice, \"Come"
1448 "and sit down and have something, and afterwards Heidi shall go"
1448 "with you. Bring her back this evening and you will find supper"
1448 "waiting for you here.\""
1448 ""
1448 "This unexpected turn of conversation set Peter grinning all over"
1448 "with delight. He obeyed without hesitation and took his seat"
1448 "beside Heidi. But the child could not eat any more in her"
1448 "excitement at the thought of going to see grandmother. She"
1448 "pushed the potatoes and toasted cheese which still stood on her"
1448 "plate towards him while Uncle was filling his plate from the"
1448 "other side, so that he had quite a pile of food in front of him,"
1448 "but he attacked it without any lack of courage. Heidi ran to the"
1448 "cupboard and brought out the warm cloak Clara had sent her; with"
1448 "this on and the hood drawn over her head, she was all ready for"
1448 "her journey. She stood waiting beside Peter, and as soon as his"
1448 "last mouthful had disappeared she said, \"Come along now.\" As the"
1448 "two walked together Heidi had much to tell Peter of her two"
1448 "goats that had been so unhappy the first day in their new stall"
1448 "that they would not eat anything, but stood hanging their heads,"
1448 "not even rousing themselves to bleat. And when she asked her"
1448 "grandfather the reason of this, he told her it was with them as"
1448 "with her in Frankfurt, for it was the first time in their lives"
1448 "they had come down from the mountain. \"And you don't know what"
1448 "that is, Peter, unless you have felt it yourself,\" added Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "The children had nearly reached their destination before Peter"
1448 "opened his mouth; he appeared to be so sunk in thought that he"
1448 "hardly heard what was said to him. As they neared home, however,"
1448 "he stood still and said in a somewhat sullen voice, \"I had"
1448 "rather go to school even than get what Uncle threatened.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi was of the same mind, and encouraged him in his good"
1448 "intention. They found Brigitta sitting alone knitting, for the"
1448 "grandmother was not very well and had to stay the day in bed on"
1448 "account of the cold. Heidi had never before missed the old"
1448 "figure in her place in the corner, and she ran quickly into the"
1448 "next room. There lay grandmother on her little poorly covered"
1448 "bed, wrapped up in her warm grey shawl."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Thank God,\" she exclaimed as Heidi came running in; the poor"
1448 "old woman had had a secret fear at heart all through the autumn,"
1448 "especially if Heidi was absent for any length of time, for Peter"
1448 "had told her of a strange gentleman who had come from Frankfurt,"
1448 "and who had gone out with them and always talked to Heidi, and"
1448 "she had felt sure he had come to take her away again. Even when"
1448 "she heard he had gone off alone, she still had an idea that a"
1448 "messenger would be sent over from Frankfurt to fetch the child."
1448 "Heidi went up to the side of the bed and said, \"Are you very"
1448 "ill, grandmother?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"No, no, child,\" answered the old woman reassuringly, passing"
1448 "her hand lovingly over the child's head, \"It's only the frost"
1448 "that has got into my bones a bit.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Shall you be quite well then directly it turns warm again?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, God willing, or even before that, for I want to get back"
1448 "to my spinning; I thought perhaps I should do a little to-day,"
1448 "but to-morrow I am sure to be all right again.\" The old woman had"
1448 "detected that Heidi was frightened and was anxious to set her"
1448 "mind at ease."
1448 ""
1448 "Her words comforted Heidi, who had in truth been greatly"
1448 "distressed, for she had never before seen the grandmother ill in"
1448 "bed. She now looked at the old woman seriously for a minute or"
1448 "two, and then said, \"In Frankfurt everybody puts on a shawl to"
1448 "go out walking; did you think it was to be worn in bed,"
1448 "grandmother?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I put it on, dear child, to keep myself from freezing, and I am"
1448 "so pleased with it, for my bedclothes are not very thick,\" she"
1448 "answered."
1448 ""
1448 "\"But, grandmother,\" continued Heidi, \"your bed is not right,"
1448 "because it goes downhill at your head instead of uphill.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I know it, child, I can feel it,\" and the grandmother put up"
1448 "her hand to the thin flat pillow, which was little more than a"
1448 "board under her head, to make herself more comfortable; \"the"
1448 "pillow was never very thick, and I have lain on it now for so"
1448 "many years that it has grown quite flat.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh, if only I had asked Clara to let me take away my Frankfurt"
1448 "bed,\" said Heidi. \"I had three large pillows, one above the"
1448 "other, so that I could hardly sleep, and I used to slip down to"
1448 "try and find a flat place, and then I had to pull myself up"
1448 "again, because it was proper to sleep there like that. Could you"
1448 "sleep like that, grandmother?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh, yes! the pillows keep one warm, and it is easier to breathe"
1448 "when the head is high,\" answered the grandmother, wearily"
1448 "raising her head as she spoke as if trying to find a higher"
1448 "resting-place. \"But we will not talk about that, for I have so"
1448 "much that other old sick people are without for which I thank"
1448 "God; there is the nice bread I get every day, and this warm"
1448 "wrap, and your visits, Heidi. Will you read me something to-day?\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi ran into the next room to fetch the hymn book. Then she"
1448 "picked out the favorite hymns one after another, for she knew"
1448 "them all by heart now, as pleased as the grandmother to hear"
1448 "them again after so many days. The grandmother lay with folded"
1448 "hands, while a smile of peace stole over the worn, troubled face,"
1448 "like one to whom good news has been brought."
1448 ""
1448 "Suddenly Heidi paused. \"Grandmother, are you feeling quite well"
1448 "again already?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, child, I have grown better while listening to you; read it"
1448 "to the end.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The child read on, and when she came to the last words:--"
1448 ""
1448 "As the eyes grow dim, and darkness Closes round, the soul grows"
1448 "clearer,  Sees the goal to which it travels,  Gladly feels its"
1448 "home is nearer.\""
1448 ""
1448 "the grandmother repeated them once or twice to herself, with a"
1448 "look of happy expectation on her face. And Heidi took equal"
1448 "pleasure in them, for the picture of the beautiful sunny day of"
1448 "her return home rose before her eyes, and she exclaimed"
1448 "joyfully, \"Grandmother, I know exactly what it is like to go"
1448 "home.\" The old woman did not answer, but she had heard Heidi's"
1448 "words, and the expression that had made the child think she was"
1448 "better remained on her face."
1448 ""
1448 "A little later Heidi said, \"It is growing dark and I must go"
1448 "home; I am glad to think, that you are quite well again.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The grandmother took the child's hand in hers and held it"
1448 "closely. \"Yes,\" she said, \"I feel quite happy again; even if I"
1448 "have to go on lying here, I am content. No one knows what it is"
1448 "to lie here alone day after day, in silence and darkness,"
1448 "without hearing a voice or seeing a ray of light. Sad thoughts"
1448 "come over me, and I do not feel sometimes as if I could bear it"
1448 "any longer or as if it could ever be light again. But when you"
1448 "come and read those words to me, then I am comforted and my heart"
1448 "rejoices once more.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Then she let the child go, and Heidi ran into the next room, and"
1448 "bid Peter come quickly, for it had now grown quite dark. But"
1448 "when they got outside they found the moon shining down on the"
1448 "white snow and everything as clear as in the daylight. Peter got"
1448 "his sleigh, put Heidi at the back, he himself sitting in front to"
1448 "guide, and down the mountain they shot like two birds darting"
1448 "through the air."
1448 ""
1448 "When Heidi was lying that night on her high bed of hay she"
1448 "thought of the grandmother on her low pillow, and of all she had"
1448 "said about the light and comfort that awoke in her when she"
1448 "heard the hymns, and she thought: if I could read to her every"
1448 "day, then I should go on making her better. But she knew that it"
1448 "would be a week, if not two, before she would be able to go up"
1448 "the mountain again. This was a thought of great trouble to Heidi,"
1448 "and she tried hard to think of some way which would enable the"
1448 "grandmother to hear the words she loved every day. Suddenly an"
1448 "idea struck her, and she was so delighted with it that she could"
1448 "hardly bear to wait for morning, so eager was she to begin"
1448 "carrying out her plan. All at once she sat upright in her bed,"
1448 "for she had been so busy with her thoughts that she had"
1448 "forgotten to say her prayers, and she never now finished her day"
1448 "without saying them."
1448 ""
1448 "When she had prayed with all her heart for herself, her"
1448 "grandfather and grandmother, she lay back again on the warm soft"
1448 "hay and slept soundly and peacefully till morning broke."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER XIX. THE WINTER CONTINUES>"
1448 ""
1448 "Peter arrived punctually at school the following day. He had"
1448 "brought his dinner with him, for all the children who lived at a"
1448 "distance regularly seated themselves at mid-day on the tables,"
1448 "and resting their feet firmly on the benches, spread out their"
1448 "meal on their knees and so ate their dinner, while those living"
1448 "in Dorfli went home for theirs. Till one o'clock they might all"
1448 "do as they liked, and then school began again. When Peter had"
1448 "finished his lessons on the days he attended school, he went"
1448 "over to Uncle's to see Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "When he walked into the large room at Uncle's to-day, Heidi"
1448 "immediately rushed forward and took hold of him, for it was for"
1448 "Peter she had been waiting. \"I've thought of something, Peter,\""
1448 "she said hastily."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What is it?\" he asked."
1448 ""
1448 "\"You must learn to read,\" she informed him."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I have learnt,\" was the answer."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, yes, but I mean so that you can really make use of it,\""
1448 "continued Heidi eagerly."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I never shall,\" was the prompt reply."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Nobody believes that you cannot learn, nor I either now,\" said"
1448 "Heidi in a very decided tone of voice. \"Grandmamma in Frankfurt"
1448 "said long ago that it was not true, and she told me not to"
1448 "believe you.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter looked rather taken aback at this piece of intelligence."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I will soon teach you to read, for I know how,\" continued"
1448 "Heidi. \"You must learn at once, and then you can read one or two"
1448 "hymns every day to grandmother.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh, I don't care about that,\" he grumbled in reply."
1448 ""
1448 "This hard-hearted way of refusing to agree to what was right and"
1448 "kind, and to what Heidi had so much at heart, aroused her anger."
1448 "With flashing eyes she stood facing the boy and said"
1448 "threateningly, \"If you won't learn as I want you to, I will tell"
1448 "you what will happen; you know your mother has often spoken of"
1448 "sending you to Frankfurt, that you may learn a lot of things,"
1448 "and I know where the boys there have to go to school; Clara"
1448 "pointed out the great house to me when we were driving together."
1448 "And they don't only go when they are boys, but have more lessons"
1448 "still when they are grown men. I have seen them myself, and you"
1448 "mustn't think they have only one kind teacher like we have. There"
1448 "are ever so many of them, all in the school at the same time, and"
1448 "they are all dressed in black, as if they were going to church,"
1448 "and have black hats on their heads as high as that--\" and Heidi"
1448 "held out her hand to show their height from the floor."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter felt a cold shudder run down his back."
1448 ""
1448 "\"And you will have to go in among all those gentlemen,\""
1448 "continued Heidi with increasing animation, \"and when it comes to"
1448 "your turn you won't be able to read and will make mistakes in"
1448 "your spelling. Then you'll see how they'll make fun of you; even"
1448 "worse than Tinette, and you ought to have seen what she was like"
1448 "when she was scornful.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well, I'll learn then,\" said Peter, half sorrowfully and half"
1448 "angrily."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi was instantly mollified. \"That's right, then we'll begin"
1448 "at once,\" she said cheerfully, and went busily to work on the"
1448 "spot, dragging Peter to the table and fetching her books."
1448 ""
1448 "Among other presents Clara had sent Heidi a book which the"
1448 "latter had decided, in bed the night before, would serve"
1448 "capitally for teaching Peter, for it was an A B C book with"
1448 "rhyming lines. And now the two sat together at the table with"
1448 "their heads bent over the book, for the lesson had begun."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter was made to spell out the first sentence two or three"
1448 "times over, for Heidi wished him to get it correct and fluent. At"
1448 "last she said, \"You don't seem able to get it right, but I will"
1448 "read it aloud to you once; when you know what it ought to be you"
1448 "will find it easier.\" And she read out:--"
1448 ""
1448 "          A B C must be learnt to-day"
1448 "           Or the judge will call you up to pay."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I shan't go,\" said Peter obstinately."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Go where?\" asked Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Before the judge,\" he answered."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well then make haste and learn these three letters, then you"
1448 "won't have to go.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter went at his task again and repeated the three letters so"
1448 "many times and with such determination that she said at last,--"
1448 ""
1448 "\"You must know those three now.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Seeing what an effect the first two lines of verse had had upon"
1448 "him, she thought she would prepare the ground a little for the"
1448 "following lessons."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Wait, and I will read you some of the next sentences,\" she"
1448 "continued, \"then you will see what else there is to expect.\""
1448 ""
1448 "And she began in a clear slow voice:--"
1448 ""
1448 "          D E F G must run with ease"
1448 "           Or something will follow that does not please."
1448 ""
1448 "          Should H I J K be now forgot"
1448 "           Disgrace is yours upon the spot."
1448 ""
1448 "          And then L M must follow at once"
1448 "           Or punished you'll be for a sorry dunce."
1448 ""
1448 "          If you knew what next awaited you"
1448 "           You'd haste to learn N O P Q."
1448 ""
1448 "          Now R S T be quick about"
1448 "           Or worse will follow there's little doubt."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi paused, for Peter was so quiet that she looked to see what"
1448 "he was doing. These many secret threats and hints of dreadful"
1448 "punishments had so affected him that he sat as if petrified and"
1448 "stared at Heidi with horror-stricken eyes. Her kind heart was"
1448 "moved at once, and she said, wishing to reassure him, \"You need"
1448 "not be afraid, Peter; come here to me every evening, and if you"
1448 "learn as you have to-day you will at last know all your letters,"
1448 "and the other things won't come. But you must come regularly,"
1448 "not now and then as you do to school; even if it snows it won't"
1448 "hurt you.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter promised, for the trepidation he had been in had made him"
1448 "quite tame and docile. Lessons being finished for this day he"
1448 "now went home."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter obeyed Heidi's instructions punctually, and every evening"
1448 "went diligently to work to learn the following letters, taking"
1448 "the sentences thoroughly to heart. The grandfather was"
1448 "frequently in the room smoking his pipe comfortably while the"
1448 "lesson was going on, and his face twitched occasionally as if he"
1448 "was overtaken with a sudden fit of merriment. Peter was often"
1448 "invited to stay to supper after the great exertion he had gone"
1448 "through, which richly compensated him for the anguish of mind he"
1448 "had suffered with the sentence for the day."
1448 ""
1448 "So the winter went by, and Peter really made progress with his"
1448 "letters; but he went through a terrible fight each day with the"
1448 "sentences."
1448 ""
1448 "He had got at last to U. Heidi read out:--"
1448 ""
1448 "          And if you put the U for V,"
1448 "           You'll go where you would not like to be."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter growled, \"Yes, but I shan't go!\" But he was very diligent"
1448 "that day, as if under the impression that some one would seize"
1448 "him suddenly by the collar and drag him where he would rather"
1448 "not go. The next evening Heidi read:--"
1448 ""
1448 "          If you falter at W, worst of all,"
1448 "           Look at the stick against the wall."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter looked at the wall and said scornfully, \"There isn't one.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, but do you know what grandfather has in his box?\" asked"
1448 "Heidi. \"A stick as thick almost as your arm, and if he took that"
1448 "out, you might well say, look at the stick on the wall.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter knew that thick hazel stick, and immediately bent his head"
1448 "over the W and struggled to master it. Another day the lines ran:--"
1448 ""
1448 "          Then comes the X for you to say"
1448 "           Or be sure you'll get no food to-day."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter looked towards the cupboard where the bread and cheese"
1448 "were kept and said crossly, \"I never said that I should forget"
1448 "the X.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"That's all right; if you don't forget it we can go on to learn"
1448 "the next, and then you will only have one more,\" replied Heidi,"
1448 "anxious to encourage him."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter did not quite understand, but when Heidi went on and read:--"
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "          And should you make a stop at Y,"
1448 "           They'll point at you and cry, Fie, fie."
1448 ""
1448 "All the gentlemen in Frankfurt with tall black hats on their"
1448 "heads, and scorn and mockery in their faces rose up before his"
1448 "mind's eye, and he threw himself with energy on the Y, not"
1448 "letting it go till at last he knew it so thoroughly that he"
1448 "could see what it was like even when he shut his eyes."
1448 ""
1448 "He arrived on the following day in a somewhat lofty frame of"
1448 "mind, for there was now only one letter to struggle over, and"
1448 "when Heidi began the lesson with reading aloud:--"
1448 ""
1448 "          Make haste with Z, if you're too slow"
1448 "           Off to the Hottentots you'll go."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter remarked scornfully, \"I dare say, when no one knows even"
1448 "where such people live.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I assure you, Peter,\" replied Heidi, \"grandfather knows all"
1448 "about them. Wait a second and I will run and ask him, for he is"
1448 "only over the way with the pastor.\" And she rose and ran to the"
1448 "door to put her words into action, but Peter cried out in a"
1448 "voice of agony,--"
1448 ""
1448 "\"Stop!\" for he already saw himself being carried off by Alm-"
1448 "Uncle and the pastor and sent straight away to the Hottentots,"
1448 "since as yet he did not know his last letter. His cry of fear"
1448 "brought Heidi back."
1448 ""
1448 "\"What is the matter?\" she asked in astonishment."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Nothing! come back! I am going to learn my letter,\" he said,"
1448 "stammering with fear. Heidi, however, herself wished to know"
1448 "where the Hottentots lived and persisted that she should ask her"
1448 "grandfather, but she gave in at last to Peter's despairing"
1448 "entreaties. She insisted on his doing something in return, and"
1448 "so not only had he to repeat his Z until it was so fixed in his"
1448 "memory that he could never forget it again, but she began"
1448 "teaching him to spell, and Peter really made a good start that"
1448 "evening. So it went on from day to day."
1448 ""
1448 "The frost had gone and the snow was soft again, and moreover"
1448 "fresh snow continually fell, so that it was quite three weeks"
1448 "before Heidi could go to the grandmother again. So much the more"
1448 "eagerly did she pursue her teaching so that Peter might"
1448 "compensate for her absence by reading hymns to the old woman."
1448 "One evening he walked in home after leaving Heidi, and as he"
1448 "entered he said, \"I can do it now.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Do what, Peter?\" asked his mother."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Read,\" he answered."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Do you really mean it? Did you hear that, grandmother?\" she"
1448 "called out."
1448 ""
1448 "The grandmother had heard, and was already wondering how such a"
1448 "thing could have come to pass."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I must read one of the hymns now; Heidi told me to,\" he went on"
1448 "to inform them. His mother hastily fetched the book, and the"
1448 "grandmother lay in joyful expectation, for it was so long since"
1448 "she had heard the good words. Peter sat down to the table and"
1448 "began to read. His mother sat beside him listening with surprise"
1448 "and exclaiming at the close of each verse, \"Who would have"
1448 "thought it possible!\""
1448 ""
1448 "The grandmother did not speak though she followed the words he"
1448 "read with strained attention."
1448 ""
1448 "It happened on the day following this that there was a reading"
1448 "lesson in Peter's class. When it came to his turn, the teacher"
1448 "said,--"
1448 ""
1448 "\"We must pass over Peter as usual, or will you try again once"
1448 "more--I will not say to read, but to stammer through a"
1448 "sentence.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter took the book and read off three lines without the"
1448 "slightest hesitation."
1448 ""
1448 "The teacher put down his book and stared at Peter as at some out-"
1448 "of-the-way and marvellous thing unseen before. At last he spoke,--"
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Peter, some miracle has been performed upon you! Here have I"
1448 "been striving with unheard-of patience to teach you and you have"
1448 "not hitherto been able to say your letters even. And now, just"
1448 "as I had made up my mind not to waste any more trouble upon you,"
1448 "you suddenly are able to read a consecutive sentence properly and"
1448 "distinctly. How has such a miracle come to pass in our days?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"It was Heidi,\" answered Peter."
1448 ""
1448 "The teacher looked in astonishment towards Heidi, who was"
1448 "sitting innocently on her bench with no appearance of anything"
1448 "supernatural about her. He continued, \"I have noticed a change"
1448 "in you altogether, Peter. Whereas formerly you often missed"
1448 "coming to school for a week, or even weeks at a time, you have"
1448 "lately not stayed away a single day. Who has wrought this change"
1448 "for good in you?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"It was Uncle,\" answered Peter."
1448 ""
1448 "With increasing surprise the teacher looked from Peter to Heidi"
1448 "and back again at Peter."
1448 ""
1448 "\"We will try once more,\" he said cautiously, and Peter had again"
1448 "to show off his accomplishment by reading another three lines."
1448 "There was no mistake about it--Peter could read. As soon as"
1448 "school was over the teacher went over to the pastor to tell him"
1448 "this piece of news, and to inform him of the happy result of"
1448 "Heidi's and the grandfather's combined efforts."
1448 ""
1448 "Every evening Peter read one hymn aloud; so far he obeyed Heidi."
1448 "Nothing would induce him to read a second, and indeed the"
1448 "grandmother never asked for it. His mother Brigitta could not"
1448 "get over her surprise at her son's attainment, and when the"
1448 "reader was in bed would often express her pleasure at it. \"Now he"
1448 "has learnt to read there is no knowing what may be made of him"
1448 "yet.\""
1448 ""
1448 "On one of these occasions the grandmother answered, \"Yes, it is"
1448 "good for him to have learnt something, but I shall indeed be"
1448 "thankful when spring is here again and Heidi can come; they are"
1448 "not like the same hymns when Peter reads them. So many words"
1448 "seem missing, and I try to think what they ought to be and then I"
1448 "lose the sense, and so the hymns do not come home to my heart as"
1448 "when Heidi reads them.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The truth was that Peter arranged to make his reading as little"
1448 "troublesome for himself as possible. When he came upon a word"
1448 "that he thought was too long or difficult in any other way, he"
1448 "left it out, for he decided that a word or two less in a verse,"
1448 "where there were so many of them, could make no difference to"
1448 "his grandmother. And so it came about that most of the principal"
1448 "words were missing in the hymns that Peter read aloud."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER XX. NEWS FROM DISTANT FRIENDS>"
1448 ""
1448 "It was the month of May. From every height the full fresh"
1448 "streams of spring were flowing down into the valley. The clear"
1448 "warm sunshine lay upon the mountain, which had turned green"
1448 "again. The last snows had disappeared and the sun had already"
1448 "coaxed many of the flowers to show their bright heads above the"
1448 "grass. Up above the gay young wind of spring was singing through"
1448 "the fir trees, and shaking down the old dark needles to make room"
1448 "for the new bright green ones that were soon to deck out the"
1448 "trees in their spring finery. Higher up still the great bird went"
1448 "circling round in the blue ether as of old, while the golden"
1448 "sunshine lit up the grandfather's hut, and all the ground about"
1448 "it was warm and dry again so that one might sit out where one"
1448 "liked. Heidi was at home again on the mountain, running backwards"
1448 "and forwards in her accustomed way, not knowing which spot was"
1448 "most delightful. Now she stood still to listen to the deep,"
1448 "mysterious voice of the wind, as it blew down to her from the"
1448 "mountain summits, coming nearer and nearer and gathering strength"
1448 "as it came, till it broke with force against the fir trees,"
1448 "bending and shaking them, and seeming to shout for joy, so that"
1448 "she too, though blown about like a feather, felt she must join in"
1448 "the chorus of exulting sounds. Then she would run round again to"
1448 "the sunny space in front of the hut, and seating herself on the"
1448 "ground would peer closely into the short grass to see how many"
1448 "little flower cups were open or thinking of opening. She rejoiced"
1448 "with all the myriad little beetles and winged insects that jumped"
1448 "and crawled and danced in the sun, and drew in deep draughts of"
1448 "the spring scents that rose from the newly-awakened earth, and"
1448 "thought the mountain was more beautiful than ever. All the tiny"
1448 "living creatures must be as happy as she, for it seemed to her"
1448 "there were little voices all round her singing and humming in"
1448 "joyful tones, \"On the mountain! on the mountain!\""
1448 ""
1448 "From the shed at the back came the sound of sawing and chopping,"
1448 "and Heidi listened to it with pleasure, for it was the old"
1448 "familiar sound she had known from the beginning of her life up"
1448 "here. Suddenly she jumped up and ran round, for she must know"
1448 "what her grandfather was doing. In front of the shed door"
1448 "already stood a finished new chair, and a second was in course of"
1448 "construction under the grandfather's skilful hand."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh, I know what these are for,\" exclaimed Heidi in great glee."
1448 "\"We shall want them when they all come from Frankfurt. This one"
1448 "is for Grandmamma, and the one you are now making is for Clara,"
1448 "and then--then, there will, I suppose, have to be another,\""
1448 "continued Heidi with more hesitation in her voice, \"or do you"
1448 "think, grandfather, that perhaps Fraulein Rottenmeier will not"
1448 "come with them?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well, I cannot say just yet,\" replied her grandfather, \"but it"
1448 "will be safer to make one so that we can offer her a seat if she"
1448 "does.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi looked thoughtfully at the plain wooden chair without arms"
1448 "as if trying to imagine how Fraulein Rottenmeier and a chair of"
1448 "this sort would suit one another. After a few minutes'"
1448 "contemplation, \"Grandfather,\" she said, shaking her head"
1448 "doubtfully, \"I don't think she would be able to sit on that.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Then we will invite her on the couch with the beautiful green"
1448 "turf feather-bed,\" was her grandfather's quiet rejoinder."
1448 ""
1448 "While Heidi was pausing to consider what this might be there"
1448 "approached from above a whistling, calling, and other sounds"
1448 "which Heidi immediately recognised. She ran out and found"
1448 "herself surrounded by her four-footed friends. They were"
1448 "apparently as pleased as she was to be among the heights again,"
1448 "for they leaped about and bleated for joy, pushing Heidi this way"
1448 "and that, each anxious to express his delight with some sign of"
1448 "affection. But Peter sent them flying to right and left, for he"
1448 "had something to give to Heidi. When he at last got up to her he"
1448 "handed her a letter."
1448 ""
1448 "\"There!\" he exclaimed, leaving the further explanation of the"
1448 "matter to Heidi herself."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Did some one give you this while you were out with the goats,\""
1448 "she asked, in her surprise."
1448 ""
1448 "\"No,\" was the answer."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Where did you get it from then?"
1448 ""
1448 "\"I found it in the dinner bag.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Which was true to a certain extent. The letter to Heidi had been"
1448 "given him the evening before by the postman at Dorfli, and Peter"
1448 "had put it into his empty bag. That morning he had stuffed his"
1448 "bread and cheese on the top of it, and had forgotten it when he"
1448 "fetched Alm-Uncle's two goats; only when he had finished his"
1448 "bread and cheese at mid-day and was searching in the bag for any"
1448 "last crumbs did he remember the letter which lay at the bottom."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi read the address carefully; then she ran back to the shed"
1448 "holding out her letter to her grandfather in high glee. \"From"
1448 "Frankfurt! from Clara! Would you like to hear it?\""
1448 ""
1448 "The grandfather was ready and pleased to do so, as also Peter,"
1448 "who had followed Heidi into the shed. He leant his back against"
1448 "the door post, as he felt he could follow Heidi's reading better"
1448 "if firmly supported from behind, and so stood prepared to"
1448 "listen."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Dearest Heidi,-- Everything is packed and we shall start now in"
1448 "two or three days, as soon as papa himself is ready to leave; he"
1448 "is not coming with us as he has first to go to Paris. The doctor"
1448 "comes every day, and as soon as he is inside the door, he cries,"
1448 "'Off now as quickly as you can, off to the mountain.' He is most"
1448 "impatient about our going. You cannot think how much he enjoyed"
1448 "himself when he was with you! He has called nearly every day"
1448 "this winter, and each time he has come in to my room and said he"
1448 "must tell me about everything again. And then he sits down and"
1448 "describes all he did with you and the grandfather, and talks of"
1448 "the mountains and the flowers and of the great silence up there"
1448 "far above all towns and the villages, and of the fresh delicious"
1448 "air, and often adds, 'No one can help getting well up there.' He"
1448 "himself is quite a different man since his visit, and looks"
1448 "quite young again and happy, which he had not been for a long"
1448 "time before. Oh, how I am looking forward to seeing everything"
1448 "and to being with you on the mountain, and to making the"
1448 "acquaintance of Peter and the goats."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I shall have first to go through a six weeks' cure at Ragatz;"
1448 "this the doctor has ordered, and then we shall move up to"
1448 "Dorfli, and every fine day I shall be carried up the mountain in"
1448 "my chair and spend the day with you. Grandmamma is travelling"
1448 "with me and will remain with me; she also is delighted at the"
1448 "thought of paying you a visit. But just imagine, Fraulein"
1448 "Rottenmeier refuses to come with us. Almost every day grandmamma"
1448 "says to her, 'Well, how about this Swiss journey, my worthy"
1448 "Rottenmeier? Pray say if you really would like to come with us.'"
1448 "But she always thanks grandmamma very politely and says she has"
1448 "quite made up her mind. I think I know what has done it:"
1448 "Sebastian gave such a frightful description of the mountain, of"
1448 "how the rocks were so overhanging and dangerous that at any"
1448 "minute you might fall into a crevasse, and how it was such steep"
1448 "climbing that you feared at every step to go slipping to the"
1448 "bottom, and that goats alone could make their way up without fear"
1448 "of being killed. She shuddered when she heard him tell of all"
1448 "this, and since then she has not been so enthusiastic about"
1448 "Switzerland as she was before. Fear has also taken possession of"
1448 "Tinette, and she also refuses to come. So grandmamma and I will"
1448 "be alone; Sebastian will go with us as far as Ragatz and then"
1448 "return here."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I can hardly bear waiting till I see you again. Good-bye,"
1448 "dearest Heidi; grandmamma sends you her best love and all good"
1448 "wishes.--Your affectionate friend,"
1448 "                                 \"Clara.\""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter, as soon as the conclusion of the letter had been reached,"
1448 "left his reclining position and rushed out, twirling his stick"
1448 "in the air in such a reckless fashion that the frightened goats"
1448 "fled down the mountain before him with higher and wider leaps"
1448 "than usual. Peter followed at full speed, his stick still raised"
1448 "in air in a menacing manner as if he was longing to vent his fury"
1448 "on some invisible foe. This foe was indeed the prospect of the"
1448 "arrival of the Frankfurt visitors, the thought of whom filled"
1448 "him with exasperation."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi was so full of joyful anticipation that she determined to"
1448 "seize the first possible moment next day to go down and tell"
1448 "grandmother who was coming, and also particularly who was not"
1448 "coming. These details would be of great interest to her, for"
1448 "grandmother knew well all the persons named from Heidi's"
1448 "description, and had entered with deep sympathy into all that"
1448 "the child had told her of her life and surroundings in Frankfurt."
1448 "Heidi paid her visit in the early afternoon, for she could now go"
1448 "alone again; the sun was bright in the heavens and the days were"
1448 "growing longer, and it was delightful to go racing down the"
1448 "mountain over the dry ground, with the brisk May wind blowing"
1448 "from behind, and speeding Heidi on her way a little more quickly"
1448 "than her legs alone would have carried her."
1448 ""
1448 "The grandmother was no longer confined to her bed. She was back"
1448 "in her corner at her spinning-wheel, but there was an expression"
1448 "on her face of mournful anxiety. Peter had come in the evening"
1448 "before brimful of anger and had told about the large party who"
1448 "were coming up from Frankfurt, and he did not know what other"
1448 "things might happen after that; and the old woman had not slept"
1448 "all night, pursued by the old thought of Heidi being taken from"
1448 "her. Heidi ran in, and taking her little stool immediately sat"
1448 "down by grandmother and began eagerly pouring out all her news,"
1448 "growing more excited with her pleasure as she went on. But all"
1448 "of a sudden she stopped short and said anxiously, \"What is the"
1448 "matter, grandmother, aren't you a bit pleased with what I am"
1448 "telling you?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, yes, of course, child, since it gives you so much"
1448 "pleasure,\" she answered, trying to look more cheerful."
1448 ""
1448 "\"But I can see all the same that something troubles you. Is it"
1448 "because you think after all that Fraulein Rottenmeier may come?\""
1448 "asked Heidi, beginning to feel anxious herself."
1448 ""
1448 "\"No, no! it is nothing, child,\" said the grandmother, wishing to"
1448 "reassure her. \"Just give me your hand that I may feel sure you"
1448 "are there. No doubt it would be the best thing for you, although"
1448 "I feel I could scarcely survive it.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I do not want anything of the best if you could scarcely"
1448 "survive it,\" said Heidi, in such a determined tone of voice that"
1448 "the grandmother's fears increased as she felt sure the people"
1448 "from Frankfurt were coming to take Heidi back with them, since"
1448 "now she was well again they naturally wished to have her with"
1448 "them once more. But she was anxious to hide her trouble from"
1448 "Heidi if possible, as the latter was so sympathetic that she"
1448 "might refuse perhaps to go away, and that would not be right. She"
1448 "sought for help, but not for long, for she knew of only one."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Heidi,\" she said, \"there is something that would comfort me and"
1448 "calm my thoughts; read me the hymn beginning: 'All things will"
1448 "work for good.'\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi found the place at once and read out in her clear young"
1448 "voice:--"
1448 ""
1448 "          All things will work for good"
1448 "          To those who trust in Me;"
1448 "          I come with healing on my wings,"
1448 "          To save and set thee free."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, yes, that is just what I wanted to hear,\" said the"
1448 "grandmother, and the deep expression of trouble passed from her"
1448 "face. Heidi looked at her thoughtfully for a minute or two and"
1448 "then said, \"Healing means that which cures everything and makes"
1448 "everybody well, doesn't it, grandmother?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, that is it,\" replied the old woman with a nod of assent,"
1448 "\"and we may be sure everything will come to pass according to"
1448 "God's good purpose. Read the verse again, that we may remember"
1448 "it well and not forget it again.\""
1448 ""
1448 "And Heidi read the words over two or three times, for she also"
1448 "found pleasure in this assurance of all things being arranged"
1448 "for the best."
1448 ""
1448 "When the evening came, Heidi returned home up the mountain. The"
1448 "stars came out overhead one by one, so bright and sparkling that"
1448 "each seemed to send a fresh ray of joy into her heart; she was"
1448 "obliged to pause continually to look up, and as the whole sky at"
1448 "last grew spangled with them she spoke aloud, \"Yes, I understand"
1448 "now why we feel so happy, and are not afraid about anything,"
1448 "because God knows what is good and beautiful for us.\" And the"
1448 "stars with their glistening eyes continued to nod to her till"
1448 "she reached home, where she found her grandfather also standing"
1448 "and looking up at them, for they had seldom been more glorious"
1448 "than they were this night."
1448 ""
1448 "Not only were the nights of this month of May so clear and"
1448 "bright, but the days as well; the sun rose every morning into"
1448 "the cloudless sky, as undimmed in its splendor as when it sank"
1448 "the evening before, and the grandfather would look out early and"
1448 "exclaim with astonishment, \"This is indeed a wonderful year of"
1448 "sun; it will make all the shrubs and plants grow apace; you will"
1448 "have to see, general, that your army does not get out of hand"
1448 "from overfeeding.\" And Peter would swing his stick with an air"
1448 "of assurance and an expression on his face as much as to say,"
1448 "\"see to that.\""
1448 ""
1448 "So May passed, everything growing greener and greener, and then"
1448 "came the month of June, with a hotter sun and long light days,"
1448 "that brought the flowers out all over the mountain, so that"
1448 "every spot was bright with them and the air full of their sweet"
1448 "scents. This month too was drawing to its close when one day"
1448 "Heidi, having finished her domestic duties, ran out with the"
1448 "intention of paying first a visit to the fir trees, and then"
1448 "going up higher to see if the bush of rock roses was yet in"
1448 "bloom, for its flowers were so lovely when standing open in the"
1448 "sun. But just as she was turning the corner of the hut, she gave"
1448 "such a loud cry that her grandfather came running out of the shed"
1448 "to see what had happened."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Grandfather, grandfather!\" she cried, beside herself with"
1448 "excitement. \"Come here! look! look!\""
1448 ""
1448 "The old man was by her side by this time and looked in the"
1448 "direction of her outstretched hand."
1448 ""
1448 "A strange looking procession was making its way up the mountain;"
1448 "in front were two men carrying a sedan chair, in which sat a"
1448 "girl well wrapped up in shawls; then followed a horse, mounted by"
1448 "a stately-looking lady who was looking about her with great"
1448 "interest and talking to the guide who walked beside her; then a"
1448 "reclining chair, which was being pushed up by another man, it"
1448 "having evidently been thought safer to send the invalid to whom"
1448 "it belonged up the steep path in a sedan chair. The procession"
1448 "wound up with a porter, with such a bundle of cloaks, shawls,"
1448 "and furs on his back that it rose well above his head."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Here they come! here they come!\" shouted Heidi, jumping with"
1448 "joy. And sure enough it was the party from Frankfurt; the"
1448 "figures came nearer and nearer, and at last they had actually"
1448 "arrived. The men in front put down their burden, Heidi rushed"
1448 "forward and the two children embraced each other with mutual"
1448 "delight. Grandmamma having also reached the top, dismounted, and"
1448 "gave Heidi an affectionate greeting, before turning to the"
1448 "grandfather, who had meanwhile come up to welcome his guests."
1448 "There was no constraint about the meeting, for they both knew"
1448 "each other perfectly well from hearsay and felt like old"
1448 "acquaintances."
1448 ""
1448 "After the first words of greeting had been exchanged grandmamma"
1448 "broke out into lively expressions of admiration. \"What a"
1448 "magnificent residence you have, Uncle! I could hardly have"
1448 "believed it was so beautiful! A king might well envy you! And"
1448 "how well my little Heidi looks--like a wild rose!\" she continued,"
1448 "drawing the child towards her and stroking her fresh pink"
1448 "cheeks. \"I don't know which way to look first, it is all so"
