1448 ""
1448 "Clara was gazing round entranced; she had never imagined, much"
1448 "less seen, anything so beautiful. She gave vent to her delight"
1448 "in cries of joy. \"O grandmamma,\" she said, \"I should like to"
1448 "remain here for ever.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The grandfather had meanwhile drawn up the invalid chair and"
1448 "spread some of the wraps over it; he now went up to Clara."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Supposing we carry the little daughter now to her accustomed"
1448 "chair; I think she will be more comfortable, the travelling"
1448 "sedan is rather hard,\" he said, and without waiting for any one"
1448 "to help him he lifted the child in his strong arms and laid her"
1448 "gently down on her own couch. He then covered her over carefully"
1448 "and arranged her feet on the soft cushion, as if he had never"
1448 "done anything all his life but attend on cripples. The grandmamma"
1448 "looked on with surprise."
1448 ""
1448 "\"My dear Uncle,\" she exclaimed, \"if I knew where you had learned"
1448 "to nurse I would at once send all the nurses I know to the same"
1448 "place that they might handle their patients in like manner. How"
1448 "do you come to know so much?\""
1448 ""
1448 "Uncle smiled. \"I know more from experience than training,\" he"
1448 "answered, but as he spoke the smile died away and a look of"
1448 "sadness passed over his face. The vision rose before him of a"
1448 "face of suffering that he had known long years before, the face"
1448 "of a man lying crippled on his couch of pain, and unable to move"
1448 "a limb. The man had been his Captain during the fierce fighting"
1448 "in Sicily; he had found him lying wounded and had carried him"
1448 "away, and after that the captain would suffer no one else near"
1448 "him, and Uncle had stayed and nursed him till his sufferings"
1448 "ended in death. It all came back to Uncle now, and it seemed"
1448 "natural to him to attend on the sick Clara and to show her all"
1448 "those kindly attentions with which he had been once so familiar."
1448 ""
1448 "The sky spread blue and cloudless over the hut and the fir trees"
1448 "and far above over the high rocks, the grey summits of which"
1448 "glistened in the sun. Clara could not feast her eyes enough on"
1448 "all the beauty around her."
1448 ""
1448 "\"O Heidi, if only I could walk about with you,\" she said"
1448 "longingly, \"if I could but go and look at the fir trees and at"

1448 "never been here before.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi in response put out all her strength, and after a slight"
1448 "effort, managed to wheel Clara's chair quite easily round the"
1448 "hut to the fir trees. There they paused. Clara had never seen"
1448 "such trees before, with their tall, straight stems, and long"
1448 "thick branches growing thicker and thicker till they touched the"
1448 "ground. Even the grandmamma, who had followed the children, was"
1448 "astonished at the sight of them. She hardly knew what to admire"
1448 "most in these ancient trees: the lofty tops rising in their full"
1448 "green splendor towards the sky, or the pillar-like stems, with"
1448 "their straight and gigantic boughs, that spoke of such antiquity"
1448 "of age, of such long years during which they had looked down"
1448 "upon the valley below, where men came and went, and all things"
1448 "were continually changing, while they stood undisturbed and"
1448 "changeless."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi had now wheeled Clara on to the goat shed, and had flung"
1448 "open the door, so that Clara might have a full view of all that"
1448 "was inside. There was not much to see just now as its indwellers"
1448 "were absent. Clara lamented to her grandmother that they would"
1448 "have to leave early before the goats came home. \"I should so"
1448 "like to have seen Peter and his whole flock.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Dear child, let us enjoy all the beautiful things that we can"
1448 "see, and not think about those that we cannot,\" grandmamma"
1448 "replied as she followed the chair which Heidi was pushing"
1448 "further on."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh, the flowers!\" exclaimed Clara. \"Look at the bushes of red"
1448 "flowers, and all the nodding blue bells! Oh, if I could but get"
1448 "up and pick some!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi ran off at once and picked her a large nosegay of them."
1448 ""
1448 "\"But these are nothing, Clara,\" she said, laying the flowers on"
1448 "her lap. \"If you could come up higher to where the goats are"
1448 "feeding, then you would indeed see something! Bushes on bushes"
1448 "of the red centaury, and ever so many more of the blue bell-"
1448 "flowers; and then the bright yellow rock roses, that gleam like"
1448 "pure gold, and all crowding together in the one spot. And then"
1448 "there are others with the large leaves that grandfather calls"
1448 "Bright Eyes, and the brown ones with little round heads that"
1448 "smell so delicious. Oh, it is beautiful up there, and if you sit"
1448 "down among them you never want to get up again, everything looks"
1448 "and smells so lovely!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi's eyes sparkled with the remembrance of what she was"
1448 "describing; she was longing herself to see it all again, and"
1448 "Clara caught her enthusiasm and looked back at her with equal"
1448 "longing in her soft blue eyes."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Grandmamma, do you think I could get up there? Is it possible"
1448 "for me to go?\" she asked eagerly. \"If only I could walk, climb"
1448 "about everywhere with you, Heidi!\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I am sure I could push you up, the chair goes so easily,\" said"
1448 "Heidi, and in proof of her words, she sent the chair at such a"
1448 "pace round the corner that it nearly went flying down the"
1448 "mountain-side. Grandmamma being at hand, however, stopped it in"
1448 "time."
1448 ""
1448 "The grandfather, meantime, had not been idle. He had by this"
1448 "time put the table and extra chairs in front of the seat, so that"
1448 "they might all sit out here and eat the dinner that was preparing"
1448 "inside. The milk and the cheese were soon ready, and then the"
1448 "company sat down in high spirits to their mid-day meal."
1448 ""
1448 "Grandmamma was enchanted, as the doctor had been, with their"
1448 "dining-room, whence one could see far along the valley, and far"
1448 "over the mountains to the farthest stretch of blue sky. A light"
1448 "wind blew refreshingly over them as they sat at table, and the"
1448 "rustling of the fir trees made a festive accompaniment to the"
1448 "repast."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I never enjoyed anything as much as this. It is really superb!\""
1448 "cried grandmamma two or three times over; and then suddenly in a"
1448 "tone of surprise,"
1448 ""
1448 "\"Do I really see you taking a second piece of toasted cheese,"
1448 "Clara!\""
1448 ""
1448 "There, sure enough, was a second golden-colored slice of cheese"
1448 "on Clara's plate."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh, it does taste so nice, grandmamma--better than all the"
1448 "dishes we have at Ragatz,\" replied Clara, as she continued"
1448 "eating with appetite."
1448 ""
1448 "\"That's right, eat what you can!\" exclaimed Uncle. \"It's the"
1448 "mountain air which makes up for the deficiencies of the"
1448 "kitchen.\""
1448 ""
1448 "And so the meal went on. Grandmamma and Alm-Uncle got on very"
1448 "well together, and their conversation became more and more"
1448 "lively. They were so thoroughly agreed in their opinions of men"
1448 "and things and the world in general that they might have been"
1448 "taken for old cronies. The time passed merrily, and then"
1448 "grandmamma looked towards the west and said,--"
1448 ""
1448 "\"We must soon get ready to go, Clara, the sun is a good way"
1448 "down; the men will be here directly with the horse and sedan.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Clara's face fell and she said beseechingly, \"Oh, just another"
1448 "hour, grandmamma, or two hours. We haven't seen inside the hut"
1448 "yet, or Heidi's bed, or any of the other things. If only the day"
1448 "was ten hours long!\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well, that is not possible,\" said grandmamma, but she herself"
1448 "was anxious to see inside the hut, so they all rose from the"
1448 "table and Uncle wheeled Clara's chair to the door. But there"
1448 "they came to a standstill, for the chair was much too broad to"
1448 "pass through the door. Uncle, however, soon settled the"
1448 "difficulty by lifting Clara in his strong arms and carrying her"
1448 "inside."
1448 ""
1448 "Grandmamma went all round and examined the household"
1448 "arrangements, and was very much amused and pleased at their"
1448 "orderliness and the cozy appearance of everything. \"And this is"
1448 "your bedroom up here, Heidi, is it not?\" she asked, as without"
1448 "trepidation she mounted the ladder to the hay loft. \"Oh, it does"
1448 "smell sweet, what a healthy place to sleep in.\" She went up to"
1448 "the round window and looked out, and grandfather followed up"
1448 "with Clara in his arms, Heidi springing up after them. Then they"
1448 "all stood and examined Heidi's wonderful hay-bed, and grandmamma"
1448 "looked thoughtfully at it and drew in from time to time fragrant"
1448 "draughts of the hay-perfumed air, while Clara was charmed beyond"
1448 "words with Heidi's sleeping apartment."
1448 ""
1448 "\"It is delightful for you up here, Heidi! You can look from your"
1448 "bed straight into the sky, and then such a delicious smell all"
1448 "round you! and outside the fir trees waving and rustling! I have"
1448 "never seen such a pleasant, cheerful bedroom before.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Uncle looked across at the grandmamma. \"I have been thinking,\""
1448 "he said to her, \"that if you were willing to agree to it, your"
1448 "little granddaughter might remain up here, and I am sure she"
1448 "would grow stronger. You have brought up all kinds of shawls and"
1448 "covers with you, and we could make up a soft bed out of them,"
1448 "and as to the general looking after the child, you need have no"
1448 "fear, for I will see to that.\" Clara and Heidi were as overjoyed"
1448 "at these words as if they were two birds let out of their cages,"
1448 "and grandmamma's face beamed with satisfaction."
1448 ""
1448 "\"You are indeed kind, my dear Uncle,\" she exclaimed; \"you give"
1448 "words to the thought that was in my own mind. I was only asking"
1448 "myself whether a stay up here might not be the very thing she"
1448 "wanted. But then the trouble, the inconvenience to yourself! And"
1448 "you speak of nursing and looking after her as if it was a mere"
1448 "nothing! I thank you sincerely, I thank you from my whole heart,"
1448 "Uncle.\" And she took his hand and gave it a long and grateful"
1448 "shake, which he returned with a pleased expression of"
1448 "countenance."
1448 ""
1448 "Uncle immediately set to work to get things ready. He carried"
1448 "Clara back to her chair outside, Heidi following, not knowing"
1448 "how to jump high enough into the air to express her contentment."
1448 "Then he gathered up a whole pile of shawls and furs and said,"
1448 "smiling, \"It is a good thing that grandmamma came up well"
1448 "provided for a winter's campaign; we shall be able to make good"
1448 "use of these.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Foresight is a virtue,\" responded the lady, amused, \"and"
1448 "prevents many misfortunes. If we have made the journey over your"
1448 "mountains without meeting with storms, winds and cloud-bursts,"
1448 "we can only be thankful, which we are, and my provision against"
1448 "these disasters now comes in usefully, as you say.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The two had meanwhile ascended to the hay-loft and begun to"
1448 "prepare a bed; there were so many articles piled one over the"
1448 "other that when finished it looked like a regular little"
1448 "fortress. Grandmamma passed her hand carefully over it to make"
1448 "sure there were no bits of hay sticking out. \"If there's a bit"
1448 "that can come through it will,\" she said. The soft mattress,"
1448 "however, was so smooth and thick that nothing could penetrate"
1448 "it. Then they went down again, well satisfied, and found the"
1448 "children laughing and talking together and arranging all they"
1448 "were going to do from morning till evening as long as Clara"
1448 "stayed. The next question was how long she was to remain, and"
1448 "first grandmamma was asked, but she referred them to the"
1448 "grandfather, who gave it as his opinion that she ought to make"
1448 "the trial of the mountain air for at least a month. The children"
1448 "clapped their hands for joy, for they had not expected to be"
1448 "together for so long a time."
1448 ""
1448 "The bearers and the horse and guide were now seen approaching;"
1448 "the former were sent back at once, and grandmamma prepared to"
1448 "mount for her return journey."
1448 ""
1448 "\"It's not saying good-bye, grandmamma,\" Clara called out, \"for"
1448 "you will come up now and then and see how we are getting on, and"
1448 "we shall so look forward to your visits, shan't we, Heidi?\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi, who felt that life this day had been crowded with"
1448 "pleasures, could only respond to Clara with another jump of joy."
1448 ""
1448 "Grandmamma being now seated on her sturdy animal, Uncle took the"
1448 "bridle to lead her down the steep mountain path; she begged him"
1448 "not to come far with her, but he insisted on seeing her safely"
1448 "as far as Dorfli, for the way was precipitous and not without"
1448 "danger for the rider, he said."
1448 ""
1448 "Grandmamma did not care to stay alone in Dorfli, and therefore"
1448 "decided to return to Ragatz, and thence to make excursions up"
1448 "the mountain from time to time."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter came down with his goats before Uncle had returned. As"
1448 "soon as the animals caught sight of Heidi they all came flocking"
1448 "towards her, and she, as well as Clara on her couch, were soon"
1448 "surrounded by the goats, pushing and poking their heads one over"
1448 "the other, while Heidi introduced each in turn by its name to"
1448 "her friend Clara."
1448 ""
1448 "It was not long before the latter had made the long-wished-for"
1448 "acquaintance of little Snowflake, the lively Greenfinch, and the"
1448 "well-behaved goats belonging to grandfather, as well as of the"
1448 "many others, including the Grand Turk. Peter meanwhile stood"
1448 "apart looking on, and casting somewhat unfriendly glances"
1448 "towards Clara."
1448 ""
1448 "When the two children called out, \"Good-evening, Peter,\" he made"
1448 "no answer, but swung up his stick angrily, as if wanting to cut"
1448 "the air in two, and then ran off with his goats after him."
1448 ""
1448 "The climax to all the beautiful things that Clara had already"
1448 "seen upon the mountain came at the close of the day."
1448 ""
1448 "As she lay on the large soft bed in the hay loft, with Heidi"
1448 "near her, she looked out through the round open window right into"
1448 "the middle of the shining clusters of stars, and she exclaimed in"
1448 "delight,--"
1448 ""
1448 "\"Heidi, it's just as if we were in a high carriage and were"
1448 "going to drive straight into heaven.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, and do you know why the stars are so happy and look down"
1448 "and nod to us like that?\" asked Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "\"No, why is it?\" Clara asked in return."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Because they live up in heaven, and know how well God arranges"
1448 "everything for us, so that we need have no more fear or trouble"
1448 "and may be quite sure that all things will come right in the"
1448 "end. That's why they are so happy, and they nod to us because"
1448 "they want us to be happy too. But then we must never forget to"
1448 "pray, and to ask God to remember us when He is arranging things,"
1448 "so that we too may feel safe and have no anxiety about what is"
1448 "going to happen.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The two children now sat up and said their prayers, and then"
1448 "Heidi put her head down on her little round arm and fell off to"
1448 "sleep at once, but Clara lay awake some time, for she could not"
1448 "get over the wonder of this new experience of being in bed up"
1448 "here among the stars. She had indeed seldom seen a star, for she"
1448 "never went outside the house at night, and the curtains at home"
1448 "were always drawn before the stars came out. Each time she"
1448 "closed her eyes she felt she must open them again to see if the"
1448 "two very large stars were still looking in, and nodding to her as"
1448 "Heidi said they did. There they were, always in the same place,"
1448 "and Clara felt she could not look long enough into their bright"
1448 "sparkling faces, until at last her eyes closed of their own"
1448 "accord, and it was only in her dreams that she still saw the two"
1448 "large friendly stars shining down upon her."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER XXI. HOW LIFE WENT ON AT GRANDFATHER'S>"
1448 ""
1448 "The sun had just risen above the mountains and was shedding its"
1448 "first golden rays over the hut and the valley below. Alm-Uncle,"
1448 "as was his custom, had been standing in a quiet and, devout"
1448 "attitude for some little while, watching the light mists"
1448 "gradually lifting, and the heights and valley emerging from"
1448 "their twilight shadows and awakening to another day."
1448 ""
1448 "The light morning clouds overhead grew brighter and brighter,"
1448 "till at last the sun shone out in its full glory, and rock and"
1448 "wood and hill lay bathed in golden light."
1448 ""
1448 "Uncle now stepped back into the hut and went softly up the"
1448 "ladder. Clara had just opened her eyes and was looking with"
1448 "wonder at the bright sunlight that shone through the round"
1448 "window and danced and sparkled about her bed. She could not at"
1448 "first think what she was looking at or where she was. Then she"
1448 "caught sight of Heidi sleeping beside her, and now she heard the"
1448 "grandfather's cheery voice asking her if she had slept well and"
1448 "was feeling rested. She assured him she was not tired, and that"
1448 "when she had once fallen asleep she had not opened her eyes"
1448 "again all night. The grandfather was satisfied at this and"
1448 "immediately began to attend upon her with so much gentleness and"
1448 "understanding that it seemed as if his chief calling had been to"
1448 "look after sick children."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi now awoke and was surprised to see Clara dressed, and"
1448 "already in the grandfather's arms ready to be carried down. She"
1448 "must be up too, and she went through her toilette with lightning-"
1448 "like speed. She ran down the ladder and out of the hut, and there"
1448 "further astonishment awaited her, for grandfather had been busy"
1448 "the night before after they were in bed. Seeing that it was"
1448 "impossible to get Clara's chair through the hut-door, he had"
1448 "taken down two of the boards at the side of the shed and made an"
1448 "opening large enough to admit the chair; these he left loose so"
1448 "that they could be taken away and put up at pleasure. He was at"
1448 "this moment wheeling Clara out into the sun; he left her in"
1448 "front of the hut while he went to look after the goats, and Heidi"
1448 "ran up to her friend."
1448 ""
1448 "The fresh morning breeze blew round the children's faces, and"
1448 "every fresh puff brought a waft of fragrance from the fir trees."
1448 "Clara drew it in with delight and lay back in her chair with an"
1448 "unaccustomed feeling of health and comfort."
1448 ""
1448 "It was the first time in her life that she had been out in the"
1448 "open country at this early hour and felt the fresh morning"
1448 "breeze, and the pure mountain air was so cool and refreshing"
1448 "that every breath she drew was a pleasure. And then the bright"
1448 "sweet sun, which was not hot and sultry up here, but lay soft and"
1448 "warm on her hands and on the grass at her feet. Clara had not"
1448 "imagined that it would be like this on the mountain."
1448 ""
1448 "\"O Heidi, if only I could stay up here for ever with you,\" she"
1448 "exclaimed happily, turning in her chair from side to side that"
1448 "she might drink in the air and sun from all quarters."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Now you see that it is just what I told you,\" replied Heidi"
1448 "delighted; \"that it is the most beautiful thing in the world to"
1448 "be up here with grandfather.\""
1448 ""
1448 "The latter at that moment appeared coming from the goat shed and"
1448 "bringing two small foaming bowls of snow-white milk--one for"
1448 "Clara and one for Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "\"That will do the little daughter good,\" he said, nodding to"
1448 "Clara; \"it is from Little Swan and will make her strong. To your"
1448 "health, child! drink it up.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Clara had never tasted goat's milk before; she hesitated and"
1448 "smelt it before putting it to her lips, but seeing how Heidi"
1448 "drank hers up without hesitating, and how much she seemed to like"
1448 "it, Clara did the same, and drank till there was not a drop left,"
1448 "for she too found it delicious, tasting just as if sugar and"
1448 "cinnamon had been mixed with it."
1448 ""
1448 "\"To-morrow we will drink two,\" said the grandfather, who had"
1448 "looked on with satisfaction at seeing her follow Heidi's"
1448 "example."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter now arrived with the goats, and while Heidi was receiving"
1448 "her usual crowded morning greetings, Uncle drew Peter aside to"
1448 "speak to him, for the goats, bleated so loudly and continuously"
1448 "in their wish to express their joy and affection that no one"
1448 "could be heard near them."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Attend to what I have to say,\" he said. \"From to-day be sure you"
1448 "let Little Swan go where she likes. She has an instinct where to"
1448 "find the best food for herself, and so if she wants to climb"
1448 "higher, you follow her, and it will do the others no harm if they"
1448 "go too; on no account bring her back. A little more climbing"
1448 "won't hurt you, and in this matter she probably knows better than"
1448 "you what is good for her; I want her to give as fine milk as"
1448 "possible. Why are you looking over there as if you wanted to eat"
1448 "somebody? Nobody will interfere with you. So now be off and"
1448 "remember what I say.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter was accustomed to give immediate obedience to Uncle, and"
1448 "he marched off with his goats, but with a turn of the head and"
1448 "roll of the eye that showed he had some thought in reserve. The"
1448 "goats carried Heidi along with them a little way, which was what"
1448 "Peter wanted. \"You will have to come with them,\" he called to"
1448 "her, \"for I shall be obliged to follow Little Swan.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I cannot,\" Heidi called back from the midst of her friends,"
1448 "\"and I shall not be able to come for a long, long time--not as"
1448 "long as Clara is with me. Grandfather, however, has promised to"
1448 "go up the mountain with both of us one day.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi had now extricated herself from the goats and she ran back"
1448 "to Clara. Peter doubled his fists and made threatening gestures"
1448 "towards the invalid on her couch, and then climbed up some"
1448 "distance without pause until he was out of sight, for he was"
1448 "afraid Uncle might have seen him, and he did not care to know"
1448 "what Uncle might have thought of the fists."
1448 ""
1448 "Clara and Heidi had made so many plans for themselves that they"
1448 "hardly knew where to begin. Heidi suggested that they should"
1448 "first write to grandmamma, to whom they had promised to send word"
1448 "every day, for grandmamma had not felt sure whether it would in"
1448 "the long run suit Clara's health to remain up the mountain, or if"
1448 "she would continue to enjoy herself there. With daily news of her"
1448 "granddaughter she could stay on without anxiety at Ragatz, and be"
1448 "ready to go to Clara at a moment's notice."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Must we go indoors to write?\" asked Clara, who agreed to Heidi's"
1448 "proposal but did not want to move from where she was, as it was"
1448 "so much nicer outside. Heidi was prepared to arrange everything."
1448 "She ran in and brought out her school-book and writing things and"
1448 "her own little stool. She put her reading book and copy book on"
1448 "Clara's knees, to make a desk for her to write upon, and she"
1448 "herself took her seat on the stool and sat to the bench, and then"
1448 "they both began writing to grandmamma. But Clara paused after"
1448 "every sentence to look about her; it was too beautiful for much"
1448 "letter writing. The breeze had sunk a little, and now only gently"
1448 "fanned her face and whispered lightly through the fir trees."
1448 "Little winged insects hummed and danced around her in the clear"
1448 "air, and a great stillness lay over the far, wide, sunny pasture"
1448 "lands. Lofty and silent rose the high mountain peaks above her,"
1448 "and below lay the whole broad valley full of quiet peace. Only"
1448 "now and again the call of some shepherd-boy rang out through the"
1448 "air, and echo answered softly from the rocks. The morning passed,"
1448 "the children hardly knew how, and now grandfather came with the"
1448 "mid-day bowls of steaming milk, for the little daughter, he said,"
1448 "was to remain out as long as there was a gleam of sun in the sky."
1448 "The mid-day meal was set out and eaten as yesterday in the open"
1448 "air. Then Heidi pushed Clara's chair under the fir trees, for"
1448 "they had agreed to spend the afternoon under their shade and"
1448 "there tell each other all that had happened since Heidi left"
1448 "Frankfurt. If everything had gone on there as usual in a general"
1448 "way, there were still all kinds of particular things to tell"
1448 "Heidi about the various people who composed the Sesemann"
1448 "household, and who were all so well known to Heidi."
1448 ""
1448 "So they sat and chatted under the trees, and the more lively"
1448 "grew their conversation, the more loudly sang the birds overhead,"
1448 "as if wishing to take part in the children's gossip, which"
1448 "evidently pleased them. So the hours flew by and all at once, as"
1448 "it seemed, the evening had come with the returning Peter, who"
1448 "still scowled and looked angry."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Good-night, Peter,\" called out Heidi, as she saw he had no"
1448 "intention of stopping to speak."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Good-night, Peter,\" called out Clara in a friendly voice. Peter"
1448 "took no notice and went surlily on with his goats."
1448 ""
1448 "As Clara saw the grandfather leading away Little Swan to milk"
1448 "her, she was suddenly taken with a longing for another bowlful"
1448 "of the fragrant milk, and waited impatiently for it."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Isn't it curious, Heidi,\" she said, astonished at herself, \"as"
1448 "long as I can remember I have only eaten because I was obliged"
1448 "to, and everything used to seem to taste of cod liver oil, and I"
1448 "was always wishing there was no need to eat or drink; and now I"
1448 "am longing for grandfather to bring me the milk.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, I know what it feels like,\" replied Heidi, who remembered"
1448 "the many days in Frankfurt when all her food used to seem to"
1448 "stick in her throat. Clara, however, could not understand it;"
1448 "the fact was that she had never in her life before spent a whole"
1448 "day in the open air, much less in such high, life-giving mountain"
1448 "air. When grandfather at last brought her the evening milk, she"
1448 "drank it up so quickly that she had emptied her bowl before"
1448 "Heidi, and then she asked for a little more. The grandfather"
1448 "went inside with both the children's bowls, and when he brought"
1448 "them out again full he had something else to add to their supper."
1448 "He had walked over that afternoon to a herdsman's house where the"
1448 "sweetly-tasting butter was made, and had brought home a large"
1448 "pat, some of which he had now spread thickly on two good slices"
1448 "of bread. He stood and watched with pleasure while Clara and"
1448 "Heidi ate their appetising meal with childish hunger and"
1448 "enjoyment."
1448 ""
1448 "That night, when Clara lay down in her bed and prepared to watch"
1448 "the stars, her eyes would not keep open, and she fell asleep as"
1448 "soon as Heidi and slept soundly all night--a thing she never"
1448 "remembered having done before. The following day and the day"
1448 "after passed in the same pleasant fashion, and the third day"
1448 "there came a surprise for the children. Two stout porters came"
1448 "up the mountain, each carrying a bed on his shoulders with"
1448 "bedding of all kinds and two beautiful new white coverlids. The"
1448 "men also had a letter with them from grandmamma, in which she"
1448 "said that these were for Clara and Heidi, and that Heidi in"
1448 "future was always to sleep in a proper bed, and when she went"
1448 "down to Dorfli in the winter she was to take one with her and"
1448 "leave the other at the hut, so that Clara might always know there"
1448 "was a bed ready for her when she paid a visit to the mountain."
1448 "She went on to thank the children for their long letters and"
1448 "encouraged them to continue writing daily, so that she might be"
1448 "able to picture all they were doing."
1448 ""
1448 "So the grandfather went up and threw back the hay from Heidi's"
1448 "bed on to the great heap, and then with his help the beds were"
1448 "transported to the loft. He put them close to one another so"
1448 "that the children might still be able to see out of the window,"
1448 "for he knew what pleasure they had in the light from the sun and"
1448 "stars."
1448 ""
1448 "Meanwhile grandmamma down at Ragatz was rejoicing at the"
1448 "excellent news of the invalid which reached her daily from the"
1448 "mountain. Clara found the life more charming each day and could"
1448 "not say enough of the kindness and care which the grandfather"
1448 "lavished upon her, nor of Heidi's lively and amusing"
1448 "companionship, for the latter was more entertaining even than"
1448 "when in Frankfurt with her, and Clara's first thought when she"
1448 "woke each morning was, \"Oh, how glad I am to be here still.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Having such fresh assurances each day that all was going well"
1448 "with Clara, grandmamma thought she might put off her visit to"
1448 "the children a little longer, for the steep ride up and down was"
1448 "somewhat of a fatigue to her."
1448 ""
1448 "The grandfather seemed to feel an especial sympathy for this"
1448 "little invalid charge, for he tried to think of something fresh"
1448 "every day to help forward her recovery. He climbed up the"
1448 "mountain every afternoon, higher and higher each day, and came"
1448 "home in the evening with a large bunch of leaves which scented"
1448 "the air with a mingled fragrance as of carnations and thyme,"
1448 "even from afar. He hung it up in the goat shed, and the goats on"
1448 "their return were wild to get at it, for they recognised the"
1448 "smell. But Uncle did not go climbing after rare plants to give"
1448 "the goats the pleasure of eating them without any trouble of"
1448 "finding them; what he gathered was for Little Swan alone, that"
1448 "she might give extra fine milk, and the effect of the extra"
1448 "feeding was shown in the way she flung her head in the air with"
1448 "ever-increasing frolicsomeness, and in the bright glow of her"
1448 "eye."
1448 ""
1448 "Clara had now been on the mountain for three weeks. For some"
1448 "days past the grandfather, each morning after carrying her down,"
1448 "had said, \"Won't the little daughter try if she can stand for a"
1448 "minute or two?\" And Clara had made the effort in order to please"
1448 "him, but had clung to him as soon as her feet touched the"
1448 "ground, exclaiming that it hurt her so. He let her try a little"
1448 "longer, however, each day."
1448 ""
1448 "It was many years since they had had such a splendid summer"
1448 "among the mountains. Day after day there were the same cloudless"
1448 "sky and brilliant sun; the flowers opened wide their fragrant"
1448 "blossoms, and everywhere the eye was greeted with a glow of"
1448 "color; and when the evening came the crimson light fell on"
1448 "mountain peaks and on the great snow-field, till at last the sun"
1448 "sank in a sea of golden flame."
1448 ""
1448 "And Heidi never tired of telling Clara of all this, for only"
1448 "higher up could the full glory of the colors be rightly seen;"
1448 "and more particularly did she dwell on the beauty of the spot on"
1448 "the higher slope of the mountain, where the bright golden rock-"
1448 "roses grew in masses, and the blue flowers were in such numbers"
1448 "that the very grass seemed to have turned blue, while near these"
1448 "were whole bushes of the brown blossoms, with their delicious"
1448 "scent, so that you never wanted to move again when you once sat"
1448 "down among them."
1448 ""
1448 "She had just been expatiating on the flowers as she sat with"
1448 "Clara under the fir trees one evening, and had been telling her"
1448 "again of the wonderful light from the evening sun, when such an"
1448 "irrepressible longing came over her to see it all once more that"
1448 "she jumped up and ran to her grandfather, who was in the shed,"
1448 "calling out almost before she was inside,--"
1448 ""
1448 "\"Grandfather, will you take us out with the goats to-morrow? Oh,"
1448 "it is so lovely up there now!\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Very well,\" he answered, \"but if I do, the little daughter must"
1448 "do something to please me: she must try her best again this"
1448 "evening to stand on her feet.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi ran back with the good news to Clara, and the latter"
1448 "promised to try her very best as the grandfather wished, for she"
1448 "looked forward immensely to the next day's excursion. Heidi was"
1448 "so pleased and excited that she called out to Peter as soon as"
1448 "she caught sight of him that evening,--"
1448 ""
1448 "\"Peter, Peter, we are all coming out with you to-morrow and are"
1448 "going to stay up there the whole day.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Peter, cross as a bear, grumbled some reply, and lifted his"
1448 "stick to give Greenfinch a blow for no reason in particular, but"
1448 "Greenfinch saw the movement, and with a leap over Snowflake's"
1448 "back she got out of the way, and the stick only hit the air."
1448 ""
1448 "Clara and Heidi got into their two fine beds that night full of"
1448 "delightful anticipation of the morrow; they were so full of"
1448 "their plans that they agreed to keep awake all night and talk"
1448 "over them until they might venture to get up. But their heads had"
1448 "no sooner touched their soft pillows than the conversation"
1448 "suddenly ceased, and Clara fell into a dream of an immense field,"
1448 "which looked the color of the sky, so thickly inlaid was it with"
1448 "blue bell-shaped flowers; and Heidi heard the great bird of prey"
1448 "calling to her from the heights above, \"Come! come! come!\""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER XXII. SOMETHING UNEXPECTED HAPPENS>"
1448 ""
1448 "Uncle went out early the next morning to see what kind of a day"
1448 "it was going to be. There was a reddish gold light over the"
1448 "higher peaks; a light breeze springing up and the branches of the"
1448 "fir trees moved gently to and fro the sun was on its way."
1448 ""
1448 "The old man stood and watched the green slopes under the higher"
1448 "peaks gradually growing brighter with the coming day and the dark"
1448 "shadows lifting from the valley, until at first a rosy light"
1448 "filled its hollows, and then the morning gold flooded every"
1448 "height and depth--the sun had risen."
1448 ""
1448 "Uncle wheeled the chair out of the shed ready for the coming"
1448 "journey, and then went in to call the children and tell them what"
1448 "a lovely sunrise it was."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter came up at this moment. The goats did not gather round him"
1448 "so trustfully as usual, but seemed to avoid him timidly, for"
1448 "Peter had reached a high pitch of anger and bitterness, and was"
1448 "laying about him with his stick very unnecessarily, and where it"
1448 "fell the blow was no light one. For weeks now he had not had"
1448 "Heidi all to himself as formerly. When he came up in the morning"
1448 "the invalid child was always already in her chair and Heidi fully"
1448 "occupied with her. And it was the same thing over again when he"
1448 "came down in the evening. She had not come out with the goats"
1448 "once this summer, and now to-day she was only coming in company"
1448 "with her friend and the chair, and would stick by the latter's"
1448 "side the whole time. It was the thought of this which was making"
1448 "him particularly cross this morning. There stood the chair on its"
1448 "high wheels; Peter seemed to see something proud and disdainful"
1448 "about it, and he glared at it as at an enemy that had done him"
1448 "harm and was likely to do him more still to-day. He glanced"
1448 "round--there was no sound anywhere, no one to see him. He sprang"
1448 "forward like a wild creature, caught hold of it, and gave it a"
1448 "violent and angry push in the direction of the slope. The chair"
1448 "rolled swiftly forward and in another minute had disappeared."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter now sped up the mountain as if on wings, not pausing till"
1448 "he was well in shelter of a large blackberry bush, for he had no"
1448 "wish to be seen by Uncle. But he was anxious to see what had"
1448 "become of the chair, and his bush was well placed for that."
1448 "Himself hidden, he could watch what happened below and see what"
1448 "Uncle did without being discovered himself. So he looked, and"
1448 "there he saw his enemy running faster and faster down hill, then"
1448 "it turned head over heels several times, and finally, after one"
1448 "great bound, rolled over and over to its complete destruction."
1448 "The pieces flew in every direction--feet, arms, and torn"
1448 "fragments of the padded seat and bolster--and Peter experienced a"
1448 "feeling of such unbounded delight at the sight that he leapt in"
1448 "the air, laughing aloud and stamping for joy; then he took a run"
1448 "round, jumping over bushes on the way, only to return to the same"
1448 "spot and fall into fresh fits of laughter. He was beside himself"
1448 "with satisfaction, for he could see only good results for himself"
1448 "in this disaster to his enemy. Now Heidi's friend would be"
1448 "obliged to go away, for she would have no means of going about,"
1448 "and when Heidi was alone again she would come out with him as in"
1448 "the old days, and everything would go on in the proper way again."
1448 "But Peter did not consider, or did not know, that when we do a"
1448 "wrong thing trouble is sure to follow."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi now came running out of the hut and round to the shed."
1448 "Grandfather was behind with Clara in his arms. The shed stood"
1448 "wide open, the two loose planks having been taken down, and it"
1448 "was quite light inside. Heidi looked into every corner and ran"
1448 "from one end to the other, and then stood still wondering what"
1448 "could have happened to the chair. Grandfather now came up."
1448 ""
1448 "\"How is this, have you wheeled the chair away, Heidi?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I have been looking everywhere for it, grandfather; you said it"
1448 "was standing ready outside,\" and she again searched each corner"
1448 "of the shed with her eyes."
1448 ""
1448 "At that moment the wind, which had risen suddenly, blew open the"
1448 "shed door and sent it banging back against the wall."
1448 ""
1448 "\"It must have been the wind, grandfather,\" exclaimed Heidi, and"
1448 "her eyes grew anxious at this sudden discovery. \"Oh! if it has"
1448 "blown the chair all the way down to Dorfli we shall not get it"
1448 "back in time, and shall not be able to go.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"If it has rolled as far as that it will never come back, for it"
1448 "is in a hundred pieces by now,\" said the grandfather, going"
1448 "round the corner and looking down. \"But it's a curious thing to"
1448 "have happened!\" he added as he thought over the matter, for the"
1448 "chair would have had to turn a corner before starting down hill."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Oh, I am sorry,\" lamented Clara, \"for we shall not be able to"
1448 "go to-day, or perhaps any other day. I shall have to go home, I"
1448 "suppose, if I have no chair. Oh, I am so sorry, I am so sorry!\""
1448 ""
1448 "But Heidi looked towards her grandfather with her usual"
1448 "expression of confidence."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Grandfather, you will be able to do something, won't you, so"
1448 "that it need not be as Clara says, and so that she is not"
1448 "obliged to go home?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well, for the present we will go up the mountain as we had"
1448 "arranged, and then later on we will see what can be done,\" he"
1448 "answered, much to the children's delight."
1448 ""
1448 "He went indoors, fetched out a pile of shawls, and laying them"
1448 "on the sunniest spot he could find set Clara down upon them. Then"
1448 "he fetched the children's morning milk and had out his two goats."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Why is Peter not here yet?\" thought Uncle to himself, for"
1448 "Peter's whistle had not been sounded that morning. The"
1448 "grandfather now took Clara up on one arm, and the shawls on the"
1448 "other."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Now then we will start,\" he said; \"the goats can come with us.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi was pleased at this and walked on after her grandfather"
1448 "with an arm over either of the goats' necks, and the animals were"
1448 "so overjoyed to have her again that they nearly squeezed her flat"

1448 "them, lying his full length on the ground."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I'll teach you another time to go by like that, you lazy"

1448 ""
1448 "Peter, recognising the voice, jumped up like a shot. \"No one was"
1448 "up,\" he answered."
1448 ""

1448 ""

1448 "voice."
1448 ""
1448 "Uncle said no more. He spread the shawls on the sunny slope, and"
1448 "setting Clara upon them asked if she was comfortable."
1448 ""

1448 "lovely!\" she cried, looking round her with delight."
1448 ""
1448 "The grandfather prepared to leave them. They would now be safe"
1448 "and happy together, he said, and when it was time for dinner"

1448 "had put it; Peter was to bring them as much milk as they wanted,"
1448 "but Heidi was to see that it was Little Swan's milk. He would"
1448 "come and fetch them towards evening; he must now be off to see"
1448 "after the chair and ascertain what had become of it."
1448 ""
1448 "The sky was dark blue, and not a single cloud was to be seen"
1448 "from one horizon to the other. The great snow-field overhead"
1448 "sparkled as if set with thousands and thousands of gold and"
1448 "silver stars. The two grey mountains peaks lifted their lofty"

1448 "young goat came and lay down beside them; Snowflake came"
1448 "oftenest, putting her little head down near Heidi, and only"
1448 "moving because another goat came and drove her away. Clara had"
1448 "learned to know them all so well that she never mistook one for"
1448 "the other now, for each had an expression and ways of its own."
1448 "And the goats had also grown familiar with Clara and would rub"
1448 "their heads against her shoulder, which was always a sign of"
1448 "acquaintanceship and goodwill."
1448 ""
1448 "Some hours went by, and Heidi began to think that she might just"
1448 "go over to the spot where all the flowers grew to see if they"
1448 "were fully blown and looking as lovely as the year before. Clara"
1448 "could not go until grandfather came back that evening, when the"
1448 "flowers probably would be already closed. The longing to go"

1448 "it."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Would you think me unkind, Clara,\" she said rather"

1448 "looking--but wait--\" for an idea had come into Heidi's head. She"
1448 "ran and picked a bunch or two of green leaves, and then took hold"
1448 "of Snowflake and led her up to Clara."
1448 ""
1448 "\"There, now you will not be alone,\" said Heidi, giving the goat"
1448 "a little push to show her she was to lie down near Clara, which"

1448 "lap, and the latter told her friend to go at once to look at the"
1448 "flowers as she was quite happy to be left with the goat; she"
1448 "liked this new experience. Heidi ran off, and Clara began to"

1448 "stronger ones of the flock. And Clara found a strange new"

1448 "only companion a little goat that looked to her for protection."
1448 "She suddenly felt a great desire to be her own mistress and to be"
1448 "able to help others, instead of herself being always dependent as"
1448 "she was now. Many thoughts, unknown to her before, came crowding"

1448 "feeling of joy took possession of her, as if everything she had"
1448 "ever known or felt became all at once more beautiful, and she"
1448 "seemed to see all things in a new light, and so strong was the"
1448 "sense of this new beauty and happiness that she threw her arms"
1448 "round the little goat's neck, and exclaimed, \"O Snowflake, how"

1448 "you beside me!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi had meanwhile reached her field of flowers, and as she"
1448 "caught sight of it she uttered a cry of joy. The whole ground in"
1448 "front of her was a mass of shimmering gold, where the cistus"

1448 "reached Clara's side out of breath with running and excitement."

1448 "\"it is more beautiful than you can imagine, and perhaps this"
1448 "evening it may not be so lovely. I believe I could carry you,"

1448 "\"Why, Heidi, what can you be thinking of! you are smaller than I"
1448 "am. Oh, if only I could walk!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi looked round as if in search of something, some new idea"
1448 "had evidently come into her head. Peter was sitting up above"
1448 "looking down on the two children. He had been sitting and"
1448 "staring before him in the same way for hours, as if he could not"
1448 "make out what he saw. He had destroyed the chair so that the"

1448 "He thought his eyes must deceive him, and yet there she was and"
1448 "no mistake about it."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi now looked up to where he was sitting and called out in a"
1448 "peremptory voice, \"Peter, come down here!\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I don't wish to come,\" he called in reply."
1448 ""

1448 "come here and help me; make haste and come down,\" she called"

1448 ""
1448 "\"I shall do nothing of the kind,\" was the answer."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi ran some way up the slope towards him, and then pausing"
1448 "called again, her eyes ablaze with anger, \"If you don't come at"

1448 ""
1448 "Peter felt an inward throe at these words, and a great fear"
1448 "seized him. He had done something wicked which he wanted no one"
1448 "to know about, and so far he had thought himself safe. But now"

1448 "was awaiting him."
1448 ""

1448 ""

1448 ""
1448 "As soon as they got to Clara, Heidi gave her orders: Peter was"

1448 ""

1448 ""
1448 "Peter, however, had never given his arm to any one in his life."

1448 ""

1448 ""
1448 "Peter did as he was told, but still they did not get on very"

1448 "match very well in size; it was up one side and down the other,"
1448 "so that the supports were rather wobbly."
1448 ""
1448 "Clara tried to use her own feet a little, but each time drew"
1448 "them quickly back."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Put your foot down firmly once,\" suggested Heidi, \"I am sure it"
1448 "will hurt you less after that.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Do you think so?\" said Clara hesitatingly, but she followed"
1448 "Heidi's advice and ventured one firm step on the ground and then"

1448 ""

1448 ""

1448 ""

1448 ""
1448 "\"Now we shall be able to come up here together every day, and go"

1448 ""

1448 ""
1448 "They had not far to go to reach the field of flowers, and could"
1448 "already catch sight of the cistus flowers glowing gold in the"

1448 ""

1448 "sunlight and the scent of the flowers, held her dumb."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter also lay among the flowers without moving or speaking, for"
1448 "he was fast asleep. The breeze came blowing softly and"
1448 "caressingly from behind the sheltering rocks, and passed"
1448 "whisperingly through the bushes overhead. Heidi got up now and"
1448 "then to run about, for the flowers waving in the warm wind"
1448 "seemed to smell sweeter and to grow more thickly whichever way"
1448 "she went, and she felt she must sit down at each fresh spot to"
1448 "enjoy the sight and scent. So the hours went by."
1448 ""
1448 "It was long past noon when a small troop of goats advanced"
1448 "solemnly towards the plain of flowers. It was not a feeding"
1448 "place of theirs, for they did not care to graze on flowers. They"
1448 "looked like an embassy arriving, with Greenfinch as their leader."
1448 "They had evidently come in search of their companions who had"
1448 "left them in the lurch, and who had, contrary to all custom,"
1448 "remained away so long, for the goats could tell the time without"
1448 "mistake. As soon as Greenfinch caught sight of the three missing"
1448 "friends amid the flowers she set up an extra loud bleat,"
1448 "whereupon all the others joined in a chorus of bleats, and the"
1448 "whole company came trotting towards the children. Peter woke up,"
1448 "rubbing his eyes, for he had been dreaming that he saw the chair"
1448 "again with its beautiful red padding standing whole and uninjured"
1448 "before the grandfather's door, and indeed just as he awoke he"
1448 "thought he was looking at the brass-headed nails that studded it"
1448 "all round, but it was only the bright yellow flowers beside him."
1448 "He experienced again a dreadful fear of mind that he had lost in"
1448 "this dream of the uninjured chair. Even though Heidi had promised"
1448 "not to do anything, there still remained the lively dread that"
1448 "his deed might be found out in some other way. He allowed Heidi"
1448 "to do what she liked with him, for he was reduced to such a state"
1448 "of low spirits and meekness that he was ready to give his help to"
1448 "Clara without murmur or resistance."
1448 ""
1448 "When all three had got back to their old quarters Heidi ran and"
1448 "brought forward the bag, and proceeded to fulfil her promise,"
1448 "for her threat of the morning had been concerned with Peter's"
1448 "dinner. She had seen her grandfather putting in all sorts of good"
1448 "things, and had been pleased to think of Peter having a large"
1448 "share of them, and she had meant him to understand when he"
1448 "refused at first to help her that he would get nothing for his"
1448 "dinner, but Peter's conscience had put another interpretation"
1448 "upon her words. Heidi took the food out of the bag and divided it"
1448 "into three portions, and each was of such a goodly size that she"
1448 "thought to herself, \"There will be plenty of ours left for him to"
1448 "have more still.\""
1448 ""
1448 "She gave the other two their dinners and sat down with her own"
1448 "beside Clara, and they all three ate with a good appetite after"
1448 "their great exertions."
1448 ""
1448 "It ended as Heidi had expected, and Peter got as much food again"
1448 "as his own share with what Clara and Heidi had over from theirs"
1448 "after they had both eaten as much as they wanted. Peter ate up"
1448 "every bit of food to the last crumb, but there was something"
1448 "wanting to his usual enjoyment of a good dinner, for every"
1448 "mouthful he swallowed seemed to choke him, and he felt something"
1448 "gnawing inside him."
1448 ""
1448 "They were so late at their dinner that they had not long to wait"
1448 "after they had finished before grandfather came up to fetch them."
1448 "Heidi rushed forward to meet him as soon as he appeared, as she"
1448 "wanted to be the first to tell him the good news. She was so"
1448 "excited that she could hardly get her words out when she did get"
1448 "up to him, but he soon understood, and a look of extreme pleasure"
1448 "came into his face. He hastened up to where Clara was sitting and"
1448 "said with a cheerful smile, \"So we've made the effort, have we,"
1448 "and won the day!\""
1448 ""
1448 "Then he lifted her up, and putting his left arm behind her and"
1448 "giving her his right to lean upon, made her walk a little way,"
1448 "which she did with less trembling and hesitation than before now"
1448 "that she had such a strong arm round her."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi skipped along beside her in triumphant glee, and the"
1448 "grandfather looked too as if some happiness had befallen him."
1448 "But now he took Clara up in his arms. \"We must not overdo it,\""
1448 "he said, \"and it is high time we went home,\" and he started off"
1448 "down the mountain path, for he was anxious to get her indoors"
1448 "that she might rest after her unusual fatigue."
1448 ""
1448 "When Peter got to Dorfli that evening he found a large group of"
1448 "people collected round a certain spot, pushing one another and"
1448 "looking over each other's shoulders in their eagerness to catch"
1448 "sight of something lying on the ground. Peter thought he should"
1448 "like to see too, and poked and elbowed till he made his way"
1448 "through."
1448 ""
1448 "There it lay, the thing he had wanted to see. Scattered about"
1448 "the grass were the remains of Clara's chair; part of the back and"
1448 "the middle bit, and enough of the red padding and the bright"
1448 "nails to show how magnificent the chair had been when it was"
1448 "entire."
1448 ""
1448 "\"I was here when the men passed carrying it up,\" said the baker"
1448 "who was standing near Peter. \"I'll bet any one that it was worth"
1448 "twenty-five pounds at least. I cannot think how such an accident"
1448 "could have happened.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Uncle said the wind might perhaps have done it,\" remarked one"
1448 "of the women, who could not sufficiently admire the red"
1448 "upholstery."
1448 ""
1448 "\"It's a good job that no one but the wind did it,\" said the"
1448 "baker again, \"or he might smart for it! No doubt the gentleman in"
1448 "Frankfurt when he hears what has happened will make all"
1448 "inquiries about it. I am glad for myself that I have not been"
1448 "seen up the mountain for a good two years, as suspicion is likely"
1448 "to fall on any one who was about up there at the time.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Many more opinions were passed on the matter, but Peter had"
1448 "heard enough. He crept quietly away out of the crowd and then"
1448 "took to his heels and ran up home as fast as he could, as if he"
1448 "thought some one was after him. The baker's words had filled him"
1448 "with fear and trembling. He was sure now that any day a constable"
1448 "might come over from Frankfurt and inquire about the destruction"
1448 "of the chair, and then everything would come out, and he would"
1448 "be seized and carried off to Frankfurt and there put in prison."
1448 "The whole picture of what was coming was clear before him, and"
1448 "his hair stood on end with terror."
1448 ""
1448 "He reached home in this disturbed state of mind. He would not"
1448 "open his mouth in reply to anything that was said to him; he"
1448 "would not eat his potatoes; all he did was to creep off to bed"
1448 "as quickly as possible and hide under the bedclothes and groan."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Peter has been eating sorrel again, and is evidently in pain by"
1448 "the way he is groaning,\" said Brigitta."
1448 ""
1448 "\"You must give him a little more bread to take with him; give"
1448 "him a bit of mine to-morrow,\" said the grandmother sympathisingly."
1448 ""
1448 "As the children lay that night in bed looking out at the stars"
1448 "Heidi said, \"I have been thinking all day what a happy thing it"
1448 "is that God does not give us what we ask for, even when we pray"
1448 "and pray and pray, if He knows there is something better for us;"
1448 "have you felt like that?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Why do you ask me that to-night all of a sudden?\" asked Clara."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Because I prayed so hard when I was in Frankfurt that I might"
1448 "go home at once, and because I was not allowed to I thought God"
1448 "had forgotten me. And now you see, if I had come away at first"
1448 "when I wanted to, you would never have come here, and would never"
1448 "have got well.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Clara had in her turn become thoughtful. \"But, Heidi,\" she began"
1448 "again, \"in that case we ought never to pray for anything, as God"
1448 "always intends something better for us than we know or wish"
1448 "for.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"You must not think it is like that, Clara,\" replied Heidi"
1448 "eagerly. \"We must go on praying for everything, for everything,"
1448 "so that God may know we do not forget that it all comes from"
1448 "Him. If we forget God, then He lets us go our own way and we get"
1448 "into trouble; grandmamma told me so. And if He does not give us"
1448 "what we ask for we must not think that He has not heard us and"
1448 "leave off praying, but we must still pray and say, I am sure,"
1448 "dear God, that Thou art keeping something better for me, and I"
1448 "will not be unhappy, for I know that Thou wilt make everything"
1448 "right in the end.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"How did you learn all that?\" asked Clara."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Grandmamma explained it to me first of all, and then when it"
1448 "all happened just as she said, I knew it myself, and I think,"
1448 "Clara,\" she went on, as she sat up in bed, \"we ought certainly to"
1448 "thank God to-night that you can walk now, and that He has made us"
1448 "so happy.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, Heidi, I am sure you are right, and I am glad you reminded"
1448 "me; I almost forgot my prayers for very joy.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Both children said their prayers, and each thanked God in her"
1448 "own way for the blessing He had bestowed on Clara, who had for so"
1448 "long lain weak and ill."
1448 ""
1448 "The next morning the grandfather suggested that they should now"
1448 "write to the grandmamma and ask her if she would not come and"
1448 "pay them a visit, as they had something new to show her. But the"
1448 "children had another plan in their heads, for they wanted to"
1448 "prepare a great surprise for grandmamma. Clara was first to have"
1448 "more practice in walking so that she might be able to go a"
1448 "little way by herself; above all things grandmamma was not to"
1448 "have a hint of it. They asked the grandfather how long he thought"
1448 "this would take, and when he told them about a week or less, they"
1448 "immediately sat down and wrote a pressing invitation to"
1448 "grandmamma, asking her to come soon, but no word was said about"
1448 "there being anything new to see."
1448 ""
1448 "The following days were some of the most joyous that Clara had"
1448 "spent on the mountain. She awoke each morning with a happy voice"
1448 "within her crying, \"I am well now! I am well now! I shan't have"
1448 "to go about in a chair, I can walk by myself like other people.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Then came the walking, and every day she found it easier and was"
1448 "able to go a longer distance. The movement gave her such an"
1448 "appetite that the grandfather cut his bread and butter a little"
1448 "thicker each day, and was well pleased to see it disappear. He"
1448 "now brought out with it a large jugful of the foaming milk and"
1448 "filled her little bowl over and over again. And so another week"
1448 "went by and the day came which was to bring grandmamma up the"
1448 "mountain for her second visit."
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 ""
1448 "<CHAPTER XXIII. \"GOOD-BYE TILL WE MEET AGAIN\">"
1448 ""
1448 "Grandmamma wrote the day before her arrival to let the children"
1448 "know that they might expect her without fail. Peter brought up"
1448 "the letter early the following morning. Grandfather and the"
1448 "children were already outside and the goats were awaiting him,"
1448 "shaking their heads frolicsomely in the fresh morning air, while"
1448 "the children stroked them and wished them a pleasant journey up"
1448 "the mountain. Uncle stood near, looking now at the fresh faces"
1448 "of the children, now at his well-kept goats, with a smile on his"
1448 "face, evidently well pleased with the sight of both."
1448 ""
1448 "As Peter neared the group his steps slackened, and the instant"
1448 "he had handed the letter to Uncle he turned quickly away as if"
1448 "frightened, and as he went he gave a hasty glance behind him, as"
1448 "if the thing he feared was pursuing him, and then he gave a leap"
1448 "and ran off up the mountain."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Grandfather,\" said Heidi, who had been watching him with"
1448 "astonished eyes, \"why does Peter always behave now like the"
1448 "Great Turk when he thinks somebody is after him with a stick; he"
1448 "turns and shakes his head and goes off with a bound just like"
1448 "that?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Perhaps Peter fancies he sees the stick which he so well"
1448 "deserves coming after him,\" answered grandfather."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter ran up the first slope without a pause; when he was well"
1448 "out of sight, however, he stood still and looked suspiciously"
1448 "about him. Suddenly he gave a jump and looked behind him with a"
1448 "terrified expression, as if some one had caught hold of him by"
1448 "the nape of the neck; for Peter expected every minute that the"
1448 "police-constable from Frankfurt would leap out upon him from"
1448 "behind some bush or hedge. The longer his suspense lasted, the"
1448 "more frightened and miserable he became; he did not know a"
1448 "moment's peace."
1448 ""
1448 "Heidi now set about tidying the hut, as grandmamma must find"
1448 "everything clean and in good order when she arrived."
1448 ""
1448 "Clara looked on amused and interested to watch the busy Heidi at"
1448 "her work."
1448 ""
1448 "So the morning soon went by, and grandmamma might now be"
1448 "expected at any minute. The children dressed themselves and went"
1448 "and sat together outside on the seat ready to receive her."
1448 ""
1448 "Grandfather joined them, that they might see the splendid bunch"
1448 "of blue gentians which he had been up the mountain to gather,"
1448 "and the children exclaimed with delight at the beauty of the"
1448 "flowers as they shone in the morning sun. The grandfather then"
1448 "carried them indoors. Heidi jumped up from time to time to see if"
1448 "there was any sign of grandmamma's approach."
1448 ""
1448 "At last she saw the procession winding up the mountain just in"
1448 "the order she had expected. First there was the guide, then the"
1448 "white horse with grandmamma mounted upon it, and last of all the"
1448 "porter with a heavy bundle on his back, for grandmamma would not"
1448 "think of going up the mountain without a full supply of wraps"
1448 "and rugs."
1448 ""
1448 "Nearer and nearer wound the procession; at last it reached the"
1448 "top and grandmamma was there looking down on the children from"
1448 "her horse. She no sooner saw them, however, sitting side by"
1448 "side, than she began quickly dismounting, as she cried out in a"
1448 "shocked tone of voice, \"Why is this? why are you not lying in"
1448 "your chair, Clara? What are you all thinking about?\" But even"
1448 "before she had got close to them she threw up her hands in"
1448 "astonishment, exclaiming further, \"Is it really you, dear child?"
1448 "Why, your cheeks have grown quite round and rosy! I should hardly"
1448 "have known you again!\" And she was hastening forward to embrace"
1448 "her, when Heidi slipped down from the seat, and Clara leaning on"
1448 "her shoulder, the two children began walking along quite coolly"
1448 "and naturally. Then indeed grandmamma was surprised, or rather"
1448 "alarmed, for she thought at first that it must be some unheard-"
1448 "of proceeding of Heidi's devising."
1448 ""
1448 "But no--Clara was actually walking steadily and uprightly beside"
1448 "Heidi--and now the two children turned and came towards her with"
1448 "beaming faces and rosy cheeks. Laughing and crying she ran to"
1448 "them and embraced first Clara and then Heidi, and then Clara"
1448 "again, unable to speak for joy. All at once she caught sight of"
1448 "Uncle standing by the seat and looking on smiling at the"
1448 "meeting. She took Clara's arm in hers, and with continual"
1448 "expressions of delight at the fact that the child could now"
1448 "really walk about with her, she went up to the old man, and then"
1448 "letting go Clara's arm she seized his hands."
1448 ""
1448 "\"My dear Uncle! my dear Uncle! how much we have to thank you"
1448 "for! It is all your doing! it is your caring and nursing----\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"And God's good sun and mountain air,\" he interrupted her,"
1448 "smiling."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, and don't forget the beautiful milk I have,\" put in Clara."
1448 "\"Grandmamma, you can't think what a quantity of goat's milk I"
1448 "drink, and how nice it is!\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"I can see that by your cheeks, child,\" answered grandmamma. \"I"
1448 "really should not have known you; you have grown quite strong"
1448 "and plump, and taller too; I never hoped or expected to see you"
1448 "look like that. I cannot take my eyes off you, for I can hardly"
1448 "yet believe it. But now I must telegraph without delay to my son"
1448 "in Paris, and tell him he must come here at once. I shall not say"
1448 "why; it will be the greatest happiness he has ever known. My"
1448 "dear Uncle, how can I send a telegram; have you dismissed the men"
1448 "yet?\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"They have gone,\" he answered, \"but if you are in a hurry I will"
1448 "fetch Peter, and he can take it for you.\""
1448 ""
1448 "Grandmamma thanked him, for she was anxious that the good news"
1448 "should not be kept from her son a day longer than was possible."
1448 ""
1448 "So Uncle went aside a little way and blew such a resounding"
1448 "whistle through his fingers that he awoke a responsive echo"
1448 "among the rocks far overhead. He had not to wait many minutes"
1448 "before Peter came running down in answer, for he knew the sound"
1448 "of Uncle's whistle. Peter arrived, looking as white as a ghost,"
1448 "for he quite thought Uncle was sending for him to give him up."
1448 "But as it was he only had a written paper given him with"
1448 "instructions to take it down at once to the post-office at"
1448 "Dorfli; Uncle would settle for the payment later, as it was not"
1448 "safe to give Peter too much to look after."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter went off with the paper in his hand, feeling some relief"
1448 "of mind for the present, for as Uncle had not whistled for him in"
1448 "order to give him up it was evident that no policeman had yet"
1448 "arrived."
1448 ""
1448 "So now they could all sit down in peace to their dinner round"
1448 "the table in front of the hut, and grandmamma was given a"
1448 "detailed account of all that had taken place. How grandfather had"
1448 "made Clara try first to stand and then to move her feet a little"
1448 "every day, and how they had settled for the day's excursion up"
1448 "the mountain and the chair had been blown away. How Clara's"
1448 "desire to see the flowers had induced her to take the first walk,"
1448 "and so by degrees one thing had led to another. The recital took"
1448 "some time, for grandmamma continually interrupted it with fresh"
1448 "exclamations of surprise and thankfulness: \"It hardly seems"
1448 "possible! I can scarcely believe it is not all a dream! Are we"
1448 "really awake, and are all sitting here by the mountain hut, and"
1448 "is that round-faced, healthy-looking child my poor little, white,"
1448 "sickly Clara?\""
1448 ""
1448 "And Clara and Heidi could not get over their delight at the"
1448 "success of the surprise they had so carefully arranged for"
1448 "grandmamma and at the latter's continued astonishment."
1448 ""
1448 "Meanwhile Herr Sesemann, who had finished his business in Paris,"
1448 "had also been preparing a surprise. Without saying a word to his"
1448 "mother he got into the train one sunny morning and travelled"
1448 "that day to Basle; the next morning he continued his journey, for"
1448 "a great longing had seized him to see his little daughter from"
1448 "whom he had been separated the whole summer. He arrived at Ragatz"
1448 "a few hours after his mother had left. When he heard that she had"
1448 "that very day started for the mountain, he immediately hired a"
1448 "carriage and drove off to Mayenfeld; here he found that he could"
1448 "if he liked drive on as far as Dorfli, which he did, as he"
1448 "thought the walk up from that place would be as long as he cared"
1448 "for."
1448 ""
1448 "Herr Sesemann found he was right, for the climb up the mountain,"
1448 "as it was, proved long and fatiguing to him. He went on and on,"
1448 "but still no hut came in sight, and yet he knew there was one"
1448 "where Peter lived half way up, for the path had been described"
1448 "to him over and over again."
1448 ""
1448 "There were traces of climbers to be seen on all sides; the"
1448 "narrow footpaths seemed to run in every direction, and Herr"
1448 "Sesemann began to wonder if he was on the right one, and whether"
1448 "the hut lay perhaps on the other side of the mountain. He looked"
1448 "round to see if any one was in sight of whom he could ask the"
1448 "way; but far and wide there was not a soul to be seen or a sound"
1448 "to be heard. Only at moments the mountain wind whistled through"
1448 "the air, and the insects hummed in the sunshine or a happy bird"
1448 "sang out from the branches of a solitary larch tree. Herr"
1448 "Sesemann stood still for a while to let the cool Alpine wind blow"
1448 "on his hot face. But now some one came running down the mountain-"
1448 "side--it was Peter with the telegram in his hand. He ran straight"
1448 "down the steep slope, not following the path on which Herr"
1448 "Sesemann was standing. As soon as the latter caught sight of him"
1448 "he beckoned to him to come. Peter advanced towards him slowly and"
1448 "timidly, with a sort of sidelong movement, as if he could only"
1448 "move one leg properly and had to drag the other after him. \"Hurry"
1448 "up, lad,\" called Herr Sesemann, and when Peter was near enough,"
1448 "\"Tell me,\" he said, \"is this the way to the hut where the old man"
1448 "and the child Heidi live, and where the visitors from Frankfurt"
1448 "are staying?\""
1448 ""
1448 "A low sound of fear was the only answer he received, as Peter"
1448 "turned to run away in such precipitous haste that he fell head"
1448 "over heels several times, and went rolling and bumping down the"
1448 "slope in involuntary bounds, just in the same way as the chair,"
1448 "only that Peter fortunately did not fall to pieces as that had"
1448 "done. Only the telegram came to grief, and that was torn into"
1448 "fragments and flew away."
1448 ""
1448 "\"How extraordinarily timid these mountain dwellers are!\" thought"
1448 "Herr Sesemann to himself, for he quite believed that it was the"
1448 "sight of a stranger that had made such an impression on this"
1448 "unsophisticated child of the mountains."
1448 ""
1448 "After watching Peter's violent descent towards the valley for a"
1448 "few minutes he continued his journey."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter, meanwhile, with all his efforts, could not stop himself,"
1448 "but went rolling on, and still tumbling head over heels at"
1448 "intervals in a most remarkable manner."
1448 ""
1448 "But this was not the most terrible part of his sufferings at the"
1448 "moment, for far worse was the fear and horror that possessed"
1448 "him, feeling sure, as he did now, that the policeman had really"
1448 "come over for him from Frankfurt. He had no doubt at all that the"
1448 "stranger who had asked him the way was the very man himself."
1448 "Just as he had rolled to the edge of that last high slope above"
1448 "Dorfli he was caught in a bush, and at last able to keep himself"
1448 "from falling any farther. He lay still for a second or two to"
1448 "recover himself, and to think over matters."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well done! another of you come bumping along like this!\" said a"
1448 "voice close to Peter, \"and which of you to-morrow is the wind"
1448 "going to send rolling down like a badly-sewn sack of potatoes?\""
1448 "It was the baker, who stood there laughing. He had been"
1448 "strolling out to refresh himself after his hot day's work, and"
1448 "had watched with amusement as he saw Peter come rolling over and"
1448 "over in much the same way as the chair."
1448 ""
1448 "Peter was on his feet in a moment. He had received a fresh"
1448 "shock. Without once looking behind him he began hurrying up the"
1448 "slope again. He would have liked best to go home and creep into"
1448 "bed, so as to hide himself, for he felt safest when there. But he"
1448 "had left the goats up above, and Uncle had given him strict"
1448 "injunctions to make haste back so that they might not be left"
1448 "too long alone. And he stood more in awe of Uncle than any one,"
1448 "and would not have dared to disobey him on any account. There was"
1448 "no help for it, he had to go back, and Peter went on groaning and"
1448 "limping. He could run no more, for the anguish of mind he had"
1448 "been through, and the bumping and shaking he had received, were"
1448 "beginning to tell upon him. And so with lagging steps and groans"
1448 "he slowly made his way up the mountain."
1448 ""
1448 "Shortly after meeting Peter, Herr Sesemann passed the first hut,"
1448 "and so was satisfied that he was on the right path. He continued"
1448 "his climb with renewed courage, and at last, after a long and"
1448 "exhausting walk, he came in sight of his goal. There, only a"
1448 "little distance farther up, stood the grandfather's home, with"
1448 "the dark tops of the fir trees waving above its roof."
1448 ""
1448 "Herr Sesemann was delighted to have come to the last steep bit"
1448 "of his journey, in another minute or two he would be with his"
1448 "little daughter, and he pleased himself with the thought of her"
1448 "surprise. But the company above had seen his approaching figure"
1448 "and recognized who it was, and they were preparing something he"
1448 "little expected as a surprise on their part."
1448 ""
1448 "As he stepped on to the space in front of the hut two figures"
1448 "came towards him. One a tall girl with fair hair and pink cheeks,"
1448 "leaning on Heidi, whose dark eyes were dancing with joy. Herr"
1448 "Sesemann suddenly stopped, staring at the two children, and all"

1448 "heart! Just so had Clara's mother looked, the fair-haired girl"
1448 "with the delicate pink-and-white complexion. Herr Sesemann did"
1448 "not know if he was awake or dreaming."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Don't you know me, papa?\" called Clara to him, her face beaming"
1448 "with happiness. \"Am I so altered since you saw me?\""
1448 ""
1448 "Then Herr Sesemann ran to his child and clasped her in his arms."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, you are indeed altered! How is it possible? Is it true"
1448 "what I see?\" And the delighted father stepped back to look full"
1448 "at her again, and to make sure that the picture would not vanish"
1448 "before his eyes."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Are you my little Clara, really my little Clara?\" he kept on"
1448 "saying, then he clasped her in his arms again, and again put her"
1448 "away from him that he might look and make sure it was she who"
1448 "stood before him."
1448 ""
1448 "And now grandmamma came up, anxious for a sight of her son's"
1448 "happy face."
1448 ""
1448 "\"Well, what do you say now, dear son?\" she exclaimed. \"You have"
1448 "given us a pleasant surprise, but it is nothing in comparison to"
1448 "what we have prepared for you, you must confess,\" and she gave"
1448 "her son an affectionate kiss as she spoke. \"But now,\" she went"
1448 "on, \"you must come and pay your respects to Uncle, who is our"
1448 "chief benefactor.\""
1448 ""
1448 "\"Yes, indeed, and with the little inmate of our own house, our"
1448 "little Heidi, too,\" said Herr Sesemann, shaking Heidi by the"
1448 "hand. \"Well? are you still well and happy in your mountain home?"
1448 "but I need not ask, no Alpine rose could look more blooming. I"
1448 "am glad, child, it is a pleasure to me to see you so.\""
1448 ""
1448 "And Heidi looked up with equal pleasure into Herr Sesemann's"
1448 "kind face. How good he had always been to her! And that he should"
1448 "find such happiness awaiting him up here on the mountain made her"
1448 "heart beat with gladness."
1448 ""
1448 "Grandmamma now led her son to introduce him to Uncle, and while"
1448 "the two men were shaking hands and Herr Sesemann was expressing"
1448 "his heartfelt thanks and boundless astonishment to the old man,"
1448 "grandmamma wandered round to the back to see the old fir trees"
1448 "again."
1448 ""
1448 "Here another unexpected sight met her gaze, for there, under the"
1448 "trees where the long branches had left a clear space on the"
